O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, dear children, I have completed this book which is the last of medical science, its fulfillment, and have ended it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is the beginning of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is closely guarded in our region and is unfamiliar to all, the knowledge has decayed and become sparse, with only small descriptions in ancient books remaining about what the hands have accomplished.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this, error and vanity have arisen, and intentions are closed, and knowledge is separated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I want to revive this treatise by ordering it according to the method of exposition and explanation, and also by providing an overview; and I will bring together the forms of cauterization tools, and other instruments used in the work, with the adjustments needed for their declaration and preparation, as required.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are to be found in our time, the art of medicine has decayed.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who wishes to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, must know the judgment of the members, their shapes and connections and separations, have knowledge of bones and nerves and veins, and the number of them, and how they move and rest, and from where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And Hippocrates says that words without deeds are empty, and actions without knowledge are harmful, especially in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	In the introduction to this book, we tell you that he who is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, risks falling into error and misleading others; as I have often seen happen with many of those who engage in this science without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a most wondrous sight, which infected the abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and affected the arteries of her neck; so much blood issued forth that the woman died in the woman's hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another wonder: a stone was extracted from an old man's bladder, and the stone was large; it took away with it a piece of his bladder, and he bled internally for three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to extract it, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; if it were not cut out, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another marvel that took in hand the treatment of a duke from our land who had a broken leg, and with the break came an injury; and the ignorant healers bound the break over the wound as if by strong ties, leaving no space for the wound to heal, and left it thus until the end; and he commanded that he should not loosen it; and so he waited until the leg was completely swollen and the pain increased and led to his loss.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	They called me to come to him, and I hastened to come and loosen the leg; and when I heard it dislocate, it was as if it had been released and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way of corruption was already confirmed in that member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until all the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another wonder: the abscess became worse, and then it was inflamed due to the evil nature of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is free from melancholic humor, it does not suit to be touched with iron unless it is in a place where everything corrupt can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear child, it is necessary for you to know that the art of healing is divided into two parts: that is to say, the work which has danger in many dispositions; and I will show you in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, it is necessary for you to keep this in mind, so that the foolish gaze cannot speak ill of you. If you take up your weapons courageously and begin to confront your illnesses gently but firmly, using the best method so that by the grace of God you may attain salvation and be happy; abandon diseases that cause despair, seeking health instead; cast aside doubts about your abilities, and have faith in yourself so that you can transition from this world to the next with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in none of his warnings: "Do not take any sick condition too seriously, unless you are called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterization and ague medicine cauterization, and it is ordered from the head to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and the tools for cauterization, and everything necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and it is ordered and the forms of instruments are described.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and torsions, and similar conditions; and it orders the use of specific tools from the neck down to the feet, and the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So, remembering the work, it is appropriate that I describe the qualities of each aid and its potential harm or benefit to each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aids and their potential harms, are the longest-winded speech and subtlest science, answering to which are the most wise, and they agreed on this; and for me, a few words suffice, as I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally for all complexes where it has matter, whether hot or dry complexes; that is to say, the hot complex with matter, and the dry complex without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In both hot and dry complexes, matter is present, some argue that cautery is great help, while others say the opposite, claiming cautery is ineffective against ailments arising from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be treated with heat for a hot illness, nor through dryness; and he who says the contrary claims cautery offers great help against hot and dry ailments that come upon humans.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and its moisture to the appearance from fire, you perceive the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, no one should attempt it except he who has tested it and knows by long practice the chapter of cautery, the variety of human complexes, the dispositions and causes of their ailments, and the outcomes and the season of time; for other complexes we have only fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all agreed and consented to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, child, that cautery brings together fire, being a secret of healing, and moreover, it is much gentler than hot medical cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not come from outside the body except to the part that is hot, and it does not harm any other member.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Hot medicines travel from one part to another by removing, and they bring diseases of great distress to the member; and perhaps the fire does not harm the patient because of its greatness and the goodness of its substance, unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And because I have found this by experience and through the long service and study that I have put into the art, and it is about the truth of things, and for this reason I excuse myself from the length of my words, since I do not wish to reveal the secret hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it heals diseases of the body, as the philosopher demonstrates; consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know this, my son, that there is agreement among them as to the time when cauterization should be performed and the appropriate prayers recited.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, because the pain-causing injury is removed by the help of cauterization; and especially cauterization is for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait until a greater evil comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear child, as they do with foolish people; for the disease that is healed by cautery has no relapse; and it should be so. But they are not like those who take care, because cautery is only a medicine that alters the complexion and dries up the humors that cause pain, and acts more quickly than any other medicine, both for its own virtue and for the authority of its work.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And another powerful thing is that the disease comes back according to the complexion and place of the illness and its virtue; and excesses accumulate within it through the acquisition of foods and similar things, except when cautery is applied in places where there are few excesses and moistures, as with cautery for pain and similar conditions, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last of medicine, and that is evident; but they do not believe that cautery is useful after medicine, for when we administer remedies in any disease and they are ineffective, then we use cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cautery is indeed the last of medicine, not according to the opinion of wise men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold cautery tools are more effective than iron ones, and they only spoke of fire for the quality of gold and for its high substance; and they said that the heat of cautery does not cause corruption, but it is not true, as I have tested it, and I have found that it is useless in any case; and gold cautery tools are more effective than iron ones, as they claim.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat the gold instrument, you are not sure if it is hot enough by the color of the gold, and as soon as it cools down; and if you heat it too much, it will burn; thus there is sufficient hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use fire cautery because we have equipped ourselves with the necessary tools for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	We have organized this chapter from the beginning to the end so that the path is easier to follow.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Cyst cautery involves applying heat and cold to the brain, and it is used for various conditions caused by disease ("soda") or many humors that descend from the head to the ears, and for numerous dreams, toothache, throat pain, especially in all diseases arising from cold, such as paralysis, "soda," apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient is purged with a solvent medicine, cleansing the head III or IV, according to the strength and age and custom of the patient; and then the head is made red again by the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him lie crossed in your hands, and place his hands on some weight; after, put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two fingers; and hold where your two middle fingers meet, if it bleeds, then heat the cautery called 'olive' which has this shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And mark him with the sign of ink, and make descending and pulling your hand in turns, dislocating it; then gently lower your hand alone, and re-align the bone if you see it has shifted; and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I told you. After that, take a little silk, put damp and soft cotton inside, place it on the joint, and leave it for three days. Then apply moistened butter cloth, and keep it until the heat has subsided; after, dress the wound with 'tetrafarmacon' ointment while it is clean.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the elders say that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purifies itself; for this reason, it needs help to heal.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one should not allow the cautery to burn off any part of the bone, and then remove the burnt part from the bone, and it will heal.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another one says that one should not allow the cautery to burn for too long, and apply it so strongly that part of the bone is also burned, just as women open their wombs to let the humors flow out; and one should keep the wound open for a long time; afterwards, one should clean and dress it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in every way, except for those who have no choice but to endure; and I think I should leave them, because the joint is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other members; and also when the patient's joint is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery seems safer and more flexible to me, from which I derive my method accordingly.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain in the head comes on and lasts for a long time, patients should use herbs and pills known as "cough drops," and purgatives for the head and eyes, and applications; and if they try the cautery we have mentioned above, it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's limb is of strong nature and not too frozen; then cauterize it from below, using a cautery as we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterizing each corner of the head just below the bone, as we mentioned before, and cauterizing the one called "vessel," which is where suction cups are placed, hold your hand lightly so that you do not see the bone. The patient feels much greater pain from this cautery than from others, and I will speak about it later; it is necessary that the cautery on the horns be more subtle than that of the middle part of the head, and this is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	For fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the head there is a sudden pain, and the disease extends to the oil (or possibly referring to an abscess), and the condition is purged with medicated remedies, and all other cures as mentioned in the classification of illnesses have been tried without success, then one should perform cauterization according to two methods: that is, with ague medicine and by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with ague medicine involves pricking a dose of alder, removing the bark and applying it to the affected area, holding it in place in such a way that you can push back the pain from the alder into the flesh; then tightly bind it and leave it for 12 hours. Afterwards, unbind it and treat the wound vigorously with garlic, leaving it for 2-3 days, then apply cotton soaked in butter until the purulent discharge stops.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the cure of dressing as long as it is healed; and if you see fit to make any burning medicine as I have written in my book on the dosage treatment of burning medicines, do so.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery according to this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head has the shape of a circle with a small amount of curvature in the middle; and place it on the painful joint, hold your hand, and gently turn the hot instrument slightly, until half of the depth of the heart is burned; and then remove your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is dangerous, and let the blood flow abundantly.

After placing cotton in the wound and leaving it for three days; then he moistens it with butter and tends to the wound until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with a cautery called "cultellare" (scalpel), be careful not to cut the artery in this new migraine.

de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have discussed regarding diseases, and your treatments do not benefit the patient, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head on a healthy surface; then position his neck between your hands in such a way that it does not move and its head remains still. Afterwards, apply moist cotton or pear juice to the area. Then heat the cautery tool which is shaped like a bow: align the tip of the cautery so that it touches the neck, either from above or below, and shape it similarly to a tent; but nonetheless, whatever the position, this bending is necessary for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, open it, and drain the pus and dry it; if it closes again, repeat the process, and apply hot cautery; hold your hand over the cauterized area to prevent any damage, and place the cautery on the fatty part of the oil, and burn.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you start the cautery close to the bone, that would be better.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If no, restart the cautery again, and do so as many times as necessary, leaving it for three days; then apply moistened butter cotton, and cure the desiccated wound until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, apply a corrosive medicine while the bone remains exposed; and the remedy will depend on what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cauterizing a fistula, of which no one among the ancients spoke.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand the fistula, and locate its source; then place a thin, sharp instrument into the gap, thus taking on this form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and it makes the quantity of a drop of blood; and hold your hand firmly with the instrument, so that the patient does not move at all, until the blood has finished flowing; and it is necessary to put cotton soaked in oil on the wound for its healing or otherwise: the blood drops into the fistula and heal the healthy tissue miraculously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed through the cautery we have mentioned, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, it is necessary to administer cold or heat, and bring the fistula back to the body according to what is appropriate for its own place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks appear in the lips, which are called 'poil', especially on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these wounds as we have discussed in detail, and the cure is not beneficial, then apply a small cauterizing instrument according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the hospital in these wounds until it comes to a stop; after that, treat the area with clean dressing until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms in the throat's root, or in the uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it causes putrefaction and swelling and becomes a fistula; then you must treat it as we have discussed in detail, but it does not benefit. In this case, you should apply cauterization according to the size of the fistula; after that, remove the fistula's hole or opening, and hold your hand until the heat from the fire goes to the bottom of it, without touching anything else. And do this once or twice, following the cure as we have said in detail, until it is healed; and if it heals in this way, it is good. But if not, you should expose the area and remove the rotten bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	no movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and this treatment with medicines is ineffective, then place the patient's aching jaw in your hand; afterwards, apply the hot cautery where the pain originates, in this way, placing a candle on the tooth; and hold the hot cautery firmly until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then release your hand and repeat the cautery according to your desire; afterward, have the patient fill his mouth with salt water, and keep it for an hour and let it flow out strongly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner, the tooth which was moving becomes firmly set, and the gums are softened and restrained, and the moisture is corrupt and dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When the pain of teeth comes from cold, or there is frost or chill, and the remedies of medicine are not effective, then it is necessary to use cautery according to two methods: butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery is done by soaking butter in a cold substance, wrapping it around the tip of a rod made of iron or steel, and applying it to the aching tooth with great care until it becomes cooled. Then, you repeat this process frequently until the pain subsides at the root of the tooth; if the butter becomes too moistened with the cloth and cotton wrapped around it, apply it again to the aching tooth, but place a hot iron on top as soon as the heat reaches the surface of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	He uses fire cautery if it is such that you can insert a piece of iron or steel, making it large enough so that the heat does not reach the patient's mouth; then, after heating the cautery, its form will appear, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, for the pain will be gone by the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in anticipation of that cautery, and then applies the heat; this is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And perform the cautery on the upper lip where you wish, according to your ability; this is the form of the instrument.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is of cold moisture, and does not obey digestion with medicines, then heat the cautery fire from this, so that it opens up to let out smoke through the cautery in another part; and place hot cautery on the abscess once, if it is necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply cautery according to its size, leaving it for three days; and then cover with moist cotton or butter until the burning is healed; afterwards treat the wound and bandage until it is clean.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture conquers the channels of the pores, especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be evacuated first with solvent medicines; afterwards, he should be cauterized at the root of the throat, and be careful not to go up to the throat, and only slightly heat with heart.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, he performs another cauterization at the joint of the collarbone with the tip of the spine, and these cauterizations that are called "clavicle" as we have shown before; and treat the limb as we have said above until it is healed.
de la toust	from the toast
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and any illness of the lungs is due to cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or chills, and if it is an old illness, make two cauterizations on strong parts of his body; and another cauterization between the two breasts; and this cauterization which is called "clavile" should be according to the shape as mentioned above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make a cauterization by pricking all the cauterization called "point" from which the shape of the illness of the ears is as mentioned above; and the points should be up to 30, or even more inside.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the treatment, reset the limb according to what is mentioned above, and make the cauterization in three stages according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the cautery is easier, because you do it three times in turn.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	On the dislocation of the shoulder.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, remember to support the patient on their back and side; afterwards, gently press the kernel inside the swelling with your left hand; if the joint is dislocated within, apply heat to the cautery with two gentle strokes as follows:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and burn the heart as long as it feels hot, and repeat this process with four burns; for this reason, the burn is made with a three-pronged instrument, so that the six burns form a figure; and the nerve corresponds to the subtlety of a thread, and this is the shape of the burn with three prongs.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never adjust it on this nerve, for there are eight burns.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After applying the burn, wrap with a cloth; then rest the patient, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated from above, this happens poorly, then apply cautery over the thick part of the cautery with a claw or many cauteries pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	Because the joint is closed, the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach while it is being extracted from its natural state, many catarrhs are multiplied within it, and the usual remedies do not help, then the patient should be made to lie on his back, extending his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From this and afterward, make three cauterizations and remove the knife from the deepest part, in quantity as thick as a finger, cauterizing the entire wound, and two cauterizations on both sides, so that the shape of the cauterization be at three angles, and there be such space between one and another that they do not stick together while they rot; and make the cauterization so perfect that it touches both parts of the heart, and the shape of the cauterization be according to this form without adjustment.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you are to be cauterized with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form, and he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and marking on the stomach at one point according to the quantity that you see fit; then cauterize the entire cautery called "point.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment we have previously discussed, as long as he is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver suffers from pain due to freshness and moisture and excessive flatulence, as long as it is removed from its natural state by excesses; and the patient is treated as we have said in sections, but it does not benefit them, then it is necessary that the patient be cautious on their head. And a sign of this is to perform three cauterizations according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, expelling the humors from the liver or the gallbladder; and there should be enough space between each cauterization, the thickness of two fingers; and the cautery should be long across the body, and do not press too hard with your hand over the entire cautery; and burn only moderately half of the heart, and let the patient keep their legs straight; and if they cannot, then they should lie down, stretch out their legs, and ease their breath. And this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish, cauterize these wounds with a knife, if you are skilled and sharp in the art, but be careful not to burn the entire heart, for it would harm the whole body; and do not let them come to a boil, because the hearts are very delicate there, and only the wise can see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you need to know if it is within the liver tissue or in the peritoneum: if it is within the tissue, the patient feels moderate pain; but if it is in the peritoneum, they feel excruciating pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure involves mirrors, it is necessary that the patient be calm on his head; then he should tie the bandage across the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a needle, from which comes this form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with the cautery until the veins are burned, and the pus comes out completely; after the cure, according to the treatment of the wounds, as long as he is healthy; and it is not appropriate for this cautery to be used by anyone other than someone who has studied medicine extensively and whose hands have never failed in treating these illnesses.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can move it bravely, but I still think it is better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	The "dou cautere de pleuresin" phrase translates to "the fire cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient ones said that one should perform the pleuresin cautery with roots of the aristologe, in this way: take a long root of aristologe, the largest you can find, and dry it, making it as thick and as long as your arm; moisten it in oil, hold it over the fire, and cauterize between the ribs and the collarbone, and make small cauterizations slightly downward in the part below the beard; and cauterize between the fifth rib and the sixth, leaning slightly behind; and cauterize across the anus, and another one on the stomach, and between the shoulders, and along both sides of the lower ribs, defusing the cautery between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but hold it open as if smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they say that no old man should use fire cautery resembling a razor, and burn it and place it between the ribs, until it reaches this abscess; and there is great pain, as we have said in the case of the painful liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work, there is great fear or the patients die now, or a fistula forms which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the divisions of treatment, and it does not benefit, then they (doctors) apply three methods of cautery, all of which are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Break the joint in such a way that you make three cauterizations, or four, according to the length of the bone, according to the figure of the cautery of the fire that we have mentioned above; and do not rush your hand over the entire cautery, let the patient be cautious on his back; another method of cauterization is to heat the cautery with two nails, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and ease the pressure where the bone is located, where the patient's pain comes from the left, and raise the elevation according to the bone, according to the length of the body, and let the cauterization be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After you have heated the two nails until the bone is pierced on the other side, then quickly apply the cautery, and thus you will have four. And if you see that the cauterization is not complete at three nails, cauterize the entire cautery with three nails.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After treatment when he has suffered for a long time, this is more effective than any of the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	It appears that the term "dystropie" is
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not effective for dystropia, except in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	If your treatment according to the methods we have mentioned in divisions is not effective, then you should perform four cauterizations around the mouth, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one near the anus; and the cauterizations should be close to the affected areas.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery open for a long time to allow pus to drain, do not leave the patient's care to the cautery; healing would be hastened, and the two wounds would heal together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the abdomen should be a knife as we have shown before; and for the back, olive-shaped, according to what is placed before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of stones
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When stones are swollen in someone who is uric, and they are filled with clear urine, you should cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and gently hold your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not pierce too deeply, so as to keep the citron-colored awl outside, and perform the cauterization according to this form.
