And never should one cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow worse, but the excess from which they come is broken off, and they are healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times, great complications arise from the blood of an artery that is cut in the wound, or in the closure of an abscess, or in cauterization of the member, and similar things; this is a very sad thing to smell.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	However, if this happens to anyone, act quickly and place your finger on the wound in the vein, pulling it firmly until the pain is entirely gone and no more blood flows; then take several small and large hot olive oil cauterizing tools, making them completely red, and afterward, according to the size of the wound, and with a firm grip, place the cauterization over the vein where you are holding your finger, and keep the cautery there until the pain is thoroughly subdued.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a sudden spark flies when you raise your hand above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, quickly take another from those at the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to perform this one after the other until the bleeding is stopped; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and let no further harm come to the patient; and know that when blood collects from an artery, it cannot be well stopped, especially if the artery is large, unless by one of the four methods we have mentioned: either cauterization, or extraction when it has not been treated, or tightly tying it with thread, or applying medications that have the power to stop the bleeding; and do this carefully and meticulously.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever alleviates the pain by tightly binding narrow bandages or placing burning things, or similar objects, on it, will not benefit unless he does it properly.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens to no one and he has no suitable medicine at hand, then he should place his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until the pain subsides both over the wound and the vein; and he must not move it, but moisten it with cold water often, as much as it is very cold, until the blood is congealed and thickened, and the pain subsides; and prepare inquiries in advance about what he needs for cauterization and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	We begin the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every illness for which it is necessary to use fire cautery, or burning medicine, and about the herbs, causes, tools, and forms of cautery; I placed that chapter primarily before this one so that those who wish to find these things more easily can do so.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, before beginning this, it is necessary, by way of introduction, that you learn that this chapter involves more risk and danger than the first one on cautery; and for this reason, greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to attempt folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	Because many ways of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from such who have grown weary of their illness to the point that they die quickly due to the harshness they find in their treatment and the severity of their suffering; and for these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who give you their trust, saying, "Wait, I am blind"; and the illness is pitiful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not grant your consent to those who come to you with such methods, but place more emphasis on your honor than on their profit, and act prudently rather than rashly regarding what you are certain of and what you can safely acquire; and use prediction and indication in the treatment of your patients, so that health may be restored; and this will help you gain good repute, glory, and lasting fame.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Most precious thread, Our Lords grant you good understanding and rectitude, and if you desire the holy inspiration from His hand, so be it.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter for you, in considering by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery that I have devised from the head to the feet, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Dou chief plein d'aigue" translates to "a head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	You know that this illness comes very often in children at birth, and when the womb contracts too tightly around the child's head; and it never happens for a reason that one cannot explain.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness except in children, and to all those that I have seen, death comes swiftly; and for this reason, it seems to me that it is better to leave the work in part, rather than attempt complete cures.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose joints were filled with water, and the head swelled each day until it could not be supported; and because of so much moisture, it became infected, and this moisture was collected beneath the bone in the synovial cavity, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such that the moisture lies between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, so you must make a wide cut through the head where the moisture is located, as long as it runs. And here is the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the openings of the abscesses on each side of the head widely open, and there is a strong discharge when you press it with your hand from inside, and it does not heal, then you must make three cuts in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture deeply.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After loosening the cracks of the drapes and powders, he applies wine and oil, leaving it for up to five days; then he removes it, treating the wound with bandages and poultices, while also gently pulling on the head until the joint is aligned and the patient is given dry meat from a pouch of moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you observe and determine the size of the abscess, and the alignment of the fluid; for it never presents itself in one place, nor behind, nor on the right, nor on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut open the abscess and drain the pus, and make an incision according to your ability; be careful not to harm the artery; then let the blood flow freely, so that the patient does not die from excessive bleeding or the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	De reume" translates to "of the
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When a person suffers from a disease called "catar" (possibly referring to cataracts), especially if it is an old illness and medicinal treatments are ineffective, the only remaining cure is cautery by cutting off both arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	When you see the patient's head covered, make him turn his head back; then rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries open, and carefully extract the patient's neck from the cloth; then observe where the vein is located, and note that the marks of the ears are on both sides, and they are properly aligned; then mark the joints with a sign, and cut one and the other with a sharp spatula, reaching down to the bone, and do this across the entire back.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, pull the spatula away from the artery and cut it above, cutting also as it should go through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it bleeds constantly upward continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open when pressed, it is necessary to measure the quantity of space in three parts, then seal it with a knot and cut it until it reaches the bone; and one should put as much blood outside as is needed (approximately six parts), or perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the patient can endure and the filling of the artery. Then, examine the wound: if it remains above the bone without pus, cut and bind the wound and apply treatment until it heals.
de emigrainne	from migraine headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine headache comes with catarrh, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples, and other similar symptoms, it is treated with medical remedies, but often none of them help. So we should drain the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method for extracting them is that the patient pulls out the hairs from his temples and reaches for the artery that opens in the temple, as it opens well with its beating, and is quickly covered by no one else. If it is covered, he gently squeezes some cloth over it, then rubs the place with a rough cloth until the artery becomes clearly visible; then take the spatula with which this form is:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then hold it with pincers and separate the threads that bind each part; and if the artery is thin, turn it to the tip of the hook, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it will not heal without great pain.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the abscess with six cuts, up to three; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it with two threads of strong silk, so that putrefaction does not come before the healing of the wound, and complications from the abscess; then cut off the excess between the two threads at that very moment, and then, if you see fit, cauterize the patient with a cutting instrument up to the bone while the joints are still cut; and this is the moving part, if the patient does not have fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery is a help to finish off moisture: hence it is of greater aid with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the wound with thick cotton and place on top well-made bandages; and when they are removed, be careful to use dried medicines that produce heat, and bandages until the wound is healed; and as soon as you see the artery exposed, act quickly with cautery, or use vitriol and press with your hand so that the wound is cleansed; and if you do not have this at hand, put ice on the wound until the bleeding stops, and gently pull out the bandage until it is removed properly; and what moves more easily and is lighter for extracting an artery is to cauterize the vein from both sides with this cautery, but the cuts should be well-spaced to maintain its heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they do not hold their heat well.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have a good amount of space between the two blades, and then once you've marked the two bones, place the hot iron until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and leave enough space between the two cuts as it is not well-joined by this cauterization entirely. And this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes descend into the veins that are on the face near the forehead, and medicine does not help at all, you see the face of the sick person turn red, and feel a burning sensation as if from a fever, and the skin becomes dry and moist so that the hairs on the eyelids fall out, and the eyelids become inflamed and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this cure is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it the ancient "scab cure", and this is what you do for the patient who has this condition: take the hairs on their forehead and shave them; then make three cuts on the forehead equally along its length; one cut should go all the way down to the nose, and the other two cuts should be made on either side of the forehead above the eyelids. Avoid incising the arteries that are next to the eyelids. Keep your hand away from the jawline. Each wound should be about three times as long as it is wide. Have a piece of sponge or cloth ready to absorb the blood, then use a sharp spatula with this shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made on the temple down to the second incision; strip all the skin that is between the two slits to the entire satisfaction that is above the bone, then make another from the middle incision down to the other second one, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert the instrument called a "cultellaire" into the first slit, it should be very sharp on one side and soft on the other; its shape is as follows:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	and place the cutting side towards the opposite direction of the slit at the bone, and the soft side towards the bone, and push until it reaches the middle slit.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the joints until the incision is continuous to open the heart, and then make a narrow slit on the other side; and then extract the blood evenly, and press out the wound for the blood taken; then place in each slit a strip of old cotton cloth, and lay wet cloths of wine and oil and wool, and be sure that no abscess forms; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and administer a strong spray of pure water, then apply the basilicon treatment with rose oil, and other remedies to cure wounds, until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	your joints
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any catarrh has become habitual, and you see the eyes heavy and small, weakening sight, and the membranes burning, and the hair falling out, and a feeling of pain in the head, the patient sneezes; then know from these symptoms that these matters and this catarrh do not come from a single cause, but the moving cure it.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to press their forehead, then make a deep cut between the eyebrows, and another one wide enough to fit a finger.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And from the cut on the left temple to the right temple, make an incision reaching the bone; and move your hand away from the nerve of the temples that close when you blink; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two edges of the wound and place old cotton on it, and cover it with linen. Then put moistened cloth soaked in wine and oil on top of it, and protect from further bleeding; once the bone has healed, it is important to rub the bone gently until new growth begins, then apply drying agents that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of rye flower and three parts of chalk, mix them to make a paste, and apply it to these wounds to draw out poison from all parts.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	from ear infection
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that causes an ear infection is one of four things: grains, animals, mineral stones or similar objects; seeds like peas, beans, beans; or flowing substances such as water and mucus-like things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When something like a stone or any other object that does not fit properly in the ear enters the ear and does not grow or settle in the ear, it should be exposed to sunlight.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, and it distills any little drop of red oil or oil of myrrh, then it is fit for extraction; and it causes coughing due to congestion, and stops the nostrils when coughing comes, and places pieces of cloth or wool inside the ear; and pulls the ear from above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times this treatment fails; and if it does not fail, then extractions with fine pincers are applied, of which here is the shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If the extraction with pincers succeeds, that is good; if not, apply an intricate wire noose of fine twine; and if it still does not succeed, make a hook of iron and squeeze the top of the hook into the ear canal or the hollow of the ear firmly, and stop up what is around the hook with soft wax so that the air current cannot enter along with the hook. Then treat it thoroughly, because often this method fails as we have said; if not in this way, then take a good amount of it, and use any sharp instrument suitable for this purpose, and place some cotton inside; then press the clot onto the stone or something similar, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not follow all these things that we have said, then hurry to pierce the ear in such a way that the abscess hardens and the spasms cease; and the manner of the piercing is such that you first make the patient from the cephalics, extract the blood according to its virtue, then place the patient between your hands and restore the ear to its original position, making a small cut at the base of the ear where the fat or tissue is attached; and let the cut be as wide as a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it with your mouth; and the cure as long as it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is trapped and swollen, then administer extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, then use a delicate spatula according to this form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and cut out the growth of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not attempt this if you think the grain is moist due to earwax, after having made many attempts; then extract it with delicate pincers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case that you extract something from the ear, it is advisable for the patient to use a gentle sneeze initially and fill the ear with fine cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lay something on that same ear, whether there is wax or water.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps through fire, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If the fire is no longer hot, take many thin pieces according to the length of your little finger and warm them slightly over fire; then insert the patient into one or both holes in their ear, and try from another side, striking with another piece on the stone inside the ear; continue this process from stone to stone until all the liquid has escaped completely, and thus it will jump out completely; and if you see that it sticks, take a thin wire, and insert one end into the ear, and the other end into fire until the thinnest part is burned; then repeat with other wires until all the liquid is gone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	During the removal of an animal, if it is a small bone, like a pin or something similar, treat it as we have said in the previous discussion; but if it is a large bone that can be felt, then use forceps for its removal; and it is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When treating earworms (vers enjanrez) as we have previously discussed and addressing distillations (a term likely referring to ear infections or discharge), if the treatment is not effective, it is necessary to examine the ear in sunlight. If no worms are visible, use fine forceps to carefully remove them; observe the shape of the wax (cainne) remaining after removal.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be tight from below and wide from above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And then, more subtly, insert the bottle into the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, then suction along the entire chain; do this often until all the air is removed.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, then close the chain with cotton as I have said before; and if they do not protrude as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have tested for worm removal, and you will find them in the section on distillations; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear using all these tools, forming them as you see fit.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And take a piece of silver or gold wire cut to the size of the small opening, and place it above the eardrum to distill; and to press inside the distillation with a well-made brass instrument, and if you see, take a razor and wrap it around the tip very carefully; then pour your oil or juice, and what you want from your medicines in the ear, and the ear should be in the pot; then put the razor completely into the cotton and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or slightly enters the ear; and let the patient feel it within, and make the distillation very hot over the fire just as it is done in the ear; and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would be ineffective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From ear pain
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born with any holes in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to a sudden wound or an object entering the ear, and this blockage comes completely into the ear unless one can see it; and sometimes the hole becomes closed and no one notices it.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When the blockage comes completely into the ear, if one cannot see it, it requires careful treatment in multiple ways, and in this case, you should place the patient's affected ear towards the sun; and examine inside. If you see the wax buildup, which gives the shape of its form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And make incisions and cuts all around, front and back, so that the ear does not remain injured; if the pain is from a foreign body or the cartilage of the ear, hold it with fine pincers and gently remove it until all bones are dislodged.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	If the pain is completely in the ear, take a fine, sharp razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then apply it to the cartilage of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the pain that the patient feels in their ear is intense, make a slight perforation, and be careful not to injure the inner part of the ear; then insert into the ear a plug according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not touch the wound for as long as it is fresh, or take a cloth and wet it in rosewater, and sprinkle it with vitriol powder; and if you see an ear swollen, it is necessary that you remove the cloth and replace it with another moistened cloth made of roset oil and wax, until the swelling subsides; then treat it as long as it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and apply other remedies to stop the flow of blood, which can be treated with distillation.
de la char des papieres	concerning the preparation of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Take all the papers that come from the eyes when they are moist and dried, it is necessary to extend them with pliers and pincers, and cut off the top of a spatula from its roots; then put it over the vitriol ground fine.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if, after removing the outer layer, the lenticular cautery is performed gently, and the cauterizer after incision moves; and often they repair themselves, as nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the ice (or frost)
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come onto paper one kind of thing that appears twisted in its form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "frost," which is a gathering of great moisture on the paper above and below; the work is as follows: take care if the frost becomes silent from one side to the other, and it is a light matter to know; then make it wide, then scrape gently from each part, then take it with pincers and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper slightly, it causes no harm to the patient; and if the split is large, with a stitch, treat it until it heals; but if it is small, do not exert yourself too much, because humors will soon restore it and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the pain is descending inside the ear towards the top part, turn the paper against it, and the pain holds onto some pinches, pressing from one side to another; and if the paper is moved by the incision, it causes no harm; and when the pain is cut away, drain the water with salt, and treat the place where it originated until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Xerophthalmia is a fat that is embedded in the thin films of paper-like substances on the eyes, and it occurs more often in children than in adults, causing great pain to their eyes. In the mornings, they experience cataracts, and because of this, they cannot bear the light of the sun, as tears constantly stream from their eyes. Therefore, they rest their faces down, sleep, and their paper-like substances become moist under their eyelids, filled with xerosis that has opened in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel the extraction between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient places his head on the healthy side, and then takes a linen cloth and prepares a tent in the form of a circle according to the amount of extraction from each part, and places it there; and he presses with his fingers on both sides so that the extraction is gathered within the circle; then, in the middle of the moisture, using a cutting spatula, they make a groove not wider than the wound made in the vein; and they continue until they reach the extraction; and in various arrangements, extraction comes from the groove in the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take therefore a whole piece of cloth dipped in fire between your fingers and turn your hand to the right and to the left as long as it is dispersed; and be careful not to insert anything into the wound, do not reach all the way to the oil, and do not touch it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the wound does not open at the beginning of the incision, gently widen the wound slightly until it opens; then extract as we have said, and moisten the cloth with water and blood, and apply to the wound, and wrap tightly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such people who grind and apply something to corrupt the moisture that is lingering.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it as long as it is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place of the hot abscess, treat it with external soothing as long as it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow in papers (or unnaturally), they become inflamed, causing harm and leading to various diseases, such as cracks and molts in the skin, and a white crust, all due to the destruction of the hairs; and the cure is according to four methods: by entire fire cautery, or by sharp medicine according to what is mentioned in the chapter on cautery, or by incision and stitching, or by binding, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your hand, then turn the paper from the oil on your left hand; if it rotates, that is good; if not, insert an needle along all the threads above; and this should be done either along the edge of the paper where the hairs grow or along the entire paper, turning it against the razor. Then make a cut in the paper beneath the hairs, close to them, from the large tear down to the small one; then pull out the thread and place beneath the paper a small piece of cotton and cloth, and draw on the paper a figure of an anchor, like the shape of myrth, and nevertheless the figure should be according to the quantity you raise with the paper which is marked at all points.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if at that part where the skill is needed, one takes a great quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make a cut along all two lines that you have marked, and begin with a large tear from one end to the other; and let it be one of the splits close to the natural hair in the thickness of a root, then turn the edge into one of the two angles at the heart, and scrape off all of it; then bring together the two edges with a single stitch using a needle and thin thread, and wipe away the blood, and remove the excess threads from the two corners without anything sticky, if you are able to do so. And if not, leave the stitching and threads for three or four days, then treat the wound without stitching with drying and constricting things, because the paper revives at the healing of the wound and its gathering together, but the stitch moves (as the ancients say), and this is work without poverty; and if in another way: it is that you mark the paper with a figure as if it were the leaf of a myrtle, as we have told, at three points according to the shape shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take what rises up with small force equally according to its form:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the pliers, and the task is not even, take a needle with thread, and wrap it around the figure; then take another thread from beneath the large tear, and the smaller one from under the small one, and twist them together equally between your fingers; then gently release your hand equally, and lift all the skin marked by you, as we have said, then sew together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; if an abscess forms at your incision, soothe it with ointment or similar soothing application; sometimes the paper-like skin grows back; in such cases, follow what we have said about the incision; but sewing is more artificial in either case.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for broken bones is as follows: you must mold the paper and make it inside according to what I said, then create two splints, thin and long like the paper and wide enough for the fracture; bind each part where you hold the bone fragments; assemble them carefully over the paper from the oil, forming the two splints from the broken parts; leave it like this for several days, and the bone that is bound will heal and stop hurting.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes time and the wound has strength, then treat it while it is still healthy; if the wound is deep, and if the paper does not adhere, and the hairs do not grow back; this is the form you will make for the two splints according to this figure and this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work involves such a task as you would prick a fine needle and wrap it with soft, thin silk thread; then align the dislocated parts and tie them gently, making the length of the threads one palm's length; next, arrange another thin silk thread quickly and tie the ends tightly together; then place the patient's head on your healthy side; and let it rest in the sun so that the work is unveiled, for it is a delicate and small task. Then push the needle through all parts to the root of the hair gently, piercing the paper hospital-style as you pull it away from the natural hair; then remove the hair up to the needle, and wrap the needle with the hair if there are one or two or three or more strands; finally, withdraw your hand until the hairs emerge completely from the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the wound is treated and the hairs do not grow with it, pull the wound out from the root to all the thread that you have arranged, until the wound comes out completely through the opening above and you see it with your eye; then pull the wound and the thread, close the eye and leave it closed for one or two days, until the hair grows back into its place and the scar appears. And if the hairs are small, accompany them with a long natural hair from the horse, and raise it with that one or as long as you keep it stretched.
de la porriture de l’oil	regarding the impurity of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness called "aleacrati" or putrefaction comes upon the body, it can manifest in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs suddenly from wounds, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of operating in this case is that you open the wound, separate the edges, and place linen strips inside, binding it tightly until it heals; and it is not appropriate to use things that dry out and restrict in the treatment of it.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than before; but it works through softening agents, such as fenugreek; and rosewater of either fresh or dried roses and flaxseed oil are cooked, and any diluent herbs melted in one of the eyes, and it covers over temporarily, and treats it.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he lowers himself now, let him see the patient before him and hold the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting briefly, then raise him again the second way, insert the instrument and when it is firmly in place and does not move up, gently extract it by rotating your hand back and forth; then lower again a little bit at a time while keeping the oil inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply the heated oil or any other moist oil mixed with rose oil and plenty of honey, and bind it with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, place hot compresses with abundance of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the substance cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, as there are many people with very hard eyes, it is necessary that you press the instrument called 'alberit', which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then pierce only the conjunctive substance, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then introduce the hot compress as we have said; and after the work is complete, provide for the patient a comfortable position to sleep in, on his back in a dark place; and let there be no movements, and feed him with light foods, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and tie him according to his condition for three days. Then release him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and make him see nothing, and then put the bandage back on for seven more days; and it is not appropriate to perform this at the time of the cure or after the incision, but it is appropriate to ease it, because acute pain rises suddenly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess appears, you must loosen the hair in front on the seventh day and apply the remedies for soothing the abscess; and once it is soothed, loosen the bandage and place a little cloth on its face to cover it for some time, and keep it in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then, leave the house little by little and recover in your own way; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Then, a man came to us from Syria who told us that in his country they use a certain root that makes people urinate freely, from which they extract water, but I have never seen or heard of it in our land, nor do I find mention of it in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of magic, for whoever does not know them will see them as different; and they should be pure gold.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head be cut from this same subtlety in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the charm on the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No one is born with these charmed figures; they do not resemble any kind of scorpion but are full of pain. And if there are such charms, either beautifully adorned with fox-colored or smooth and of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this case where the wound is hot and raw, you should place the patient between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, pour wine into those wounds, and treat them fiercely; but pull as much as you can hold in a thin, sharp instrument from one side, until you know that the wound is completely healed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is anything left that cannot be pulled out with all the delicate, thin instruments, opening it further with slight force, so that nothing remains; and without delay, cutting as it should be done; and if it are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize until the blood is completely drained from all wounds, then apply heat or cold and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he feels heat and moisture in his head, know that it is clean; but if the moisture does not come out as it should, know that there is something stuck in the upper bone, which prevents the instruments from cutting. Then you must insert a thread of linen somewhat thick, being careful with your hands, and leave between each space the desired or lesser distance, and place the patient's foot in the thread at his convenience, and pull gently while smelling until it comes through the gum inside the mouth; and often children do so at school, and it is a light thing for him who wants to do it. Then hold the head that comes through the gum with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, knowing one after the other as we who are in thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as you know, corrupt the new charcoal, then treat the child, wipe away the blood, and moisten the wound with Egyptian ointment, and put it back to the neck as before; do this for three days or more until the ointments corrode all that is remaining of the charred flesh. Then place a moist compress on the neck for no more than a day while it heals, and if there is a need for drying medicines, use them; this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, with which one distills oils and medicines into the neck.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or gold, resembling an open lamp, like a pipe, and use it thus; if you see, make a closed pipe, and let the instruments be full to purge the head; and have many at hand for the head to hold when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the pain near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often, near the nose, a pain arises called "telul," which swells and grows very large, making it a thing of concern to look at; and for this reason, you must catch it at the beginning, take it all out completely, then apply cautery or the burning medicine; and if one delays in treating it until it becomes large, be careful if it is hard, of poor color, or without sensation: do not touch it with iron, because it is an abscessed joint, for when you treat it, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is sensitive, not of poor color, and you see that it can be completely treated, empty the patient gently and apply the treatment without causing pain, curing the limb from things drying and restricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is broken and bruised
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	You know that when the fragments of these powerful cartilages come together, it brings little relief, indeed, to no one.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to do nothing when the wound is fresh and filled with blood; then close the two lips with a single stitch, and treat it until it heals; if the lips are already separated on one side or the other, you must scrape all parts of their core while they heal, then bring the two lips together with another stitch, and tighten them, and apply powder made from dragon's blood and incense that has been ground; place a piece of strong or other adhesive plaster over the powders, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat the wound with care until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is such that you bring the wound together: either with needles, as we have said in sewing the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, the abscesses on the lips appear as hard, grain-like bumps, both small and large. Then you must turn the lips and make a cut in each one, using pincers to pull out the pus and applying vitriole (a caustic substance) to each part after the incision; then use a dry leaf to clean the wound until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	from the condition of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a condition afflicts the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; it is necessary that you hold it with tongs, and cut at its root, allowing the bowel or abscess to drain; then place upon it vitriol powder, or other restrictive and desiccant powders; and if this condition returns after incision, and often occurs, especially when cutting the gums a second time, and cauterizing them: if it does not return after cauterization; these are the shapes of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of disorders
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	No teeth should be forced together at the gum line, between the rough and unpleasant scales; nor should they be black and yellow and rotten as long as the corruption affects the gums, making them stinky; it is necessary that you make the patient hold still in your hands, keeping his teeth or gums firmly in place until nothing remains; and so do with black, green, jaundice, and other kinds of decay, as long as they are present. If you remove what is at the root cause, it is good; if not, continue to try again on the second and third days, until everything has been removed; and know that teeth require various types of instruments for removal, according to what the work demonstrates, because the tool used to remove them from between the teeth has a different shape than that used to remove them at the gum line; and these shapes should all be prepared in advance.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	You should cure the tooth of its pain as soon as possible, for you must not delay treating it at all, for it is a very delicate matter so there is no excuse for postponing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is in great pain, it is necessary that you be certain about the tooth's condition.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the patient cries out from the pain, believing it to be from a tooth infection, and has it pulled; but nevertheless, the pain does not cease until the abscess is drained, for we have already experienced this with many patients; and when you are certain about the tooth's condition, you should cut around it with a sharp instrument to protect the gums from all sides. Then use tweezers to grasp it gently at the first sign of movement, as carefully as possible, until it is well dislodged.
