Affirm your hold on the tweezers and place the tooth between your fingers under your jaw, holding it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take none of these instruments and push it gently from every side, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is broken and chipped, it is necessary to fill the gap with cloth, either at the opening or the perforation; and if it is tightened tightly with pliers, be careful not to break it while pulling; and it must be done very carefully around the gum line to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Be very careful not to break it, and if a piece breaks off, return it to the patient; due to the evil of its root, it will cause greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not act like the ignorant healers who, out of haste and foolishness, break the vessel many times, and do not listen to what we have said; but they bring about a great illness through their words, either because of the roots where it dwells or because of the vessel that is broken, as often happens; and when the wound is deep, wash the place with wine or honey and silk; and the flow of blood comes, which often occurs, if you employ vitriol paste; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one first mutely extracts the tooth, should be long and sharp with thick handles, so that they do not bend when pulling the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have strong members that do not bend when pulled, made of well-forged iron, and toothed for proper movement.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains stuck when pulled, it is necessary to place cotton moistened with butter on it for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the eyes are moistened, then apply the pliers called 'algefri', which resemble a bird's beak, and they should be made as follows:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out of these claws, it is necessary that you uncover the whole area around the root, and place the instrument called "alethal" or "palainche", which has this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is very hard and does not break, and the root jumps out by itself, that is good; if not, use all the instruments whose shapes are as follows:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument with two prongs, its shape is:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are used in the treatment of teeth, and of this tool which resembles large pliers, whose form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	This tool should be of a strength that it cannot break, and you must know that many tools for teeth exist; and also other tools, which are not mentioned. The most skilled surgeons invent their own instruments, according to what their work and the illness show them, because there are certain diseases for which no instrument was taught by the ancients. If a part breaks or an object is stuck in a bone, and he seeks the appropriate instrument that I have told you about, and uses gestures, then its form is as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and well-holding to hold the bone, that it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then return the limb to suitable medicines for this, and if there is putrefaction in the bone, small or large, use all these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural course of things and its shape is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the one before it, and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or polished: then extract it. And if it is loose with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a small beak, made of sharp steel.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And take a small, sharp knife in your hands each day for the pain in your teeth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it from one side as this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	It is also like filing the iron that makes the needles; file the tooth little by little in your hands every day gently, so it does not move until it heals; then, at the end, there should be no jagged edge, and if the tooth is too sharp, it bleeds the tongue, so you must file its roughness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth aches severely, whether by impact or pulling, and the patient cannot bear pressure on it, he suffers from a painful condition. Treatments with restricting medicines are ineffective in such cases; instead, they should be restrained with a golden thread. Note that silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes. The thread should neither be too thin nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth. If you need to align the teeth, take the thread and loop it double between two healthy teeth, then place the aching tooth(es) in between the healthier ones. Continue tightening until you reach gently yet firmly the sound tooth on the other side. Then repeat the process from the beginning until the aching tooth is secure at the root.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the joints with a pair of pliers, assemble them, and reinsert them between the healthy tooth, and arrange it so that the tongue does not get damaged; and then leave it as tight as possible, and if it loosens, the thread will unravel, if held by another thread; it should remain in this position for the entire duration, and this is the shape of the teeth and the proper arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, as you can see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is removed and replaced in its socket, fresh one by fresh one, as we have said; it should only be done by someone skilled and patient, and never shaped like a bone of a weak tooth, but placed in the missing spot, held as we have said, and remain so for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to uncover the tongue's ligaments
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No, these are the ligaments that originate from beneath the tongue, either naturally or due to a deep wound; and the work involves opening the mouth of the patient with care, so that his head is in your hand, and gently lifting the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament widely, as much as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or any resistance, and this is due to a sudden wound, then use a hook and cut the ligament widely; be careful not to cut too deeply, in order not to harm the artery beneath; and after you have done this, raise the tongue with rosewater or some other soothing liquid, then apply a thin linen cloth under the tongue; repeat this for each patient every night, so that the ligaments do not harden.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the flow of blood comes, apply vinegar to it immediately; and if the pain intensifies, cauterize it with a slow-burning caustic, which is good for this; then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it is of red, black, or hard color, so the patient does not smell it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it inclines to white and there is moisture, pour vinegar on it and cut it with a fine spatula from both sides; and if the pain persists in your care, apply vitriole ground until it is stained, then return to your care as you remove everything; then lift the limb gently and slowly, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	from the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No sign of these abscesses in the throat, which are called "godath," should appear, and they are properly known as the II amandres. And when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they remain untreated, be careful: if they are small and have a thin, pale color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is thick, do not touch them with iron, also to prevent the spread of pus; but leave them until they die, and then you will remove them, or they might break on their own. And if they are white in color and the root is thin, have a ready instrument to cover them, but first ensure that the abscesses are calm and at ease.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit before the sun, and his feet in a healthy position, and open the mouth, and press the tongue down with the instrument between his hands, pressing it firmly to the end of the tool, from which the shape is formed; and let it be made of silver or fine gold as if it were a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You cannot press the tongue down onto all of this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the hook and the file and insert them into it, pulling upward as much as possible; and do not touch any part of the threads with your fingers, but cut it off with the instrument, from which the shape resembles a forceps; nevertheless, the head is bent, one side towards the other, and they are very sharp, made either of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, if you make it with pincers, then it has this form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	It should be carved on one side and smooth on the other. Once you have shaped one of the mandibles, shape the other in the same manner, and after the incision, rinse the patient's mouth with hot water and cold, clear water, and if bleeding occurs, rinse the patient's mouth with water treated with pomegranate peel or myrrh or similar substances until the blood is stopped. Then apply the cure as long as it remains clean; and no other abscesses will form in the throat besides the two mandibles, so shape them just like the two mandibles.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was in her throat, namely a small abscess; and had she tightly closed the whole throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passageway, and could neither eat nor drink, she would have died if she remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had forced two ribs through the two openings in the throat where it originated.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then quickly inserted a probe into one of the openings and pulled it through, causing great pain; I withdrew it and did the same on the other side, opening the throat and pressing the tongue; afterward, I inserted the probe into these abscesses and extracted some pus; and thus was the passage from the throat of the woman opened, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to drain the abscess for a long time; but the abscess returned again, filling the space that I had emptied, becoming quite large. Then I seared it within the throat and so it healed; in this way it did not return, and I departed from these tasks, leaving God to complete them after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the retina descends into the eye, and it is swollen and detached, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thin and round, it is called "retina".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have mentioned in the previous section, but the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscess is calming down, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to drain it; and the round one that is not completely detached; and it is bloody or of a bright red or black color, then be careful not to cut into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the poor patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see this, according to the manner I have said, you should make the patient lie face towards the sun and press his tongue with the instrument we spoke of earlier; then insert the hook in the eye and pull from behind, and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned for incising the stones.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is important that you do not remove more than the excess beyond the natural limit, because if you do, it will cause great pain to speech and movement; and after incision, use what we said for incising the stones and dress it as long as it is clean.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient suffers from great pain, it is necessary that you use tools for cauterizing the sensitive parts.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of cauterization should be sharp and swift.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place his head on a healthy surface and then press his tongue against the instrument described in this chapter of cauterization with firm but not too harsh pressure; using the movement of this instrument, which has the following shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the head have a hair or cloth on which to place the medicine, like the shape of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and have the patient lie on his side so that saliva and mucus from his mouth can wash the medicine down without going to the throat and causing pain; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for about half an hour until you see it dry up and the stinging of the medicine subsides; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around the instrument and dip it in the medicine, and continue moving the instrument over the cotton on top of the eye until the cotton dries on the eye; repeat this several times until the cauterization is complete, then leave it to dry for three or four days. And if you need to re-apply the cauterization with the medicine, do so, and after cauterizing, wipe it around the eye using cotton dipped in medicine, and then clean it with cold water and make gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than cauterization, especially for incision; if it is carried out by fumigation in this manner, take plenty of calament, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, and similar herbs, and combine them all or any of them in a pot, and put it on the fire; let the mixture be well cooked over a strong flame, and place the pot on a hot stone according to this method.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or gold, and one of the feet should be pressed into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, while the eye remains moist; after that, it often recurs as the eye dries, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, as many complications can arise; and only perform this when the hot abscess declines.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a cane and insert within the mouth a piece of wool soaked in vinegar, so that it does not burn too much for the patient; for the woolen strand does not let the hot vapor burden the mouth, and this is a good cure together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a burning sensation occurs in the throat from bone or fish spine, or some other thing. Therefore, it is necessary that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing move; and if it does not open and remains stuck in the throat, it is good to make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach. Perhaps this will dislodge the foreign object through vomiting. Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval gant, or a leaf of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread; and ties a thread to the sponge, and then swallows it; and when it reaches the throat, it will burn, and then you can pull it out forcefully. And if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of salt according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be bent towards the throat so it can enter more easily, and hold the head raised high; beware not to touch the epiglottis, lest all of it comes down, nor push any bones inside; and make sure the patient pushes the instrument, because it needs to move in order for the object to come out; if it goes down into the throat, pull it out slowly until it is completely out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the throat treated with medicine, as I said in the previous division, other than through the use of medications; and if it does not benefit, then look into the throat of the patient at sunrise, and press their tongue with the instrument I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, pull it free from every tiny thorn, or subtle pincers that it holds.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if the wound does not heal, take a horsehair, and insert it into the throat of the patient, then pull or raise the hair slowly, doing this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in slowly, letting the patient swallow it, doing this often; and immediately as the wound feels the water, it will close.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not break as we have said, and infuses the patient with bad odor from the fumigation of the eye, do this many times, for it will eventually come without warning.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The method of fumigation consists of filling a pot with hot coals and placing a perforated cover over it; the instrument should be placed in the hole in the center of the cover. The patient then puts the tip of the cane in their mouth, seals their mouth, and inhales the fumes until they reach the back of their throat, without letting any smoke escape. If the mucus does not come out, repeat the fumigation many times. The patient should endure thirst and eat salty and spicy foods, avoiding water; then, it will be necessary for him to spit out the mucus using this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if it is possible to see it, resembles a curved claw that enters the throat, and it looks like a hawk's beak, and has the roughness of lime, so that whatever it takes hold of, it cannot leave. And here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many appearances of abscesses are, according to the remembrance that this book presents here and there, diverse in their openings and dimensions; and they exist in two ways, one being of the same appearance, and those that retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the head is different from that of the base, and the abscess of the fleshy limb is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if, for abscesses, one must not pierce the bowel until it is completely dead according to its completion; and if for others it is necessary to pierce when they are hardened, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are in the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from damaged joints, and they are left until the pus is drained around them, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is in the main member and you delay the incision until it is gangrened, it will harm the principal member; or if it is from the foundation, perforate it only when it is thoroughly gangrened, otherwise it will not be cut completely, remain inside, and become a fistula, and will not heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the moment of perforation of the abscess which is killed according to completion, and this is when the pain is soothed, and the fever departs, and the pain and redness diminish, and the swelling of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation depend more on the abscess itself, and there where it moves; and let the perforation be long in the body, and if the abscesses are in hands or feet, or in joints and tendons and arteries, and everywhere equally without any swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when there are abscesses in soft flesh, it is better that you do not make an incision until the swelling subsides after the digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you make an incision too early, the body's defenses will weaken due to the wound, and it will be filled with bad humors; and by chance, the lips may harden and become attached to it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscesses that have been pierced are too deep into the flesh, according to what the member requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should treat them with small incisions, small openings; and in large incisions, large openings, and many fissures according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to press the heart, and cover; when they have reached a suitable size like a cloth, and are softened, then you should treat them as you do with blisters: and if there are such that are cut in three angles, and if there are such which are covered like the fleece of mistletoe, like the abscesses of an attack; and if there are such where a large size is made, and other sizes and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those who do not have a head, like a superficial sore abscess, you should pierce it thoroughly; and if the abscess is large, and it has collected great bowels, and you pierce it, without draining all the bowels at that time, but only part of them; then stop the abscess for the next day, and then do nothing from there on; repeat this many times, gradually, until the bowels are completely drained; especially if the patient is of weak strength, a pregnant woman, or small children, or old, decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For often the patient jumps at the result of the bowel movement, which may suddenly cause the sick person to die, and you should not be surprised.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Beware therefore of this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, if the wound is clean, and the abscess wound is small, then apply a thin cloth or fresh cotton; but if it is a large abscess with many openings, then put a tent over each one so that they press against each other. And if in the abscess there is a part of hard skin, and you have cut it around, then fill it with old cotton or linen raspings without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and treat the wound with medicine until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the bleeding occurs in your work, apply cold water and ice, moisten the bandage, and lay it on the affected area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bleeding persists, apply government and treatment, as well as the powders I mentioned in this book, and if it is a deep wound or an abscess, it is necessary to place moistened cloths and drapes on top; and if the wound is fresh, moistened with wine and hot oil; and if it is chronic and the flesh is fleshy, lay moistened cloths with cold water and fresh oil, or wine and hot oil, until the third day, as we have said; then remove the abscess and clean and treat it as appropriate, as long as it remains healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know this universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have already told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and now see this chapter.
des soros	from blood
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Often, small abscesses come from the head, and they appear in various forms, just like the pus of a wound or that of a boil, and there are many similar conditions.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are large and soft, containing moisture, just like veins; and others that are hard and resistant to cutting, but there is no doubt if the arteries do not oppose them.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work on the body if such that you should try all instruments called 'entangling', from which the form comes as follows, containing something.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they make a hole from above down through it.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, it pulls out nothing leaving the skin that contained the moisture, for it returns again when you leave nothing; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; if not, use water and string, and apply to the wound, and leave until the other day; and this will cure what has been left behind due to night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the bandage again, as before, on the second and third days, until you know for certain that it does not remain during the night; then treat the wound with suitable care until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if an abscess becomes hard, following this form, it should be incised lengthwise; and drain the pus, and scrape from all sides, and apply all your care to draw out the pus from where it lies; and if the artery reacts contrary, do as I have told you.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same with an abscess that is pus-filled, and cut and treat it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut the abscess and the moist flesh first; it is lighter because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if none of these abscesses or boils have any moisture, and these are the type of abscesses that I found on an old woman's chest; I found the abscess as hard, rough, and white like a stone, unyielding, and if one tried to break it, it would cause just as much damage as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that appear on the head, especially those at the top of a child's head or at the root of the ear, the opening should be kept completely open for as long as possible to allow the pus to drain; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess appears in the neck, and it dissolves the adhesions, and causes anger, and never comes anywhere else on the body, and they are painful, and are entwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly inside its rib, as we have said of the new and abscess from the head, and these scrofulas have many similarities.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others of a malign nature that will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those you see with a good disposition for touch, resembling the healthy color of the flesh, silent from every side and not exposed as the skin around the neck or the artery or vessel, and not too deep; it is necessary that you sever it from above, peel it from every part, and the two lips of the heart remain in their place, if need be, as we have said in the chapters on the head; and move it little by little, ensuring you do not cut the nerve or vein, and do not let the scalpel slip, so that your hand is safe, and look forward with caution, so you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you sever the vein or artery and it does not allow you to work, apply vitriole (a corrosive substance) or any powder that stops blood flow, constricts the wound, and leaves it until the inflammation subsides, and the wound softens, then begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is stained with blood, it returns to your work until you complete it; then pay close attention to your skilled indication if there are no small abscesses remaining, if you drain and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the abscess, it is not enough that you drain only the abscess at its root, but you should tie it with a double strand strong thread and leave it to heal without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian dressing, and cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you drain the entire abscess, it is necessary that you close both edges of the wound and sew them now, so that there is no delay due to the size of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you want to understand how to deal with it, and pull it out firmly, and cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have an excess, pierce them where they appear to be dying; and the piercing should be done as mentioned before, depending on it, then apply these treatments with bandages and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what is left from the corruption; and once the wound is well cleaned, continue the healing treatment until it is healed.
de squinance	squinance (Old French) translates to "squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	They old ones spoke and discussed about the incision of the throat; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with squint, it is necessary to avoid the incision of the throat known as "epiglote"; no aid should be provided for this, because all the veins and the source of the pain are in those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the tongue, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to prevent the damage that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it through three circles or four small cuts across, between two circles or according to the size of the cut, without touching the cartilage; and these cuts are most suitable for cutting through the epiglottis, so that there is no sticking, and the wound heals quickly.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the surgeon is afraid, it is necessary that he stretches the throat skin to the entire opening, then cuts through the heart until it reaches the trachea; and avoid blood vessels, if you see any, and then cut through the tissue, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the river of the trachea that comes out through the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and doubt arises about the strangulation, gather the two edges of the wound together where the cartilage is, and cut it completely through; then administer medications that promote healing as long as it remains healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuscasim (a type of herb) should not be used until the throat is completely sealed, and the patient is considered near death, as it lacks effectiveness.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then, they should open the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, thus preventing death; and for this reason, the ancients advised to keep the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, which takes three or four days. And then they ordered to close the wound and treat it as long as it was healing; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a damsel was wounded by a knife, and she stabbed it into her throat, cutting part of the tongue from the gum; and I was called to cure her, and I found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and realized that she had not coughed up any pus or phlegm, nor had the injury caused any discharge other than into the throat, and the vein had burst from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I acted swiftly, sewed up the wound, and cured her until she was completely healed; and she could not speak for lack of voice, but later recovered fully; therefore, I say that in the surgery of the epiglottis there is no need to be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	from the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cysts known as "throat hernias" are large abscesses with the appearance of a pus-filled sac, and they predominantly affect women; they present in two manners: natural and accidental, where the former has no apparent cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And accidental hernias present in two manners: one resembles fatty tissue, and the other appears as an abscess stemming from an artery; these cases instill fear, and it is not advisable to perform any surgical incisions unless absolutely necessary. If you discover a hernia resembling fat and find no apparent cause, treat it like a common nose hernia by carefully cutting away the affected skin and ensuring complete healing.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways by which we can suffer, of which I will describe all their appearances; and now it is necessary that I explain the distinction between our state and its origin.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the origin is heat and fever as long as the ebullition persists, and when putrefaction is complete, then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new birth, there is no heat, no fever, or pain, and it possesses satisfaction, which is its own sac, according to the color of the body, and begins like a seed, becoming fat; and they are similar in two ways, either greasy or moist, and have much the same color as I mentioned in the previous division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is important when you approach the treatment of a new patient that you first test and inquire about all instruments called "entromissory" according to their form, as described in the subsequent chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	The method of inquiring about abscesses is to press more or less moistently on the abscess, and move your fingers in and out little by little, until you know that the instrument has reached the center, then, according to the size of the abscess, extract the entromissory tool, and be careful not to let it slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the abscess is surrounded by a hard crust, it has the same color as described for other abscesses; and if the entromissory tool does not come out moist, know that it is full of pus, so make a cross with it, and grasp it with pincers, and peel it gently from each side, taking care to remove all the pus, or wash it with new bandages until it becomes clean. If you cannot do this, cut off pieces of it, removing everything.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it does not move, the pain returns many times; and if it moves a little bit and does not cause great discomfort, it employs the wound with some corrosive powders or hot water, constricts the wound, applies soothing things to the abscess, and treats other ailments until it is healed; and if the pain is great, it cuts both sides of the wound and treats it accordingly.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the pain is intense or other discomfort occurs and you hurry, use the vitriol powder and leave it for two or three days until the wound purifies and the inflammation of the blood subsides; then return to cover what has come undone from the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the shapes of the instruments introduced, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters called "albaret", and one called "breb", and they are also like needles used to cut through sorceries, made of gold, silver, or iron, and move best when yellow, and are most effective for encircling fistular corbs; and these are also of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the hooks are very similar, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and there are also hooks with two curves in three ways; and some hooks have three curves, also in three ways; and others have two curves, or even just one curve, and they are also in three sizes; all these are necessary for their use.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The tip of these instruments is sharp, and there are some that do not cut through both sides, which tear the skin, because one does not sever the vein or nerve; and these insertions are blades placed in several ways, so that the patient does not lose blood when opening abscesses; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and they should only be used on fleshy parts like legs, arms, breasts, wounds, and similar places; and one never makes a smaller instrument resembling a forceps, according to this form, to stop the flow of blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it should never be placed in places that heal poorly after cutting veins and arteries, and never according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflate the breasts of any man when they begin to be corrupted, as long as they appear like women's breasts; they remain ugly and swollen, and anyone who wishes to cure them must do so according to this form described in this line b until g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and apply medicinal herbs with charred wine to the wound, then sew together the two edges of the wound, and treat it until it is healthy; if the breast dips downward, and becomes soft due to its size, just as in women, if it has two cuts, like splits, then one should hold onto the other at the end of each, so that the larger cut contains the smaller according to this form described in this line b to line g. Then scrape off the leather between the two edges, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for treatment, until it heals; if it does not heal, or the incision has not been properly made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood flow, then you should fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive dressing, and leave it until it removes the fat and flesh, then treat it until it is healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	from the abscesses of armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are hard scrofulous nodules or they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line B to line G.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply a wound dressing of clean cotton, leaving it for another day, then remove all the cotton and continue with appropriate treatment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, then do it as we have said about cutting into scrofula, and if the wound opens, apply the fire cautery as we have mentioned before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When an artery ruptures and the tissue above it sears, many abscesses often form, and similarly, there is often a swollen vein with an abscess; and if one knows thus when it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and severe; and when you feel this in your limbs, it feels strange; and when it is due to the vein, it appears red and inflamed; and it is folly to treat such an abscess, especially when it is deep within joints and muscles and other places, and it is very great.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should seek iron cautery, and whoever is in charge should also be cautious, and for those with an artery close to the skin, make a cut from above the flesh down; then carefully sever the artery from its attachments just as you have been taught when extracting the two arteries within the temple. Then mark the space between the two cuts with an instrument until no pus remains, and treat the abscess; then apply the appropriate dressing while the wound is still infected; and care for any subsequent treatment as needed, until it heals. If the abscess is located alongside a vein, be sure to keep your hand over the entire area, then insert the needle from below the affected area, and pierce it through, forming a double thread, so that you can pull it from the other side; then bind the abscess as I have instructed, or tie the thread to one of the two ends. If you doubt whether the thread has completely detached, insert another needle into all the remaining parts of the abscess, just as with the first, and pull out a total of three threads; then remove the excess material until only the healthy tissue remains, and apply a moist cloth, followed by treatments and dressings until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	from the abscesses of nails
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly to abscesses in arteries and veins, nails can also develop abscesses when they are injured or subjected to excessive work, among other things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this occurs more frequently in joints and fingers where there are many articulations, which is a source of great abscesses, and their appearance resembles the color of the flesh, and they are in various forms filled with pain; and when they are pressed, the patient feels great pain, and it is not entirely whole like the heart, but remains in the center; and it moves well from all sides, neither advancing nor retreating, neither downwards nor upwards, and the one that is in the joints should not be covered with iron; perhaps it would cause contraction; and those on the head or forehead make the flesh splotchy.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, and it has a clipper, cut it at its base; and if it's large, suspend it with a hook, then scrape off the skin, remove the flesh, and stitch up the wound until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	Des grosses boces pendants" translates directly to "hanging large mouths
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	It never occurs in the belly alone, but elsewhere as well, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its appearance, it has subtle roots, and large droppings; and there are both small and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two or three funguses in his belly that were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, had thin roots, and were constantly oozing with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I collected them and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6 Z., and the work of incising is such that if you look at the patient, they are moist, and the color of the artel (joint) is pale and moist and of subtle root; if it sticks to a wide spatula, then perform fire cautery in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For cutting often brings too much blood loss, and if it weakens you, then hurry to cauterize; and if you see the patient afraid and anxious about the incision, take a well-made thread and bind the joint as we have said, leaving it for two days; then restrain it, and do not stop pulling the thread until it detaches the joint, without effort; and if the roots are thick, be afraid to cut them, especially in the abdomen, but you can still cut half of them, then cauterize so that it does not return. Then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the tissue which is of dark color and poor quality and full of pus.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess enlarged, and I will come to the treatment of the ulcer after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is closed for too long.
