Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the wound comes from cauterization of the flesh or a fracture of the bone, and it is on the belly and not in any of the bowels, as it happens with other ruptures, or of blood that cuts veins or arteries according to what is above, or of farts; and if it is due to the rupture through the bone and through the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of flesh, and is a small thing without pain, and has various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed at its ends, it re-forms, and then returns, and sometimes it narrows, and widens greatly at the entrance of the bath and through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and opens well when pressed in the hand, without constraint; and if it is due to blood, it appears through these signs: a thick and hard abscess, inserted according to its quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it feels soft to the touch, and the severity is such that you must look to see if it is the blood of an artery, or a vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary, you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For in the case of abscesses, as I described in the chapter on veins and arteries, there is often doubt and fear, which can lead to death.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if it appears to be an intestinal or bowel issue, you must instruct the patient to keep their rectum relaxed and completely open; then make incisions around the abscess, stretching it straight, and cut across the entire width of the abscess; tie it firmly with a strong thread or sturdy silk string, making sure the intestines are not squeezed; then open the abscess while it is tied, and gently pull on the intestines; if you find them caught in the string, release them and bring the intestines out through the opening; if it's a bowel issue, take care at the anvil, cutting off excess tissue; if the artery or vein obstructs your work, move around it carefully, then take two needles and push them through in the shape of a cross that you made with your initial incision; pull the abscess apart three times with the needles, and if visible, remove the needles, leaving the abscess to heal on its own until it disappears, and treat the wound as necessary, completing the abscess treatment as we have said; then drain any blood or moisture you find, treat the area as appropriate, and close the wound.
dou chancre	A deep ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the previous section the appearances of chancre and how to treat it with medicine, and how to avoid the cure of iron; we say that chancre should be attacked in the early stages, and great caution should be taken when treating it, and they advise that when a chancre is located where it can be cut out like the one on the mammary gland, or the ankle, or similar places, it must all be removed when it is in its beginning; but when it is large and old, it is not appropriate to approach it, for I have never been able to heal any, nor has anyone else before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for the work when it is located where it can be removed as we have said, it is that you do not at any time purge the patient of black blood; then make it healthier if there is a visible fullness, and cut out the illness in the good place to perform the work; then pour on your poultices or chancre, and the head from all sides, and remove it from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow completely, and examine the wound with your hand or any object, and if the bleeding continues after the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood is stopped. Then apply another cure as long as it is healed.
de ydropisie	From hydropsie (a condition marked by excessive fluid accumulation
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have previously described the similarities of hydropsie (a condition marked by excessive fluid accumulation) and in what way the assembly of water is formed within it, the signs of each manifestation, and the cure that is carried out through medicine, and that which is cured with iron: only in this case; and one should not touch iron in these two manifestations: namely, tympanites and yposarche, as it is a mortal thing. Therefore, when you administer medicine to this manifestation of hydropsie called "eclites" by medicine, and the cure does not benefit, if the patient is weak or has another illness other than hydropsie, such as stomach distress or similar conditions; then do not touch iron, for there is doubt. And if you see the patient possesses strong vitality, and he only suffers from hydropsie alone, and is neither too young nor too old, then thus should you proceed: place the patient in a sitting position on your hands, and have the minister press the abdomen towards the lower part while expelling the water, then take the sharp spatula according to this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And make incisions from both parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Pierce with a point, but do not insert it so deeply that it reaches the intestines when pushed in, and do not let it burst; then observe if there is any droplet formation towards the intestines. It is necessary to make an incision through three-quarters of the bowel, directly below the armpit, and if the drops are due to a liver disease, make the incision on the left side of the armpit; but if it is due to the urinary bladder, it should be on the right side. Do not let the patient lie on the incision to avoid any excess fluid flowing to the weak point. Then cut through all the skin with an instrument, and the bladder, and gently press your hand against all the tissues between the skin and the underlying structures as if scraping with a fingernail or slightly around it; then pierce the bladder until the tissue becomes pale, which is the sign of blood vessels, and remove the instrument. This is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a delicate silver chain, thin as gold or bronze, and has one small opening in the center, three on one side, and two on the other; and the part is cut like a feather, which is the shape of the incision that scribes make to cut feathers.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of it, there is a cavity, so that when the tool comes to the water, it sinks immediately onto the instrument; then empty half or a third of it, for if you empty more than is necessary at that time, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit into the weapon, or he may lose his palm, or approach death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the sick person suggest, and his pulses; then take up the instrument and hold back the water, which is now retained by the stop that closes the opening on the side we spoke about, then pierce in this manner; then repeat the process the next day, if you see the patient suffering from it, and draw out a small quantity of blood; do this every day, and be careful not to let any water remain for too long.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave much water, whether through the cure of a burial or hot sand, or by sweating or a bath or in the sun, and it turns to drinking; and apply dry medicines until it is healed, and cauterize the stomach and liver and spleen after draining the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	from the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without an opening in the penis, or if the opening is small, or it is not properly positioned.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary at once that he does not pierce all the subtle spatulum according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then open the subtle hole in the bladder and hold it closed for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the closure so he can urinate, and then put it back; and sometimes it is not necessary at all, because the force of the urine will not allow you to keep it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the hole is small, it is treated with a gentle closure of the bladder, as we have said, so it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the rupture in their place are blighted, because none are born with a rupture at the top of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot come up to the bladder, and this is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method for performing it is that the patient lies on their stomach, then the penis is stretched and lifted up as much as a quill, so that the rupture can be made in the right place; and beware of the discharge of blood which comes many times, and if it occurs, stop it from those who stop the bleeding, and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	from the pus of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often, this affliction appears on the penis, and it manifests in a disagreeable manner; there are both malignant and benign cases. You must prick them gently with a needle, drain them, and then clean and bandage them with moist cotton in an Egyptian ointment. Then apply the healing ointment as needed until they heal.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the affliction is malignant, with pus and an unpleasant odor, it requires cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have achieved it, and if the splint is in a sleeping state, with some part within the flesh and some part outside, then you must first remove the splint that is inside; and when it is dried, then treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, unless you are certain about the condition of the splint that it is not broken, it will turn black and corrupt in the bone and joint; then it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply a plaster made of honey and flour from crushed red apples and times, and continue to treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two ways: that is to say, for the bleeding and for the corruption. If the tip of the knife is rotten and withdrawn, it is necessary to push or guide the knife with a plug of cloth, and let the patient urinate; and if the hair at the top of the penis is dry on those who have never been circumcised, or there is a wound or abscess, then you must scrape it with a sharp instrument until the strings are loosened, and free the part of the penis from all sides. And if it is difficult to decide how to do this, it is necessary to scrape it with a certain spoon-like instrument from the top of the penis and the scrotum; then gently separate them, and place a thin, moist linen cloth on it in cold water so that it does not dry out directly.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a dislocation of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own will, especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best and lightest work for their healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, as they do not practice it in their laws, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and elders who practiced circumcision in those days, strong and skilled, using an entirely new instrument; it was customary for them to cut one cord while preserving the other, or perhaps they would remove both at once.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or she returns with double pain, and the point of the limb is not assured during washing, and perhaps the iron escapes and the wound is corrupted, and the work is ruined, and often they heal in such a way that no further washing is needed, and I wish it so.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the washing done with force, I have found the benefit of experimentation, for the forces cut just as well from above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, if the cut is even in all parts; but ensure the thread is well twisted around the skin; and make the first operation in such a way that the child, if it understands, thinks that you are only tightening the thread around the stick and then making it tremble in every possible way; then straighten it between your hands and spread the forces between your hands or beneath your feet so that the boy does not see them, nor any of the instruments. Then pull your hand away from the stick and blow on it, pulling it upward until the end of the stick is completely free; then wash it well with the dirt that is collected on it, tie a double knot around the wound, then tie it to another thread below, keeping two fingers on the second tie at the pouch and the proper index, then cut between the two threads, then lift the heart gently and pull the end of the stick; let the blood flow slowly, for it is curative. Then apply powder above and below, covering it with a gluey strip from half an egg cooked in rose water, mixed with good rose oil and fresh herbs, and leave it until the next day, treating it in another way as long as it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of purification is as follows: both shoulders should be held and cut, and the shoulder blades should also be large and equally balanced.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in purification is when the veins escape during incision; then you must extend your finger to press them, so that they do not form an abscess; and treat it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, use tweezers and then treat it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed three days, and the skin under the arrow is swollen, leave it until the abscess has healed, and gently peel off the wound; treat it as best you can, and be careful to avoid the arrow's tip, and there will be no harm done.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the wound suddenly caused by gunpowder, which we have spoken of in treating about powders, and if one takes too much care beyond measure, and it goes above, then it will not harm; treat it therefore, as we have said, while it is clean.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to an obstruction such as a stone, or frozen blood, or bowels, or a newborn, or similar conditions, as we have discussed in the previous section. If the urine cannot be released and you notice retention caused by a stone in the bladder or neck, it is necessary for the patient to be bent over his knees; pressure should then be applied to his lower back, and he should be made to extend his abdomen upwards, towards the small of his back, thereby constricting the neck of the bladder around the stone. This action will often cause the urine to flow. If, however, this does not work, and the patient experiences severe pain, a syringe (a device consisting of a tube with a needle at one end) should be used to extract the urine as quickly as possible. The syringe should be made of thin, light silver, roughly 10.5 cm long, and easy to handle.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method of urination is as follows: take a double thread, tie one end to a ball of wool or cotton, and insert the thread into the syringe; cut off the excess wool and insert it up to the top of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and place the patient on a bed. Elevate the bladder and the urethra with moist oil and olive oil and still water; gently insert the syringe into the urethra until it reaches the root of the urethra, then double it over towards the opening. Insert the syringe in front up to just before the bladder, let the patient feel the urine flowing out until it empties, and if it does not follow this order properly because the direction of the thread is twisted; cut off the thread at each knot of wool, and the urine will follow the thread, then pull it out and drain the urine. Repeat the syringe until the bladder is empty and relieve the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	From the illnesses of the bladder.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorching or inflammation comes to the bladder, due to putrefaction gathered therein, you should view it as a distillation of waters and medications. This is done with an instrument called a "clepsydre", and its form is thus:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is sealed, and if it has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see; the lever's edge by which the medicine cuts so well the sensation without addition, if one can drain the moisture and push as necessary. And when you pour your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the instrument in the moisture and draw out gently the substance within; then pull the lever firmly towards itself. The moisture will follow the lever into the bladder immediately, that the patient may feel it; and this is the form of a delicate enema by which one enemas the bladder: thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or gold, and the wound is deeper; then take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you wish to use for enema, tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat this moisture over fire; then insert the enema into the rectum, and press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make it circular, and pierce it roundly; then thread a strong string through these holes, assemble the circle as one assembles a dal, and put inside what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it with the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed the methods of treating stones and their extraction along with various medicinal practices; I have explained the distinction between stones that cause rain and all the signs, and in which cases one should perform surgery; concerning the bladder and the penis, I will now clearly and succinctly tell you.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign of acute urinary retention, similar to the clarity of water; it opens the urethra and greatly pains the patient, often repeating itself, and then becoming chronic; and it attacks the foundations [of health]. The treatment for children up to four years old is light, but much more difficult in the case of the elderly, and is a middle ground for those between youth and old age; the cure is lighter for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with a cleanse bath, in order to draw out all impurities from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often gets stuck while trying to pass the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and upright them, moving them away from the body so that the stone descends completely into the bladder, without getting stuck in the upper part; then place him between your hands with his legs away from his hips, so that the bladder is tilted downward; then search and touch inside. If you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out at the touch, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, and if the patient is weak, use your middle finger, and if they are young and robust, press down on their lower back, grasp the stone, and when you feel it against your finger, apply pressure upwards from the outside or where you see the cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the helper to press the bladder with their hand, and command them to extend their right hand upwards, and with their left hand, remove the skin covering the stones in the area where the cut is made; then use the spatula to completely remove it, forming as follows:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make an incision between what is between the cheeks and the foundation, not in the middle but on the side of the left navel; let it be straight on the stone, and your fingers should always rest on the foundation, and cut through so that it is wide enough to prevent sticking, but narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure from the finger resting on the foundation will cause it to come out easily; and know that there are stones with angles and margins: if they are stuck, they must be carefully removed; and if there is one beneath, similar to a spearhead or curve, whose passage is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If there are angles and margins in the stone, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, you should use pliers that are similar to a file at the tip, so as to extract the stone without letting it escape; or you can insert a thin curved instrument at the tip; and if you cannot do this, open the wound wider and, if necessary, pull with vitriole; and if there is more than one stone, first extract the largest one from the urethra, then cut, then pull it out, and afterwards the smaller ones.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, they should cut it out carefully, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things can happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine returns again through the wound that the muscles cannot close; but nevertheless, make every effort to extract it, either with tweezers or by scraping, as long as you treat it in pieces. And when you have completed your work, apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, tighten it, and place a moist cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then dress the patient's neck, and do not loosen the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, if a lot of warm oil and water arise from the joint, then apply healing ointment and basil-ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosion arise in the wound, and congealings of blood in the bladder, and retention of urine causes it to flow out with difficulty: then press your finger into the wound and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder and cause decay; then cleanse the wound with water and fire and heal it in every way you can, until it is healed; and it is necessary that during all treatments, you bind both thighs together and apply medicines to the joint.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in a urethral channel, and stuck together, and urine cannot pass; then if you treat it as I say, cutting it many times, that will excuse the cutting through this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tested it thusly.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take the iron at the front according to this form, and be sure it is inserted into three pieces of wood:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra away from the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then gently push the drill into the urethra until it reaches the stone, and turn the drill in your hand slowly against the stone from all sides until you can pierce the stone; soon urine will come out, and press your hand on what is remaining of the stone inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is sometimes broken and jumps out with urine, and the wound is infected; and if you cannot do this for any reason that hinders, then hold the stone from below and another from above, then make the stick into a lever against the stone between the two edges, then pull it out forcefully, loosen the bond, and clean the frozen blood in the wound; and cure it as long as it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of women's stone" (a common term for kidney stones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is rare that a stone occurs in women, and if it does occur, the cure is difficult, and it is hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; the second is that it is not possible to find a woman well-versed who knows how to uncover herself properly, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art of healing; and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman's body is more hard than that of the man, so it must be cut deeper, and great fear is involved. And if necessity calls for it, it is right to engage a midwife well-versed in this matter, and look carefully for one who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command regarding the examination of the stone; and pay much attention to whether that woman is a virgin. Then she must push her finger into the base and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she should force it down under her thumb and press her left hand on the swollen bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she feels it, she must move the stone gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to the root of the thigh; then cut into the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the cone, where it is moved and appears, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her leg above or below the stone, or make a small incision first. Then press the rat (probably referring to a lever or tool) against the wound until you feel the stone coming out as far as it can go, and know that there are many types of stones: small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know these similarities, you will know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If the wound does not heal, apply crushed vitriol and keep it for an hour until the wound is cleansed; then return to your task, as long as the stone remains firm, and have the tools I told you for removing stones from humans to assist you in your work; if the wound persists, and it's an arterial cut, sprinkle powder on the wound and press with tenes and belts, and don't repeat this, leaving the stone and not pulling it out, unless by chance the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the eyes opened, return to your task, as long as the stone remains firm.
de hernie carnouse	from herniated cartilage
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Rameous water is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white matter, which is detached from the heart of things, containing the soul; and it is called "white matter," and never properly part of the soul's fabric, if one considers that this is another thing; and it is the thin skin of the soul between the white matter we have mentioned; and this does not occur spontaneously.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this white matter is due to weakness, which affects the limbs, and that material is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never does it come from percussion on the joints, and this moisture takes many forms: it can be yellowish, or devoid of redness, or black, or white watery, and so on; and these are signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is white as we have said, then the abscesses are bright red, very long in shape like a serpent, and do not open the joints because they are filled with moisture.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	If there is moisture in the flesh itself, then the abscesses are bright red with a part of the effusion, and because of this, one thinks it is another infection; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white substance, it smells quite well; so when you want to know the color of the moisture, try to feel all over the affected area, as its shape has been described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after, judge of those who are inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to their ability and the replenishment of their body; then place them on their back, on something slightly elevated, and cover them with many sheets; then have them sit on their left side, and instruct the healer to sit at their right, and extend the staff to one of the two ribs near the heart of the chest; then take the scalpel, and cut the skin of the ribcage from the long end to the elbow, and make the incision completely straight by examining the skin of the ribcage until it reaches a satisfying white, and carefully remove the flesh according to the patient's ability; then punch the fabric plain with water at a wide opening, and extract all the water, and then apply your bandages, and pull the fabric upward; and do not touch the heart of the ribs, but only the fabric; cut around it carefully, subtly, than if you do not cut it cleanly, the water will return; and if the air escapes from your work, put it back in its place when you have completed the fabric work; then sew together the two books of the ribcage with a stitch, and treat it as other wounds, until they are healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the heart corrupted by another illness, it is necessary that you hold the vessels that are suspended, doubtful of the outflow of blood; then open the coccyx throughout the suspension, extract the heart, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the blood is collected in two parts, knowing that these are two branches, open the other part just as you did with the first, then drain the blood, and apply a clean moistened lint cloth with rose oil to the wound; and place another moistened linen cloth with wine and oil, and put the two coctions on top of it, and cover them with doubly-lined cloths, and bind it securely according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloth strips, and prepare them from woolen rags according to this form, and join them together by sewing in the groin of the trousers, one strip covering the thigh from the base up to the back, and the other on the palm side; then sew the third strip over both these, forming a loop at the back of the trousers. Never use this ramage (herbal preparation) as cautery in place of iron, but rather take a sharp cautery instrument, pierce through the skin, and burn it with this delicate cautery hot:

Cut it in any way you can, as long as everything is removed; be careful that the fire does not touch the egg (or other sensitive area), and know that this method is safer; move gently to avoid blood clots or complications from surgery; and if anything goes against you, whether it's an abscess or blood clot or another issue, treat what's going against you as described above.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its terribleness, then apply a perforation as I have said, and make certain by the signs that we have mentioned that ramice aquouse (a specific tool) is at hand; therefore, place the patient in a raised position, since the abscess is located beneath the skin, deep within the whole wound. Make the incision long through the body, and ensure the wound is wide enough for all the pus to drain. Then apply cotton to the wound and bind it, allowing the remaining pus to drain, then treat the wound until it heals; and if a clean cloth does not allow the pus to escape from the wound's opening, then insert a needle or the instrument used to treat water retention, as shown before. Open the wound wider and know that the pus will return and be collected after six months or so, and when it collects as before, in this way the patient's condition will improve each day.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the hairs
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Knowing that in this section there are various causes of great danger, it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone; and I will tell you the work and the signs of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say, therefore, that many abscesses come where there is hair; and most often in the hairs; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is known from the excessive acridity and fever that spreads to the hairs, or from percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the skin; it does not cause pain, and it is a serious abscess; and sometimes there are several abscesses that are hard, pale, dark in color, and never come from new arteries or veins.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is through no fault of an artery, if it is blocked by the arrangement of a hot abscess when you press on it with your hands; and it is not appropriate that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is afflicted by a swelling of the veins is blocked due to the arrangement of their expression when touched by the fingers, and can have an incision made in this similarity, and in other parts; and it is to remove the heart of the clots, then there is warmth at the top, and treat the pain strongly with white medicine, and release the suspension from all parts of the clot.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the clot is already solid with these means, then it is necessary that you treat and remove the clot; and if it is hard to the touch, or within the veins, it is necessary that you release all of this tension, and treat it thoroughly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the source of the pain is behind, it is necessary that you remove it entirely, and extract the foreign body, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is done, immediately apply a moist linen cloth with rose oil and wine to the wound, and then use other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the cowshed
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a similar covering like a borion, with the swelling of the glands, and it makes the patient suffer greatly; and the cure for this illness is as pressing and fearful as the one mentioned before, yet we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.

de la routure dou syfac	from the dislocation of the shoulder joint
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The cure for this condition is through incision or extension at the site of dislocation, allowing the intestines to descend from that rupture into one of the openings; and this dislocation occurs either in the shoulder joint or in the abdomen in the region of the angles, causing the intestines to move from that rupture to one of the openings. This dislocation results from either a blow, a jump, shouting, lifting a heavy weight, or similar actions; and its signs are as follows: it happens little by little over a long period, rather than suddenly, and the abscess is evenly distributed up to the very edge, since the dislocation pushes the intestines forward.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac. And the method of the procedure is that you command the patient to realign the intestine in his hand within the wound if he can; then gently hold it between your fingers and lift the thigh. Envolve the testicles with the thread and tie them together so that no vessel that nourishes them can enter, and the abscess does not come back; then make another ligature with the first long ligature, two threads from it, leaving one part of the white skin beneath the heart of the testicle as long as a finger. And after all this, do the rest according to the curvature that the testicle has; then cut the part below the thigh's skin until it is smooth and bow-shaped, as we have previously mentioned. Then apply moist wool to the wound and dress it, and use the ligature that we have described.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never should the white scar be cauterized, as we have said, after the incision, out of fear of further bloodletting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, leaving the wound open until it heals by itself; and if it takes time to heal, it can be helped with hot water, and we have said, as long as it needs; then treat the wound with another remedy, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia (fleshy protrusion)
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, never should anyone attempt to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients say that it is made like a rivet that joins together the bone, in such a way as you tie the vessels after cutting them slightly on the inside and then cure the abscess of him who opens, until the vessels stop bleeding; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No rupture should occur without opening the veins as we have said, and draining them; nor should any intestines be exposed, and if they are, it is a sign of danger, and repair must be done every hour; nevertheless, if it lingers too long at this stage, believing it to be a wound or abscess, until the intestines drain; and this happens due to the expansion of the syphac (abscess) which is located near the veins, as it expands then softens and opens the vein; and the cure for this, as we have previously said, is cautery, and never by iron in this manner: and thus, the patient should lie on his back with his hands beneath him, then cut the vein of the rupture with a sharp blade according to its width; remove the syphac located below the skin with the usual tool, then take the rake and place it over the exposed part of the syphac; press it firmly into the abdomen, then cut both parts of the syphac on top of the rake's handle, and stitch them closed; then remove the rake, and do not drain or expand the abscess in any way, as I have previously explained regarding the cure for intestinal ruptures; then treat it with wound dressing.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat the wounds, if they become contaminated and the wound heals, as long as it is clean.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The treatment is difficult, and it has no appearance in the fracture, but the cauterization moves on this side, and is closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the tough skin of the limbs
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often, the skin of the limbs is softened in no one person, because the muscles inside are relaxed, and it is easy to see. When one wishes to treat it, one must lay the patient on their back and cut the soft skin at the site of the muscle; then bring together the two edges with a single stitch or, more securely, three stitches; then cut between the stitches and treat the wound as other wounds, until it heals, and draw out the thread.
dou chastrement	This treatise" 
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You know that castration is outlawed in our law, and for that reason I would not speak of it in this book; however, there are two reasons why it is necessary: one is that you should be able to answer knowledgeably when asked about it, and provide the appropriate treatment; and the other is that we often need to castrate certain animals to aid us, such as goats, sheep, cats, and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say, therefore, that castration is done in two ways: either by pulling or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method where we pull, we should immerse the animal in hot water until the testicles are softened and relaxed; then with your hand, grasp them firmly as they return to their normal state and you no longer feel any sensation.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the operation of castration: You must restrain the animal and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspending string, and cut each testicle at the scrotum, when you have well sliced them; leave no drop of blood or the subtile blood that is on the vessels; and this method of castration differs from that which is done by attraction, because at attraction, by chance, something of the testicles may remain, causing the animal to desire lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphrodite is according to two manners in men: one such that between the two testicles appears also like the form of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and never shortens the urethra.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another way is for women; it has a protrusion on the wrist as well as two fingers.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for thirst and hunger is to remove all the adjusted characteristics, and heal it like other wounds; in the second way, for men whose urine jumps through the skin of the penis, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the goiter
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Goiter is an adjusted characteristic on the natural part, so severe it's unattractive; and no woman can bear it as much as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you hold the excess of the tendon in your hand or with pincers, and cut it lightly; do not cut too deeply, so that no further bleeding occurs, until the cure takes effect; and for another condition that appears at the opening of the wound, apply and use it, and perhaps it will fly out, and it resembles a cow, and for this reason they call it in old times "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you cut it, as we said about the tendon, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erroneous is the judgment when one does not correctly perceive the nature of women, or if the wound is small; it is either innate by birth or accidental due to illness that occurs; or it is caused by a tight fit, or some subtle or specific pain, and it happens in any part - front, side, back, or wherever; and it affects conception, childbirth, and perhaps even the flowers to be born; knowledge of these things comes from observing the signs.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the symptoms are soon apparent, whether to your touch or at a distance.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle pain and the symptoms are soon apparent, act quickly: place both your index fingers together, have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread apart; then form both hands into fists until the subtle pain disappears, and so the symptom vanishes. Then take wool, dampen it in oil, and place it over the affected area, having the woman rest on each side every day so she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if it is hard and rough, you must cut it with a scraper resembling a holly leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from heat, suspend it at the joint and cut it; have medicines that stop blood flow, such as elderberry, dragon's blood, incense, in abundance; then apply a wide bandage so that the wound cannot close; and thus keep it for a long time, and then apply a dry linen dressing; and continue other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when the swelling comes from cold, it must be covered in this manner; if it is an abscessed swelling, it must be treated accordingly.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that has worsened in the wound, one must not attempt to treat it with fire.
des emorroides	hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that, without proper care, can become chronic. In this division, we have previously discussed the similarities and signs, and I will now describe those that receive treatment.
