Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and their complications, when they are completely in the anus and do not cause pain, can only be treated properly with heat.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the sea, one can feel, are those who can heal.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then stretch her legs with pliers and cut into her roots, then sprinkle medicinal powders to stop blood, such as sage and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water. And when the bleeding stops, make a decoction of sumac and bark from pomegranates and gall and similar things, and then take flour and confit it with honey and herbs, and make an emplaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it becomes soaked, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If that does not work, apply cupping glasses on the back and around the mammary area without causing injury; then take linen and soak it in juice of plantain or hazelnut with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has subsided, keep the wound clean until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles an open wound, so it must be covered as I have said in the previous text; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	from the abscess of the mare's uterus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the mare's uterus, such as chancres, old abscesses, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, among others, as mentioned in the previous section.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I discuss in this treatment the hot abscess that occurs in the mare's uterus, which is not a true abscess but rather a swelling; and if you observe the effect of heat, consider whether the abscesses are red and hot at their onset, and full of feverish pus, and turn red, as you can see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but let the patient suffer until the pain is relieved; then place the ailing person in a reclining position, with two small pillows where he bends and leans on his back, gathering his feet towards the affected leg; spread his knees wide apart, placing his arms below his knees and binding them firmly with a good bandage. Then insert the blade on the right side, and use the instrument to open the wound, from which this shape will emerge. And it is important that when you insert the instrument, you first test the depth of the wound, so that what enters from the instrument does not go further than necessary, and does not harm the patient; if the instrument is too large, it should be covered with cloth to prevent it from causing pain, and the instrument itself should be placed on top.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens and one makes it with a gentle hand, if necessary cover the wound with a sponge or a piece of cloth dipped in rose oil or dry green oil; place the bandage deeply into the wound at the margin of the abscess, and put over the abscess and the surrounding joint a clean moistened lint soaked in boiled almond milk or chamomile; then treat after this for two days with ointment coming to pass, until it is healed; and never raise up the abscess or the wound by a cleansing enema of water and honey, nor of water and extracts of lily roots and long-soaked aristoloche; then return to treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the joint, it is necessary to avoid heating with iron, but treat it as we have said in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	From childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Skill is first in the dance, knowing the figure of natural childbirth, and its signs are when you see the woman struggling down, and she desires to smell the air: then hasten for the child to be born; then know that these children come according to nature, and are delivered head first, and secondarily with him; and when you see these signs, gently press her belly, so that the child is born soon; for when it descends on its head, it helps him deliver, and the mother gives birth to her superfluities through proper cleansing; and this one who comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes upon its feet, and strikes the body here or there, or the hands, or comes upon the belly or back, and turns by chance upon its neck, or takes other bad forms; so it is necessary that he who deals with it be wise and subtle in these matters, and guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the forms how he should help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the evil spirit comes upon his head through natural causes, and a woman gives birth badly, and her virtue is weak, then she should sit on a saddle, or women should hold her; and take out of the oil or fennel seed cooked, and then apply the ball between her two fingers, in the shape as mentioned below:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut through the second joint, and saw off his finger as far as the moisture that is stuck in it; and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, it is necessary to wash the woman with fennel seed mucilage mixed with sesame oil; then make her cough and sneeze from a position of comfort, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	If both hands are stuck out, it is necessary to reset them little by little; and if they still cannot enter, place the woman on a seat and raise her feet up; then remove the seat from the ground and have the woman lie down, so that she does not try to get up; and if her hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, cut off the hand at the joint that has been previously placed, extract the child, and reset it properly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes on its feet, it should be pushed upwards, and then pulled back little by little until it is even; then press on the feet and extend them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it can jump up to the ankles, under command press down, and make it sneeze from its condition; if it jumps further, God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not respond as we have said, pull back little by little until it is according to its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes slightly better.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not improve as we have said, take some musk, and oil of rose, and gum resin, and grind them all in a mortar; then apply this remedy to the woman's vagina both inside and out, and let her sit in warm water reaching down to her ribs; when she is moistened, put on a collar of myrrh and leave it for an hour. Then have her sit on a seat, and make her sneeze, and press her mouth and nose, and gently massage her abdomen, as the child will now come out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the birth of the child on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, he moves his hands little by little; then he sits up on his collarbone, and his feet hang down, and he lies on his side; and he bends his hands little by little, then takes hold of his hands on his stomach, and removes the cushions from beneath him, until he is completely relaxed downwards; and if the child does not cry, he takes his feet and moves them, then moves his stomach upwards, and turns his hands inside out; and gently handles the child little by little; and tells the woman to press herself as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the birth of the child who comes out with a large hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I know how to bring the hand back: if it cannot be brought back, one must raise the woman and let her rest; if she cannot stand, lay her down on her side and support her legs; then apply the musk as I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on a chair, then study how to bring the hand back; deliver the child according to its natural position, make it sneeze, and tell it to push until the baby comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on its mother's lap, with its hands spread and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I want the patient to hold his hand, then twist it little by little and gently; and when it is even, he should apply a light, muscly compress of wool and oil, as we have said, then instruct him that it move little by little; and when you have done this, let it rest on a pillow, and command it to press; and make the patient sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner, do all of the following:
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it progresses in this manner, if the seconding (unclear term) sticks to your finger, drain the moisture; and if it gets caught on its face or neck, cut it from the edge so it is not trapped, and let the child breathe; then place the baby inside, as you have learned it should be, and instruct the woman to sneeze several times. Then gently pull.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the origin of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Knowing that twins are born many times, and never three or four at once; this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	These are strange things, and they do not live, they have no name; I know that they are multiplied, and their fate is in the will of him who divides them, who is bound to the womb; and they never emerge as naturally as one single child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge painfully, as the cure has been said, and there are subtle joints, making the process slow and gentle, doing what is necessary for their safe delivery.
de plusors enfans	from many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	They are never formed in the womb I, II, III, IV, V, VI, VII or more up to XV, and they are all shaped like a child according to the measurement of its wise form, and it is necessary that the midwife knows all this, for by chance, something similar may happen; so do as is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure a woman who has suffered the death of a child in her womb, as I have said in the previous division, and there is no expulsion, and you are compelled to use manual force; it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound constitution and has no fear or concern over the death; she should be placed on her back, with her feet inclined downwards and legs raised. The midwife should apply a mixture of two parts, or keep her in bed so that she is not subjected to the downward pull of the child. Then, she should gently rub the woman's mouth with moist eye drops prepared from fennec and fenugreek seeds, and then anoint the perineum with these oils and eye drops. Then, she should apply gentle pressure, and if necessary, insert fingers at suitable angles so that the head of the child descends; place the finger in her vagina, either in her own orifice, or her labia, or mouth, or hard palate, or under her beard, or in her vulva, or near her anus, and press gently until the head is free. If the descent is complete, insert a finger and hold it there while she bears down with her middle finger; this will prevent any tearing. It is important that she grasps the finger with her right hand and places the index finger of her left hand between them, then applies gentle pressure with her entire hand, keeping it in place until the delivery is complete, and the vagina becomes empty. This is the shape of the finger:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find another joint, where you need it most, so that the extraction is even; and then they move equally from one side to the other to be able to dislocate, and this joint becomes sharpened to hold its position, as follows:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains stuck, apply no oil to any of its sides, but push it into that part, and pull the other part; and if nothing comes out, place this joint higher up on the limb, and do this until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward before the other and it cannot return due to tightness, you should wrap it with a drape until it completely straightens; then cut at the joint of the foot or the knee, and do the same for the other hand, and have both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and stuck in the birth canal, it is necessary to insert the spiny spatula between your fingers, and move the head, extracting the water; or you can use the instrument called 'almidach', from which the form comes with the tools of this chapter, and thus do the same for a child with a large natural head; then carefully pull the bones with pincers, and if the head emerges but the moisture remains in the canal, break it off piece by piece as you can; and if it is swollen in the abdomen or under the ribs, pierce it until the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the disease is in its feet, it has a light pull, and the direction towards the opening of the wound is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is in the belly or the bowels, it is necessary to pull it with the drape wrapped around the hand; and make an incision on the belly or the bowels, as much as the moisture that is there allows; and if the other members are broken and the feces remain, he should press his hand from the wound towards the mouth of the wound, and pull it out; then he can use a hook or a forceps to extract it; and if the mouth of the wound is constricted due to the heat of the abscess that has formed, it is not appropriate to work on it, but rather to apply moist and greasy substances; and apply poultices, and immerse in soft water that softens and moisturizes.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the dislocated joint is on his side, and you can put it back even, just as we have said for a living child; and if it cannot be moved, then treat it in parts, and leave nothing of the dislocation.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, apply what we have said for abscesses that come near the wound; and if bleeding occurs, it should be treated with cold water, and other remedies should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose stomach had been cut open and a child had been removed, then another was cut open on that same wound, and the other one was saved.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there comes a abscess in the cheek, and it swells so much that it opens, and begins to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called upon for treatment, and I thought for a long time, but could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong plaster, and an bone came out, and after a few days, others followed.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because this belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought this was a bone from a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and found a bone in my hand, as long as the woman was in the best condition; and the woman remained in that state for a long time, and then a little bow-shaped part of the bone emerged from its place; and I have never remembered this chapter being written except because, when a master encounters something strange, they know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the wife back to her place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of a press, with which books are bound; and at its turn to the second part, to the two threads.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle in their tightening, and made of ebony or box; the mouth should be wide enough, and the margin of the trees, one palm and a half long; and both sides of this same horn should have a firm adjustment, about half a palm long, or a little bit more; and this adjustment is inserted into the mare's mouth to open it when turning the horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling pliers; it will have two sides, as you can see, one palm long and two fingers wide. When opening the mare with all the instrument, make the woman lie down on her side, with her feet apart and legs open. Then adjust both sides firmly into the mare's mouth and hold the base of the instrument between her thighs; then operate your hand over the entire instrument, just as you did with the pliers, until the opening in the mare's mouth is wide enough for what she needs.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	The surgical instruments are all sorts and have many similarities; and when you have made them appear clear to the eye, then the work is done faster, and it requires greater skill for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disregard the instrument even if you have not made it clear, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second stage of labor is reached, if it is necessary to retain the child, you should instruct the patient to hold her breath and then force a sneeze, while holding her hands to her mouth and nose; and if she does this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If no, then take I a pot and make I an aperture or cover, and put therein herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as calament, rue, anis, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, should be cooked or boiled in water over fire; then place one end of the pot or aperture into the wound, and the other at its opening, and hold it until the vapors go inside the wound; then make the patient sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second treatment fails.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if after this treatment, the wound remains and is not healed, instruct the patient to moisten their left hand with sesame oil or alder mucilage, then place it in nature (the air or environment), and want a second treatment. And when they find it, press and stretch it little by little straightening, so that the wound does not open during extraction; but they should move it slightly to the right and left, and then extract it. It will come out and depart.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the wound is tightly closed, we have said the remedy of sneezing and herb fumigation; and if it does not respond to all that we have said, be careful not to follow these remedies; but it is necessary that he who has a wound in the mouth, ties it to the woman's thigh, then cleanses it with a four-ingredient ointment; after which it will heal and leave, but nevertheless, if it opens again, there will be a bad odor in the stomach and on the head, and the patient will become worse.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	It is therefore necessary to use appropriate fumigations: none of the ancients have tried fumigation with arugula and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one cauterizes the woman to prevent the flow of blood and the discharge is this one.
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it resembles a glass tube, and one places the narrow end naturally in the wound, while the wider end is held over the fire; and the smoke should rise from the charcoal until it is completely consumed, then another one is started.
de percier lou fondement	to drill into the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not had their foundation drilled, but instead have a weak spot covered by thin skin: therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to perceive this weak spot with her finger and not pierce it with anything sharp, and protect it so that she does not touch it; then she should apply a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not return, if you insert or perforate a plug of cotton, and leave it there for days, and it has to be removed when the wound wants to heal.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And this sudden stopping of the wound or abscess should never be allowed; it is necessary to cover this stoppage, whether it is cured as we have said with the plug of cotton.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from its origin
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that originate from below the fundament are larger and more serious than those that arise from above, or in the space between the two parts, if it is a fistula or several; and when this nodulation has been present for a long time, if it opens up, and still emits white, moist, or subtle pus, these fistulas do not heal; and they are known because there is discharge or flatulence when the patient evacuates, and sometimes they burst open.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the ulcers perforate to the bladder, and to half of the penis; and they reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the root of the cow (leg).
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus, you recognize the fistula that is not present (or open), and it is necessary to insert your index finger into the anus and push a thin needle made of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, and you insert a thin plug or a horsehair as far as you feel it in your hand, and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge of pus or wind as we have said, then know that it does not perforate; be quick to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or up to the urethra, if it bleeds while urinating and cannot be healed with medications.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is located near the hip joint, then the veins are close to the surface; if there is no curvature or sudden onset of pain around it, and it persists, neither medicine nor any ointment helps; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure but labor, and vanity on the part of ignorant people who try to treat them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case where it is not persistent and old, there is hope for healing with fire, as I have experienced, and the patient lies on their back between your hands; they bend their legs up to their hips, and their hips are inclined towards their belly; then draw a tent-like shape with an arrow, or a curve if there is curvature, as long as you know where the vein originates.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain throughout his body, it is necessary that you press your index finger into his palm, and then he will feel where the pulse is beating; whether you feel it between your thumb and forefinger or in your wrist, know that it is present; if not, it cannot be treated.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	Despite this, no one can be completely cured, but progress is possible; and the aid that is provided consists in applying a gentle cautery according to the extent of the fistula, as mentioned above; it should be done hot all around the fistula until it comes out at the base; and do this two or three times, until you know that these charred areas have healed, which resemble the quill of a bird's eye; then apply moist compresses until the wound is completely sealed, and then proceed with treatment using ointments that promote healing and close the wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is in this state, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this cannot be, then he cannot be cured; and if a thread enters between his fingers or the nail bed, and does not pierce through to the flesh, place a thick covering of wool or similar material between your two fingers and where you see the fissure near the covering; when the pain from the beginning of the fissure subsides, remove it before the thread, and then cauterize after, as much as possible towards the tip of the finger; and the thread will be released and healed. Then beware of those evil threads that seem like a bird's feather, and do not delay in treating them.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pain persists, and a cut occurs between you and the task, cauterize it with fire or strong medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cautery combines two beneficial things: namely, the burning of these prepared materials, and the drawing out of blood and moisture; then, for moist wounds, apply butter or crushed herbs until the heat softens the burnt skin; finally, treat the wound with hot compresses and dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it becomes healthy and does not relapse.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula appears all the way to the bottom of the foundation, and it is removed from the body, if you press down on its root or foundation, it will close up again.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tentation and between it is the web or the syph or the char, or it is about to pierce, unless there is no other way of hope and salvation, through one of the three means: you cauterize it as we have said, or cut it all the way to the bottom, or if you can gently pry it open and treat it as before; but be careful not to go too deep, so as not to remove the covering that holds the foundation, and let the healing happen without the patient's knowledge. Then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will heal, or you remove that covered part and clean it then, after cutting it away from the base, either with a tent or some other pointed instrument; then purify the wound, as best as you can; and try to prevent the fistula from returning in the area beyond the foundation. If it is a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are the fistulas made in this manner: and it is when you press the tent into the fistula, and it is on the side near the base of the skin above, if a piece of cloth is taken with a point at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And it is pressed into a twist with the thread, and press the tent along all the thread in the fistula as long as it is at the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is persistent at the base of the skin, then extract the thread from that opening, so you press your two foundations together; and handle the top with the thread, and join the two parts together, holding them close to each other, and leave it for one or two days; never loosen it, until the threads have healed completely which are between the two parts, and stop moving. Then treat the wound as long as it is sealed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, even if you try to open it in every way possible, it will not be too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For if the opening is not deep enough and then you try to heal it before it heals properly, as we have said, it will not be healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form is a sharp, spiky one from which the fistula is made, if it is thick and solid on one side and hollow on the other; on no account should you try to open what you should not open, as you can see.
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids exist in two ways: either they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, with small and large ones, and oozing blood, or they protrude from it, singly or in clusters, and are inflamed at the base; but those that protrude have little moisture, sometimes a bit of clear water or blood, and have a skin color. For the treatment of hemorrhoids located inside the anus, you should order the patient to lay on his side until the anus heals and the children are born; if in a hurry, use tweezers or your fingernail to remove them, then cut them at their roots. If they cannot be held due to their moisture, grab them with cloth, cotton, or a piece of chamois, and extract them gently. Then cut them and apply hot powder over them as described in the cautery chapter, or cauterize them, after which treat them with other remedies until they are healed; if the anus cannot be opened, use a strong enema to wash what is inside, so it can come out easily. As for the pain of the patient and the size of the children, this treatment is light. You can pinch them with your fingernail or tweezers and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they heal, avoiding surgical incisions with a hot iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary for you to administer the stitch in this manner: take a twisted thread, and wrap it around an needle, then draw the thread from above and pierce the needle from below, and pass both ends of the thread through the needle, and if it is too thick, tighten the thread well, then tie it off, and extract the needle, and do so for all the others, leaving one for drawing out the excess blood; then apply a damp cloth or wax to the base, and place it there, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until the stitches fall out, and when they have fallen out, treat the wound with care or other remedies, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Carefully and slowly prepare the causes or foundations.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often, there is a drying up of causes in the intestine, due to restrictions of nature, and when the illness is old and no medicine avails.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you scrape off the crust with a spatula or your fingernail, which will not let it moisten; then treat it as it should be until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, continue shaving more forcefully than before, until it is moist and cut; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	He shudders.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Mice are small, hairy creatures that move just beneath the skin, and they go in deep; neither fire nor any other treatment can stop them, and their movement feels like a tremor, affecting the entire body, especially the hands more than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a thin piece of a duck's feather or a strong vulture's feather, and place this feather on the tremor until it engulfs the tremor completely; then turn your hand over the entire feather until you envelop all around the tremor, and reset it in its place, eliminating the tremor from its source.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make this of a snake's or iron wire according to this form, and be subtle from below and draw upwards.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not cut, so as to hold the two together, and press. And if you see, cauterize the tremor, as it is in front or at the beginning of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a douche
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never use a clister of silver or gold, or melted iron or wire; nor ever these small and large instruments according to those by whom they are used.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	He who thus administers treatment to children and those who are weak and afflicted, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the enema is small and wide at the top, or the abdomen is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and I say that when the abdomen is bound in this manner, as you see, and the stool is contained inside, it has one opening on one side and another on the other. The abdomen should be filled with medicinal liquid from a bladder of an animal or parchment, and all around these openings there should be small spaces, separated by one thread, then tightly wound into these openings a thin, twisted thread in X or any other pattern, and assemble the abdomen as if it were a bell. And when the medicine is inside, fasten the instrument with a strong thread at its front end, and perform the enema; this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and apply a warm compress of oil or egg white, or something similar, then gently squeeze it out; then the attending practitioner should massage both hands together until the entire body is relaxed, then remove the compress, and have the patient rest his legs against the wall, and let the medicine come out as much as possible; if he sleeps soundly through the night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the enema for a bloating disease of the belly and the medicine comes out quickly, it should be repeated until it is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoid is at the anus or abscess, it should be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the very subtle clamp to hold the skin tightly.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the use of stone, and sword or knife, or lance or spear or arrow, or similar objects; or they are made according to the laws of the body, such as a wound that breaks through the collarbone, or head, or side, or stomach, or liver, and similar parts; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is caused by stone or similar objects, and the skin is nonetheless torn and the wound is deep, and you doubt there is an abscess: do this as soon as possible to heal the cephalica, especially if little blood comes from the wound, and treat it on the contrary of the affected part; and let the patient avoid fullness of wine and heavy meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to be healed, let his flesh be reduced and he should not drink wine or eat meat; and apply a poultice of rose oil alone, or of astringent wine; and if there is a hot abscess, place it on the wound while it is still fresh with all its blood, and do not let air, powder - which I will speak of later - touch it, as long as it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword's width and similar, and the edges cannot be brought together, then bring them together with stitching, as I will say of abdominal wounds, by suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed through bone, and is deep, but only holds for a short time, then dress it with medicine, and replace the skin with hard wood, and instruct the patient to eat hearty meats, such as beef, cooked wheat, also poultry, and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrefaction in flesh or leather that has not reached the bone, and it consumes all the putridity, then dress it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, from which nothing stops, and medicines cannot stop it, then cut the artery, and if you dislocate it, bind it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: it is that you apply this powder that seals so as to move the fire.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The method for the powder is as follows: take one part frankincense, two parts dragon's blood, and three parts quicklime, mix the powder finely, apply it to the wound, and tighten it until it disperses well and joins with all its moisture; then tie it securely and leave it unbound unless it swells. For the medicine is not removed as long as it remains healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never should one use quicklime only, unless one has frankincense or dragon's blood; but the fire must have moved the wound first.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved the wound, especially if there is no powder applied; but put on some boiled herbs, or a paste of barley flour made with water and honey, until it flows; then apply other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture occurs with the wound and it is small, then extract it with delicate pincers; and I will tell you below about the fractures of the skull.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is simple, then it has no distinction from that at the top, but if there is damage within the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is an artery, then there is no other remedy but to allow the healing and not put anything restrictive, as it hurts the artery and causes it to retract; do not apply any sharp objects to the wound, because the substance of the artery is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member. But use medicine as if washing with cool water mixed with rose oil, and clean bandages also in cool water, and other stones according to this method, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, cutting through skin and muscles, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and wide, filled with pus, pierce them to the bone or below; and if an artery is cut, and blood flows, treat it with discretion, cauterizing if necessary; and if the spine in the throat is cut, or the juices, guard the passage so that the flesh does not stick to the bone in the throat, but remove it according to its natural form; then apply a tight bandage and do not release it for several days, applying poultices until healed. And if the wound has pressed into the bone, treat it as needed. If there are pieces of bone that cannot be removed, let them stay until the wound festered, becoming drained and lighter; and if the wound is fresh, apply the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones or a fistula in the wound, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and deep, pay attention to the signs of the patient's condition: if they are conscious alone, then know that the wound is mortal; but if it is not very deep, and still has fresh blood flow, do not apply any medicine in the first hour, nor bandage it tightly so as not to delay its healing. Instead, apply an attractive dressing and change it twice a day; and if you have no dressing, put old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three or four days, or more. If there is no spasm, no tremor, or no other distress, then know that the wound is healing well.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the wounds with various remedies and others, as long as they are clean; and if they cannot heal, know that there is a fistula; then treat it as appropriate.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is shallow or deep in front, or back, treat it as described above; if it is large, use stitches; and if small, apply powder, and if it affects the bone and has pieces of bone, clean the wound thoroughly, and remove foreign objects if necessary; and if they are not removed, let the wound heal, and the extraction will be easier. And for other wounds in other limbs, judgment should be made as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	disruption of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The disruption of the belly is great and medium and small; from a large wound, the intestines or the nerves of the intestines leak out, causing an opening; and stitching is more difficult, and never worth less than a small wound compared to a large one, because one must handle the intestines delicately, pulling them up and down; for they tend to swell soon after, making it seem like there is pain, so one must be careful not to pull them too tightly, and because the smaller wound allows for more delicate handling of the intestines compared to others. And know that the rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: common stitches in the stomach's stitching, and the stitching of other wounds on the body, and other specific stitches are common to other wounds; yet they are still more suitable for stomach stitching, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the bowels is affected, and it is a difficult thing to repair, then this is by one of two methods: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the cause.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in the following manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth with hot water only slightly, or boil water with cinnamon and cloves and pepper, and straighten the intestines as soon as the swelling is gone; never use wine that constricts, and it will be moved so as to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is filled with water or some other fluid and the hemorrhoids are cooked, because by this means the entry becomes easier for a short time; and if it cannot enter, they make a small incision with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to move the stool, that we should not cut it without great need; and this is the instrument to split: slice inside the pile and turn it away, and see the shape like this.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound has enlarged and the intestine protrudes, if you can return it to its natural position in its proper place, do so if you have the ability, for this is beneficial.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and located in the lower part of the belly, it is necessary to make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen, put the head and anus higher than the other parts, and also ensure that the rupture in the abdomen is in one of the two parts so that the injured area is higher than the other; thus it is appropriate to apply what I have said to both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, prepare a gentle medicated liquid to cover the entire wound with your fingers and gather the edges; this is the common method of stitching. Sew an agle or more, according to the size of the wound, leaving a small gap at the top of the wound; then insert a strong thread through a needle and sew from behind the skin down to the wound, gathering the two edges together; this forms four stitches that meet at the top. Then tie a double thread around the needle on both sides, gathering the edges of the wound properly, leaving small gaps, and inserting another needle; repeat this process until the entire wound is secured. The needles should be medium-sized, neither too fine nor too thick, as thin needles can pierce through the flesh and open the wound before sealing it, while too thick ones cannot penetrate sufficiently. Therefore, they should be medium-sized; do not pull the needles too far from the flesh and skin, otherwise they may cause discomfort to the patient when sleeping. Place tents or sheets at the sides of the needles to keep them in place until the wound is healed.
