This stitching method is more suitable for small wounds as it only requires one or two stitches; for larger wounds, you gather the edges with a needle and strong thread, making a single stitch across the entire width. I sewed a wound on a man's belly who had been stabbed by a knife; the wound was over a palm in size and extended several palms from the intestines.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its proper place after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed completely within fifteen days, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they marveled that he did not die, and it was a miracle; I did not cure him with any treatment, for I was in a place where none could be found, neither medicines nor anything else. I put clean cotton on the wound twice a day and washed it with honey-water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and thread it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced through the flesh, bring the edge together with the needle or stitch where you have threaded it, and then pierce from the other side, going from the outside to the inside; the understanding of this stitching is that you sew as a pelter sews fur, leaving one edge unsewn on each side until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second stitching method, which Galen properly calls, is like a way that no one does, which joins the two parts together naturally, and applies one of the ends with pleasure to the other end, in this manner: take a needle or an end of thread close by, and pierce it only into the surface, leaving the two ends of the thread; then turn the needle and pierce it from the opposite part inside as far as the two ends of the thread; then pierce one and the other from the opposite part inside to the other side, in the two other ends of the thread that are on each other's sides; and this is the moving stitching method and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen calls this method "sewing the belly with two needles," where each needle has thread, and one needle is passed from one side and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and know that when the rupture is within the belly, the stitching is more difficult than for other abdominal injuries.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you cut into a fresh wound until all its blood flows out, if the flesh moves, then cauterize and bind it tightly; apply the healing powder, and if the flesh moves again, apply some immediate treatment, as long as the wound remains open; then sew it up, and let the bandage, mirra, and balsam heal it, just like other wounds until it is healed; and if you have no medicine, immediately place a piece of old cotton and move it back and forth during the day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you need no other medicine in addition to these remedies for simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound is spreading to the principal members (of the body), then it is necessary to moisten a light linen cloth with warm temper oil, or rose oil, and place it around the affected area, under the armpits; and if it feels painful or putrid in waves, and this happens often, then give it enemas of warm red wine, especially if the putridity reaches the intestines. If it is the large intestine, healing will be easier than for the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestinal organ, called "young" (or "jeun"), cannot heal when it is weary, and this is due to the weakness of the veins, and the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the fat (or flesh) jumps out of the wound, push it back as far as the intestine while it is still fresh; if it has become old and turned white or black, then you must tie the black part to prevent blood from coming, for it contains veins and arteries; then cut away the tissue in between, and hang the two pieces down on either side of the wound until the fat falls out, thereby facilitating its removal.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it cannot be cured in any man, as I have seen a nobleman pierced through his bowels or stomach; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, it became inflamed and formed a fistula, from which came evacuations and flatulence; I applied treatment according to my ability, and did not cease to apply remedies until he was healed and the bowels healed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him healed, I doubted that the patient would not have pain in his stomach; but he felt no pain, only improved conditions, diet and drink; and certain practitioners said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be treated in this manner: take a large bandage, then pull together the edges of the wound, and when the bandage has opened its mouth, place it over both lips, so as to draw his mouth together; then cut off the top of the bandage, and this will hold until he is completely healed; then apply another bandage in the same manner, until the wound is fully closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the sharp end of an intestine penetrates the body and causes no harm to the patient, it is possible to sew it up with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal: take the sharp end of this intestinal thread, which is well cleaned, and then tie it to the tip of a fine flaxen thread twisted, then wrap the thread around the needle, and stitch the intestine, and arrange it in the wound; this method of sewing is not inferior in effectiveness, provided that it follows the path of reason and hope. If the wound is deep and wide, especially when it involves one of the major intestines, no one can heal it except with great subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula, regardless of its location.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Every wound or abscess, when it opens, is generally called a "fistula", especially when it is chewed and hollowed.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula, according to the truth of its formation, is hard and white, causing no pain, and just like the feather of a bird; sometimes it is clear and thin, other times thick and pastey; sometimes sour, other times sweet; and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds: every wound that is not healed, and there is no discharge, is due to one of the nine causes. These are: the lightness or hardness of blood or pus; its evil nature; the presence of hard matter within it, preventing the formation of discharge; excessive secretion; the bad state of the veins or their closure; the quality of the material being of poor quality; improper medication; corruption indicative of a plague; delayed digestion and late absorption in the region due to natural properties; or the existence of veins or bones. I have already explained all these causes, their symptoms, and the cures for them in detail.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I make you know the treatment of a fistula which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistules that affect major veins, arteries, and nerves, or the bladder, intestine, or kidney, or any of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joint in the hands or feet, and they can be as large as these structures.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas of this type are difficult to heal and require hard work and knowledge. If there is a fistula that does not come to the surface as I have described, but you are confident in the cure, take a thin piece of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, use it; if it is crooked, seek a subtle piece of pliers, for the pliers will bend around the curvature. If the fistula has an opening in the hand and you cannot reach it properly with pliers, wash it with one of the openings, as moisture travels from one opening to another and cleanses it; then cut it cleanly in your power, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and whether it is completely removed, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press your hand on it and the location where he feels it. When you have accurately determined the location, and if it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, or vein, or any of the openings I mentioned, cut it as I instructed, and remove all debris and corrupt tissue inside; then heal it as sanely as possible. If the fistula is very deep and straight, cut it completely through as best you can; then apply moistened medicine-soaked lint around it until the medicine corrodes any excess that remains at the bottom; then put clean, healthy bandages on it until it heals; and if this does not work, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not affect your primary member as we have said, and if the bone is exposed, with corruption and blackening, wait until all corruption is removed, then treat any remaining issues thoroughly until it is healed; and if it is not healed and bows again as before, know that you are not yet safe: expose and cleanse it as much as possible, remove all corruption, then restore it to its place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If no, know that the corruption is too extensive, and you cannot restore it; if there is no other cause but to let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupt bone, and you can extract it with suitable pliers, then remove all the bones, leaving none; and if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cauterize and dry, and relieve the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put something corruptive on the wound, and let it fester until the pus has drained out among the bones, and then the bones will become lighter; and if it is a large bone, like that of the leg or thigh, scrape off the corruption as much as possible until all the blackness is gone, then close the wound; and if there is a great deal of corrupt matter, and it extends almost to the bone; it must be kept clean and covered up until the corruption has completely healed, and then treat it until it is firmly healed. And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take an example from it and provide aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around XXX years old who had a pain in his leg due to something that arose inside the body, causing the materials to reach the leg, and it was infected with a large abscess, and there was no clear cause for opening; but because of their folly, they pricked the abscess so much that many things were drained, and it became a fistula, and there were numerous openings that let bowels and moisture out of the body; and many treatments were attempted for two years, without any wise person in the art of medicine, until I was called to see him, and I observed his leg and the medicines used to cure it, and what was corroded by the openings in the large body; and the skin of the young man turned red, and had a citrine-like color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these gaps, and then I examined all the gaps, and I found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	Then I quickly acted and cut into one of the gaps until I discovered a portion of the bone, which was corrupted and broken, and the corruption extended inward to the bone; I understood what appeared to be the corrupt bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except that which I had left; and I began to treat the wound with medicines for a long time, but they could not unite. Then I re-examined it and discovered the bone as before, and found that the corruption continued in the bone, so I treated it and then secured it, but I could not press it together until I had removed a palm-sized piece of the bone, and brought it back to its natural shape; then I treated it again with medicines. And it was healed and united firmly, and did not want to begin the operation again except for the weakness of the patient who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because for the complete evacuation of blood, it often happens, but it was healed entirely, and a hard scar remained in place of the bone, and was of good disposition, causing no harm or contrary effect at all, neither to leaving nor entering.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be handled in this manner: take a rope, and stretch it across the opening of the bone, and instruct anyone to pull it upwards; then tie another thicker rope of linen over the first one, and fasten it to the flesh that is now separated from the bone, pulling the flesh downwards, so that you dislocate the corrupt flesh from the bone, and expose the flesh beneath where you saw the break. Put coals or a plank underneath the bone to cover the corrupt flesh; and be as careful as possible, as you must see and feel the corruption, and do this again if necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if a bone is corrupted and will not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then expose the whole body; then apply heat from one side to the other of the corruption, and make it firm for a long time as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut out the corrupt joint, and make the bone strong on the other side; and if the corruption is in the connection between two joints, do not cut anything else but that which contains the corruption; and if the corrosion is at the wrist of the hand or the ankle of the foot, it is very difficult, but you should investigate how it opens, and purify it in every way that does not harm the vein or nerve; and know that there are many instruments for cutting and binding bones, according to their position and appearance, their thickness and thinness, their size and hardness, and therefore it is necessary to match each work with its appropriate instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument needed, according to the knowledge of this art and the signs of the ways of illness; choose the instrument that suits you best.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joint dislocates internally or externally; and when you have medicated that corruption with the cure of medicines, but they do not help, it is necessary to cover that limb until the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes from death, or from evil, which is greater, through the fault of the limb; and the sign of this is that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackening, since that corruption goes from member to member and takes hold throughout the body; then hurry to cover it, and if it is due to the bite of some venomous creature, such as a sea scorpion or a snake or similar, immediately dislocate it, and do not give it time to come to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, so that the bone affects the joint, preventing corrosion from reaching the arm; and if it comes to the arm, then cut at the elbow; and if it passes through the elbow, it is death, and there is no cure outside of its quantity of strength; and thus does corrosion affect every part: if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, then cut through the entire foot; and if it rises to the leg, then cut at the joint above the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or binding the member is as follows: bind it from above and below, and extend one assistant with each tie, and you sever the flesh that is between the two ties with a wide spatula, until the bone is exposed; then cut or bind it, and place a linen drape on each side so that the linen does not touch the healthy part, and cause further injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the flow of blood occurs when you open it, cauterize the vein properly and do not apply any restrictive powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, bind the affected limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you that which happened to a man in great pain: he had a blackening which seemed to be burnt by fire, and that corruption appeared first on his right foot, until it discolored the whole foot; and when the man saw the corruption, he covered his foot, and it was healed; but a long time later, the corruption returned on his left hand, and came to me, and I applied reflective substances after purification of the body, and the corrosion would not stop; and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to do so, as I had hope of reflecting the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, since the man's virtue was weak; and he became completely desperate, returned to his land, covered his hand, and it was healed; and I have never heard of such a case except for when one does otherwise, if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No abscess ever forms in a fresh wound, and it lingers so long that it causes great tension within; then it bursts and pierces the bowels, and remains until the vital force is exhausted, just like a vessel; and the skin covering it is as delicate as fine cloth, and doesn't extend to the bone or nerve, and this condition is called "sain," not "fistule." But if it spreads so far that it reaches the bone entirely, it is called a "fistule"; and the skin should be cut all around, especially when it is delicate, just like fine cloth; and its corruption is not easily recognized.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you believe that the skin is infected and the corruption is not completely healed, and the skin is dry and brittle, then treat it with a cleansing enema: check if the breast is swollen and the wound emits a bad odor, then give an Egyptian medicine made thus: take equal parts of salt, oil, and lithargy, and place them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey. Then take as much as needed and mix it with water and honey, and use it to enemize the breast, squeezing out the discharge; leave the medicine for two hours, then extract it while straining; do this several times until the breast is clean and the pus is gone. If the patient cannot endure either the Egyptian medicine or the water from ashes when that medicine is not available, crush ashes from vine wood, pour water over them, strain it, and use it in the enema; continue until you are sure that the breast is thoroughly cleansed. And if the patient cannot tolerate this, give an enema of honey and wine, with a little bit of powdered lithargy, as honey has purifying and cleansing properties, while wine helps to aerate the wound; when you have done this and believe the breast is clean, then give an enema using whatever causes the breath to become sweet, whether it be incense or some other medicament; and if the opening in the breast is too small for the enema needle, enlarge it slightly with a hot iron and apply the Egyptian ointment or basilicon until it is wide enough; and if the wound is very large, cutting it will not leave enough space for the enema to enter, and if the discharge flows downwards, place the enema higher than or lower than that point.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Because when the bowel is in perfect condition, it does not allow itself to be interrupted; and if you cannot cover the opening of the wound as well as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bowel moves to the lowest level it can, because when the bowel is perfectly healthy, it does not allow itself to be interrupted, and if you cannot cover the opening of the wound as well as you see fit, arrange it so that the bowel moves slightly downward, leaving no part of the bowel exposed; and take consolidative medicines to apply over the wound, and place them under a linen drape that covers the entire wound; then press with force around the opening in the side of the wound, making it slightly larger than before; apply gentle dressing according to the size of the wound, and place it over the opening in the healthy tissue to lighten the pressure from the bowel, and do not remove the large linen drape for several days; and whoever is over the opening in the side of the wound often removes it to relieve the pressure from the bowel, and knows what comes from the bowel—whether it's poison or a bit or enough, or digested or undigested—and be careful if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and how your medicine has spread in this way, and you see the nature that springs up on the opening of the wound, then know that healing is already beginning; and then release it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the dressing, and renew the treatment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast becomes bowed and indigest after many days, knowing that it will not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons appear after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are some who have late discharges of pus from their wounds, and others do the opposite; and if the breast becomes bowed and indigest after many days, knowing that it will not open; and if the breast remains closed for a long time, and is far away, then apply moist medicines with a subtle substance and dry in virtue, as a definitive cure, because there is a great part of vitriol, which is the last medicine; take the definitive cure, and make it with rose oil, and mix it with old wine in substance; then preserve it and use it; and do the same with cooked honey thickened, when definitive ointments are not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and crush them, and powder them on honey while it is still warm from the fire; and then spread it on the breast, and never administer in large doses, nor roots of celestial lis, which is also like wheat flour and centaury; and use simple or composite ones: grind them, and make a powder, and put it on the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the cure takes a long time, and this cure does not heal, then know that corruption is in full force, and makes an impression on the bone, or hard members, or ligaments; as we have said before for the treatment of fistulas.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Gangrene is an abscess that forms under the nail in the hand or foot, or occasionally in other parts; and when it becomes old and one does not take care, it develops a gangrenous abscess, causing pain and discharge as it eats away at the root of the nail, and possibly even the entire nail. It leads to corrosion down to the bone, producing a putrid odor, and the nail bed becomes swollen and red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the previous section, but the treatment is not effective, then you must remove all debris remaining under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is of great aid if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound; and if the nail pricks the flesh, and begins to puncture, and the wound bleeds, it is necessary that you place the edge under the nail that punctures the flesh, and lift it up, and gently and lightly cut off the flesh, and apply burning and corrosive medicines to remove all of it; then treat the wound with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and pull it away, for as much as the bone decays, it cannot heal; and if you see both bones corrupted, remove them as mentioned above, then treat it until it is healed; and if it is heated and swollen, and causes great pain, it is necessary that you dress it first; then cut the nail with a sharp scissor diagonally from above, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, apply something soothing.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of a severe wound should be soothed by the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The adjustment that is born in the hands of no one by chance is entirely fleshy, and perhaps has part or all of its bones, and never has a claw, and neither does it emerge at the root of the joint, where birth is not within our control.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	What is born in no place has no movement, and what is born at the joint of a limb might not move; the shape of that which is fleshy should be light, in this manner: size it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: if you keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In him who is born or has an injury elsewhere, it is necessary that you first cover the wound thoroughly to the bone, then cover the bone with a suitable cloth, and then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The deformities that come at any age come either from birth, or from the union of wounds, or from burns by fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you need to tighten that suture, so it must be repaired according to their natural shapes; then place between two moistened cloth or drapes in rose oil, so they do not stick together; or put between two pieces of fine leather, as long as the skin is sewn, as appropriate.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If dislocation occurs in any of its fingers with the palm, tighten the suture as appropriate.
des vils	Des vils" translates directly from Old French
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	They are veins thickly enveloped, full of melancholic excesses, which come to many members of the body; and more so in the legs of those who walk, work, and bear weight, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary for you to administer purgative once, and then cleanse the basil (or abdomen).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of fire is according to two methods: one is with cauterization and extraction of the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and drain it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The operation is carried out according to this method: first, raise the affected limb with hot water until the swelling subsides, then extract the sick limb from above the ankle to the knee joint; next, cut the vein in one, two, or three places with a broad knife, then squeeze and drain the black blood into your hand from one end to the other, as much as the patient can bear; then bind it and order him to immerse the affected part in water, causing the formation of dark flesh; and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, until harm to the patient ceases.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	They should raise the affected limb, remove any hair, and immerse it in hot water until it turns red and swells; then heat it over a fire if there is no bath. Afterwards, apply pressure to the vein from above the knee joint or the part below the ankle, opening the skin at both ends as you feel it pulse; it will appear red and black, and like a white string when exposed. Then pull gently on it from below, until it detaches from the skin, and repeat the same process with another pin, as before. Apply more pressure if needed, then lift it slightly and apply a fresh pin at a different point, just as you did previously; then pull and lift again, moving to a third pin, then remove the skin gently, and apply a fresh one on the second pin, and so on, removing and applying new pins until the entire vein is removed. If it cannot be pulled out, insert a strong needle through its entire length, and draw and twist it back and forth; also pull from below with a finger and remove the needle when there is nothing left to draw. Be careful not to sever it, for if it breaks, it cannot be pulled or removed, and will cause harm to the patient. Once removed, place a moist, soft cloth over the wound, using wine and rose oil, and tend to it until healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if you see that it is contracted and twisted and rolled up together, and it is not straight at all, as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cover it; treat it as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The way to treat it if the vision is crooked and does not straighten, without cutting the vein, but only compressing it; it is of great curvature, because if it were delicate, it would cut the vein, but since it is thick, as we have said, then this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and on land where there is no moisture; and sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to putrefaction that comes from below the skin, as it winds and coils within the body.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein appear, it is that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to protrude forcefully, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, it is necessary to wrap a piece of cloth around it, from one and a half fingers up to two fingers wide, and leave it on the leg; every time that it appears at the surface, you should wrap it again around the flesh, and remove any excess; and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the rest back, but do not cover its root until it is completely out. For if you cut it, it will retract into the flesh and cause an abscess and putrefaction, or some other malady. Therefore, it is necessary to treat it little by little, up to the point where no trace remains in the body; and this vein appears as long as five palms, or even more; and when you cut it, it leaves one or two openings, and perforates to the bottom, allowing everything to come out; and you should empty the matter that is inside, and apply medicine to the wound that prevents putrefaction for as long as needed, just like with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never should one touch this vein again, especially when it opens at the foot or leg joint, or where there is much tearing and bleeding; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that emerge between leather and skin.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "beef disease" in our land because it often affects cattle, and it is characterized by the emergence of small worms between leather and skin. They travel throughout the body, ascending and descending, causing great pain from one limb to another, until they break through the skin where they were embedded, and they exude a strong odor; this disease is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, just as worms, serpents, and lice do in the belly; and its malignancy is doubted because when it spreads throughout the body, it rises to the head, reaches the eye, sometimes retracts, and destroys the eye; and this occurs many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it healing and draining, it cannot be done faster than it goes: therefore, you must lie the limb above and below with a strong, tightly bound bandage, then cut and drain it, and if the wound is deep in the flesh, do not remove the bandage until it has healed; and the greatest harm it does is when it causes bleeding, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the oil, tighten the sorcil (fist) below, then cut and drain it; and it is necessary for the patient to use purification of the body with solvent medicines to remove bad humors, and to wash with foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain that comes from flatulence.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in no particular member, but can move from one member to another; and I have seen this as I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and after that, I noticed something rising on her shoulder, brighter than anything else, like bright silver when it cuts through flesh; the pain left that spot and moved to her shoulder, and then, shortly afterwards, spread throughout her body, reaching the other arm; then she told me that she felt it returning around the body, as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled greatly at how she moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had observed that many experience great pain when moving from one place to another, but I had never seen it in a woman; and I thought it was due to her dry skin, exposed veins, and this constrained windiness; and I did not find this to be the case with those who are delighted, and have moist skin and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease heal, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, press down hard from above and below until that constrained windiness in the place subsides; then cauterize the place; and if you do not have these at hand, cure it with those who relieve windiness, such as foul pills, snake venom pills, and others like them.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows vary, according to their appearance and according to the parts of the body from which they come.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Their diversity is such that there are those with large and small tips, those with barbs, and those without; some have two points, others have lengths, and some have pieces. They can pierce any member in two ways: either in a principal member, like the head, body, liver, kidney, intestine, bladder, or similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it breaks in any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appears: it is necessary that you struggle with the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after various dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not fully extracted, pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow breaks and pierces the bone, and there is a sudden sensation in the head, as if it were hitting, and blackness and darkness and turning in upon itself, and redness of the tongue, and spasms, and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps the arrow comes out through the nose or ears; and sometimes it loses the ability to speak and sing; and there is also a white moist discharge from the wound, like pus, and sometimes it smells bad like horse urine; and if these signs appear to you, take care, and extract the arrow even if it's not fully embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of an arrow when it pierces or enters the body is that it is close to the left breast and feels as if it were embedded in something hard, neither empty nor hollow; and by chance, the arrow may become silent like the pulse, and produce black blood, coldness, and cold sweat, and even fainting. Therefore, be certain of death.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never revives is that no foam comes from the wound, the throat swells, the patient's face turns pale, and he breathes heavily and stops moving.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow breaks off in the deepest part of the flesh, it leaves small bones shattered; it causes great pain and breathing difficulties and heavy sighing, and all the muscles around the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow pierces the stomach, perhaps something from the indigestible flesh jumps out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces the belly, and there is no trace of good through the intestines, then there is little hope for treatment or for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces the bladder, and urine jumps and flows out, and the patient feels intense pain, know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, as they feel and the pain in the throat, shoulder, and back, along with the stiffness in the joints and the legs, and the dislocated limb, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you should do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	There once happened to me a case of an arrow that entered the ear or cheek root: I tried it, and pulled it from the other side, through the fat of the ear, and it was completely healed without any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And once, in a game, an arrow entered the fat of the neck below the skin and below the paper, and the arrow was lodged, and it only left the tip towards the wood, and it was a large arrow with a blue bow, without causing any pain; the wound healed, and no bad accidents happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And take an arrow from the throat of a Christian, which was an arrow with ears: I cut the barbs, and pulled as I took it, and healed the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I extracted an arrow from a man, which had penetrated his chest and abdomen, and thought he was dying; but after thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut the arrow, and removed it, and there were no adverse effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	If you wish to treat a man who has an arrow lodged in his back or chest, and the wound is deep, let the arrow remain within him, and do not alter his natural conditions; nor will you find any harm from any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man to whom an arrow fell in his face and the wound became deep; he remained thus unable to suffer great pain; and many others like him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated a prince, the king himself, who had an arrow in his neck that was slightly inclined to the right side, and the arrow was completely embedded; I was called for treatment after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very deep.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it gently all around, and I felt nothing; but he experienced a sharp sensation and pain from behind his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I placed a soothing poultice on the joint because the joints were not swollen; and then I saw the arrows in the joint.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the poultice on for several days, and thus healed the wound; then the patient endured the arrow inside his body for a long time, until he felt it in his flesh; and so he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it healed, and then I probed it; I felt the tip of the arrow stuck in the joint; so I adjusted the opening of the wound using that medicine until the part of the arrow became visible; it took about four months for the wound to heal, and then I pulled out the arrow using pincers, moving it from side to side, but it wouldn't come out; then I continued to try subtle and clever methods, until one day, as the shape of the arrow's head appeared at the end of this chapter, I managed to remove it while treating the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they consider that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I then restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have also told you about the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you place your cure where I do not mention it, because books cannot contain everything; but wise masters compare well and carefully a few small things, as well as what is present and lacking, finding new works and new tools for the descent of strange things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of members unless they are removed in two ways: either through the place where they entered or from another part; and that which comes out from the side where it entered is an arrow embedded in the flesh, and does not come out again at any time.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not now come out, let it stay until the swelling around it subsides and becomes light; and if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days and then move it; and when it comes out, use a fine needle to pierce the opening until the swelling around it is widened.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone at the base of the skull and goes all the way to one of the cavities of the brain, and none of the aforementioned accidents occur for the patient: do not try to pull it out, but let it stay even for several days, for if the arrow reaches that far, it can be fatal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded only in the bone and does not come out satisfactorily, it leaves the patient no days without some bad consequence, if cleverness in pulling it out is lacking.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then apply tar around it, as I have told you; then cure the wound while it is still healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is deeply embedded in the flesh and cannot be seen, even after trying everything; and if you feel it, use any suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves nearby, leave it until the wound has healed; and pull out the arrow if possible, and if it has roots by which it is attached, remove the part that is firmly embedded on one side, while bending or folding the arrow's tip, as much as you can without breaking it, so that you can pull it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, so that the bone around it is completely healed, then treat it later, for extraction will be easier.
