Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the signs of infection contradict what we have said about treatment in its chapter, then apply as we have described for the cure; and be careful with incision near the nerve and the vein, and find a way to extract the arrow without risk, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow entered, for that is the greatest help there can be, and if you cannot do it, then follow the signs as they show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another direction, opening something within, where the skin is swollen in a noticeable way: cut then on top, as much as the pincers can grasp, and then extract it: if it still projects outwards.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, widening it, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be extracted, leave it for now, and then try again until it comes out; and if there is a splinter of the arrow remaining in the flesh, let it stay, and then continue to extract; if it is hard, you must press gently, as if administering a stratagem, so that the tip of the arrow enters the opening of the instrument; then push it out, and if the arrow has been removed from the wound, insert the instrument with its point entering fully, in order to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is stuck, it is necessary that you clean all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow has pierced the skin, or the abdomen, or the bladder, or the side, and it is close to vital parts, and you can reach it, cut it out; but be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, then extract it, and cleanse the wound, as is necessary, and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The tool used to extract arrows resembles a bird's beak; here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form that points downward like a horse's tail is also like the feather of a bird, to push to the tip of the arrow, as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of claws to push and to hold, if this is the case:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins from which one can draw blood, of which there are 16 main ones: 2 veins behind the ears, called "herb cheeks"; and 2 arteries visible in both temples; and 2 veins in each elbow, called "aspirations"; and the vein across the forehead; and the vein at the base of the skull; and 2 veins around the collarbone; and 2 veins above the lips, called "augerich"; and 2 veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The common veins from which one draws blood are 5 in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, located on the left side and commonly called "vein of the head"; and the median is called "fast" and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and the common people call it "vein of the body"; and the basilic is on the right side and the common people call it "vein of the belly", located above the femur, and it is the one from which blood is taken, clearly visible through the skin.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the cure is the vein that lies between the little finger and the ring finger, and if it rains; and in the leg, there are three veins: one below the ankle on the left side, and the second on the ankle of the right side; and the third vein called "nasse," which is on the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg, there are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The cleansing of the veins behind the ears aids in the treatment of old catarrh and migraine; and the quality of this treatment is that you raise the patient's head and rub the affected area with a rough cloth; then bind the patient's collar tightly until the two veins behind the ears appear in two parts depending from the head. Hold them there, and where you feel the pulse below your hand, it signifies improvement; then take the lance and cut through the vein just below the bone, lifting your hand up the entire vein upstream, cutting and cauterizing the skin and vein well away from the bone, and drawing out blood until you see; then bind and tie it until it heals, as I have already mentioned incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	He heals the two arteries that are in the temples, if they are old and sore, and accustomed to tearing, and at the source of hot tears alone; and the quality of healing is as I say: and it is that the patient pulls his collar tightly, until the two arteries open wide; and feels the pulsation beneath his finger, and then signs with a gesture; then gently presses the heart over the artery above his right index finger, and withdraws the lancet underneath, and loosens the artery above, and the clot, as you have done in the other arteries, and do according to your need; then release the patient, and put your finger on the artery for an hour, then put a cotton ball; and then form a bandage and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their healing and extraction, as well as the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The health of the vein on the forehead is as valuable as the health of the cerebral vein, in the treatment of old facial ailments, such as migraine and redness; its quality is that the patient tightens his neck by twisting, until the vein appears. Then take the instrument called "disserter," which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip on the vein, holding it with your hand or something else, allowing the blood to flow according to its quantity; then loosen the patient's neck and tie the vein as long as it remains healthy without any wide wound.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, one must not let the flames be too strong; and do not cut across the body, for the bone is close, and there is a risk of breaking the flames when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The health of the two veins located in the arms is particularly important for healing wounds, itching, redness, and facial disorders; and its quality lies in the patient's ability to straighten their neck without any tension, as mentioned earlier. Then, the treatment should be gentle, with the flame slightly thin and not too long, for there is no room for error.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, it may break; then draw out the blood gently, as much as you need, and then bind it with cloth, and tie it tightly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The health of the vein near the nose is very valuable for treating sudden and severe conditions, such as migraines and redness that appear on the face, both new and old. The quality of the health is such that the patient tightens their collar and pulls their nose to the left hand, taking a subtle flame, long and thin, and inserting it between the two nostrils, since the vein does not open well enough, and the blood will begin to flow. Do not dig too deep, and draw out the blood gently according to your need, then bind it for one night, as it is quickly restored; this is the shape of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The holy oil of the two glands is helpful for the tightening of the eyelid, and for the onset of inflammation, and for many ailments, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and boils; and the quality of the oil is such that it draws the patient's skin away from each other, as we have said, and the master who is on top of the sick person's head, and the sick person sits in a certain place, then he opens the vein with a long cut, then treats the blood with temper, or as much as necessary; then does the same to the other vein, then loosens the bandage, and tightens the veins slightly so that the patient is not strangled, and leaves it until morning, so that the wound may heal.
de la sainie des leivres	from the cleansing of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cleansing of the veins of the lips helps to improve the condition of the mouth, and it aids in the healing of gum disease, lip cracks, and pain and swelling around them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the cleansing involves having the patient sit before you, holding their chin as mentioned earlier; then turn the lip and examine the veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left, which can be recognized by their black color and the small veins around them. Therefore, clean both of them, and if you do not know or doubt, take care to clean the thicker ones from each side, and in the same way, clean the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from cleansing the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The cleansing of the veins that are beneath the tongue is a valuable procedure after cleansing the head, and it helps with throat constriction, eye diseases, and mouth ailments; the quality of the cleanser should be such that the patient holds it between their hands in front of the sun, softens the tongue, and looks for dark veins on both sides. Then cleanse them, but do not press too hard, as there are arteries beneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck, which are commonly cleansed, are done so in two ways: either by pressing with a hot flame, or with a delicate olive-shaped instrument called an 'anesil', and they vary in width and tightness according to the veins themselves.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame burns intensely if it is very renowned, and it is wide as you can see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it requires skill to open veins with thick, clear blood that contain much blood and pus; and this is the shape of the olive-colored flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicate pointed, and it is for healing the subtle veins where there is delicate, yellow-tinged blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The healing of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, provides aid for diseases that are beneath the throat, and the collarbone, and the chest, and the belly; and it is important for the healer to heal gently and wash the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it affects the artery, and blood loss occurs, if it is necessary to stop it, as I have said; and the fire should not be painful, but cutting like a blade.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, it is necessary that you extract it and change it for another; or if you do not want to cut from it, heal it in place with a bandage: it opens clearly; and cut through it like a blade, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you recognize the place of the vein, it is necessary to extract the arm as you know its pulse; then mark the place with a signet, and bind the arm, and cut through the vein with a blade; but be careful not to hurt the artery when you see it swell, for that is the artery: beware of it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protruding at the top as urine from a child, and the veins are red and thin, know that it is an artery: then hurry, and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger so that it does not bleed again; this happens often. Let the arm be still, and do not move the patient; be afraid, and do not move until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the veins do not stop bleeding and it weakens you, and there is no medicine available, if the artery opens up, as the source of the retreat; then stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of fig bark, and cut it, and take one half and bind it tightly to the other half; if the wound stops bleeding, that's good; if not, treat it as we have said with powders that stop blood; the binding is not too tight due to the size of the wound, and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	If the vein bleeds from its head and body, it is because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; the healer should wash himself for the nerve below, and if he does not reach it thoroughly, and it touches the nerve, it swells and the health is compromised, and perhaps it cannot heal; this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then it must be healed with an instrument for venipuncture; avoid touching the nerve.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two bones, cut it from the tip.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere. However, it is necessary to seek the lightest method and do not be concerned if it fails the first time, and start over; and sometimes the veins may swell in some people when they try it for the first time, but there is no cause for concern.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it should only be done to maintain health and prevent future ailments; and it is performed through one of the three veins: the cephalic, femoral, or basilic. Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bloodletting to treat ailments does not have a specific time frame, but should be done as needed throughout the day or night; and children under 12 years old, and women who are pregnant for less than seven months, should not undergo bloodletting.

Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses. Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The doctor of salvation from the hand if it is good for all soft diseases, and this is the way: stretch the hand, and immerse it in hot water as long as the vein is inflated; if you feel the pain on one side, cross the hand over so that every nerve is exposed to the heat, and then immerse the hand again in hot water, if it feels numb in the wound, and it cannot heal.

The sage of the soul holds sway over all diseases that affect the body, such as diseases of the marrow, retention of flowers (perhaps referring to a metaphorical blockage or inflammation), diseases of the kidneys, and old injuries to the legs and feet, and similar ailments.

des sainies de ventouse	From the medical treatments of the suction cup.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horn, or iron, or glass; and the suction is created in two ways: either by puncturing and drawing out blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	This suction without piercing is performed in two ways: either with heat or without heat; and this type of suction, made by puncturing and extracting blood, is done in twelve places on the body, one over the forehead; others between the collarbone; others on both sides of the collarbone; one under the chin; one on each shoulder; one on the knees; and two on each leg; two on each ankle; and it does not involve the suction of blood vessels, only small veins scattered throughout the body, so as not to weaken anyone too much, as is done with vein punctures; and it should not be performed with heat or without heat in any illness resulting from excess, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary to open them due to illness or habit, then we should do so every hour at the beginning and end of the month, and in between; for there are those who, when they need to be opened, have a heavy head; and some experience swelling and redness on their face, head, neck, and become dark; and others have a drop of blood in their mouth, their tongue is swollen, and they bleed; and there are those who dream, see red blood, feel pain, die, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, and especially in the middle of the month, we order them to be opened after three hours during the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The doctor of the muse helps with the great pain in the head ...  that comes from sudden movements, and it is not appropriate to do so after evacuating all the body; and this treatment is for the health of the skull, and it is not appropriate for those with a cold complexion or scabs, as they cause them much harm; and for this reason, old people should not use it, nor those who have cold head ailments.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become blinded; and for this reason, they should apply the suction cup a little lower, out of doubt that it may cause blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation of the chest should be in favor of the health of the heart and basil (organs), and for this reason it causes constriction of the lungs, and a split in the channel of the diaphragm, and to all things related; and it is necessary to expel it with caution, because if it holds too tightly, it can cause impairment or harm to the stomach and body.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilation between the ribs can cause pain in the head, eyes, and migraines, as well as strangulation and pain at the roots of the teeth, being contrary to the health of the heart and basil (organs); and it is necessary that you instruct the patient to relax his hand when placing them, not to press the artery, and prevent complications with blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The inflammation of the gums is beneficial for mouth diseases, and for the corruption of gums, and similar ailments in the mouth; it is useful for the healing of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The inflammation of the shoulders is beneficial for diseases that arise from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The inflammation of the veins is just as useful as three veins in the arm, as it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to press too hard, for the skin is bare without fat, and knows how to close off vessels and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the rump is as harmful as bloodletting from the depths, and it causes diseases below, and it is necessary that the suction cup be large and made of iron, so that it needs to be well stretched; and perhaps, if it is too thin, it will break; and it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs close tightly, as they draw blood from throughout the body, and they are like the ancient pains of the kidneys, and bladders, and intestines, and they cause convulsions; and they are located on the two thighs, and the two ankles, but after long use, they weaken the body and bring on greater pain.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying a cupping glass is as follows: if you place it at first entirely empty and suck gently, then apply it firmly, move it equally, and do not stop until you see the red and inflamed skin, and open up the pores; afterwards, remove the cups, and pay attention to the condition of the skin, for there are some with thick, hard skin and others with thin, delicate skin. It is enough to make a single pass, and it is necessary to make deep wounds, and a little bit thoroughly; suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is deep, it is necessary to make two incisions: the first time to open slightly the thick vein of blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the pain is very sharp, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw out blood little by little, we are content with only one strike.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we should strike often; and if the pain is sharp, striking with precision until the vessels are suddenly pierced, it is necessary for one who has thick and tough skin, and who has calloused hands, to apply oil from suction cups that are softening and dissolving: in this case, purple oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in ivy, watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amaranth oil, or balsam, or donkey oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if anyone has a skin that is tender and has large pores, it is not appropriate to put oil on it, but after the cleansing with rosewater, or cold water, or blackberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or any similar water, it should be washed.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, if it rises from this, or from myrrh water, and sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excess mucus rise from old wine, or eucalyptus water, or chamomile decoction, or other similar things; and it is not advisable to use a cupping glass before a bath or after a bath, but rather an hour or two afterwards; and they should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that they wash themselves when they need to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And let those who have a fever be careful not to make it worse; instead, they should consume cold things like pomegranates, endives, lettuce, and similar foods; and eat little, lean meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, should sip syrup of honey and fragrant wine, neither too old nor too new, and eat little, and eat raisins and small birds and pigeons; and on the day that he undergoes an operation, he must drink more than he eats; and it is advisable to give any man, at any time, three times or a pinch of triacle or musk before or after the procedure to strengthen the principal members; but the cold should be avoided by those who are hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are applied without causing harm are those placed on the liver, and the spleen, and podagra, and the belly and the bowels and the kidneys and the hips, for these members do not tolerate being hurt in any way, and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, as we apply cupping to the breasts when the nipples are healthy; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cups on the belly and bowels to reduce the member; and it removes pain when there is congestion or a stone, as it may by chance draw away the congestion, or leave the stone in its proper place; and thus it acts when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retention of wind, and these cups are left empty to suck only; and they should never be made too hot, nor filled with cold water, as in cases where tears flow, and in this manner we fill the cup with hot water mixed with suitable herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cup (ventouse) administered by fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It should have two parts as broad as half a palm from end to end, and on its outer edge, near the middle, it should have a small hole, no larger than to fit an needle, and it should be made of iron or steel, so that it does not injure the patient when placed over the limb; and in the middle there should be a crossbar of iron or steel, to hold a cloth with a good grip, and their size can vary according to the disease and age of the person using them; for the cup sizes for children are different from those for adults and thin people compared to fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus should one place this cup on the affected member: take wax or linen cloth and put it through the hole in the cup, so that the light shines at the bottom of the cup to prevent burning the patient; then place it on the member, and your fingers should be on the opening we have mentioned, so that when you look, the vapor goes out, and remove the cup; and use the linen cloth as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cup used to treat pleurisy and other acute ailments, there is no hole or opening, and it can be applied effectively only when filled with water. It should be placed on the affected member only when it is completely full of water; this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without bandages, they are only healed in members where one cannot apply a tourniquet due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and when the skin is stripped from the member, like a doe or goat, or others of a similar nature, and if the quality of the wound is such that when you find bandages that are in clear, sweet water without putrefaction, take them; and place them in clear, sweet water until they become smooth, and have nothing in their bellies; then make an incision with a vein and tourniquet, rub the member until it turns red, and apply the bandages; and when they are sore and chafed, if this is a member where a tourniquet can be applied, apply it, for it is much better afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If he does not lift the lion from its place, and then water, well, and then hopes; and if his joints feel too stiff after the body of the bones, so moisten the linen cloth with cold water, and put it on, until the bones are relaxed; and if the bones are multiplied, so put vitriol powder or gall, and similar things, until they are relaxed; or you place half a peeled fava bean on the lion, and leave it until it attaches to the bone, then it will relax now; and if you need more, take other bones.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the bones do not want to be taken, rub fresh blood on the lion, or insert an needle into the bone until it bleeds, then place them back; and soon as they smell the blood, they will attach; and when you see that they are chewing, sprinkle a little aloe and silk powder, or ash, and they will stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	We begin the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the wise minds of this chapter come from a knowledge never seen in ancient books, nor written down; for this reason, the science is strange in our land, because I found no good book on it, and learned nothing about it except through the knowledge of ancient books, upon which I have so diligently studied, both by experiment and the custom of my life. And so I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and at the end I have abridged it, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we explain in this prologue of this book the principles of speech and the chapters where the wise men apply their understanding, and focus on truth, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When a fracture, dislocation, or twist occurs, it is necessary to quickly tend to the patient, both on the affected side and the other, if nothing helps, such as weakness of the body, illness, or old age; or if the condition is very severe, or too cold, and you use things that are cold like ice packs, or a horse's or deer's skin, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty foods, and do not fill the body with meat that fills the veins with blood, as long as you have doubt about the formation of an abscess or the spread of material to the limb; then the patient will return to their previous condition as they had used to be.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one alleviate the patient from foods that cause excessive belching, or have a viscous consistency, such as cooked flour in water, laughter, and pressure, and the stomach, and effusions, and odors, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For excessive belching often prevents the bone from healing properly, and delays the recovery of the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones broken in the very old and decrepit do not heal well or unite firmly according to their nature because of the stiffness of the members, nor do those that are too soft, such as the bones of young children; but take no heed, rather hold fast to the broken bone with strong tenons that join the member together, as it was before, and do not remove it entirely from its place, for this reason one must consume large amounts of substantial foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manners of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another when sharpening, such as the cutting of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, then it is a small crack all around.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each condition has its own mechanism and specific tool for restoration, according to the memory that comes to mind; and the fracture of bone is known because the joint is twisted, well opened by force, and sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twist or pain in touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it can have a twist, or a split, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with the hand, but apply remedies that come to mind later, and then gently tighten it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes up in the air, and the two parts are disjointed, he must now set them even, so that the abscesses come from there; and if hot abscesses come, he should not leave it for any day, until the abscesses calm down; then place it evenly as you can lightly and skillfully, and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restorations of where it is broken. Then tighten it, as is appropriate hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if a bone is broken in two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or one of the smaller members, or at the joints, or at one joint and your hand, place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are out of alignment, all the instruments adjust themselves to their proper places, and be careful not to cause the patient any injury or pain through your work; and carefully align the two ends of the bone.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he will feel it well with his hand if it seems to him that it is not well: if it is dressed properly and not pulled too hard, not pressed as those who cause the hot abscess and contraction in the member by their own work, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is at rest, gently encourage the patient not to move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor turn it in any way; and be careful that the member is well secured so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, and it is not yet healed, it is necessary to put it in a position where he feels no pain; and be careful that it is put right, so that there is no twisting when it is restored; and the quality of the damaged member will depend on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that broken members are diverse in size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For it has small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: it is necessary to wrap them with soft and fine linen; and those that are large, like thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and firm ligature, for the wide ligatures embrace the whole member, and tighten it equally from all sides, so that there is no movement; then apply slight, light compresses, three or four times around the member, and tighten your hand slightly on the entire ligature, then go above the fracture and tighten less, allowing the fracture to move a little; and soften the ligature little by little, until you press greatly on the healthy part below; then take another ligature and wrap it around again from the top of the broken member; then go back to the underpart of the fracture, and tighten it moderately, not too tightly or too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above; then place between the ligatures soft linen compresses or pieces of cloth, until it is all even, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply a hot, soothing compress to it, which reduces the swelling, and leave it for several days; then stretch your limbs, and use a narrow cane cut sharply from a tree trunk, or palm fronds, shaped as follows:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the cane placed on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others; and as long as is suitable for the member, whether small or large; then tighten the canes as you did in the first layer, but tie them with thread as in the first layer on the fracture; tighter now, less later; and the thread should be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of flax; because if the thread is too thick, it's like the work of fools who make their bindings from twisted flax threads, and that is a great error, for the binding cannot be even if it is too thin, and it does not suit that there be less space between each cane.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is troubled by the roots of the stars after dislocating them from their healthy places, he should place soft cloth or other dressing over them to avoid bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the veins are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to extract all the stars from all the broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the members are large, it is not appropriate to put stars inside until after 5 or 7 days, or according to your judgment based on the heat of the abscess; and see here the ancient method of using emplasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, mix it with enough egg, and make this paste, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common method for an emplaster that restores fractures in various positions, especially for women and small children, as it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to make a plaster that restores fractures, dislocations, and twists: take equal parts of bear's fat, lard, wool, asafoetida, and gum arabic; add X parts of myrrh and aloe, V parts of aloes, VIIII parts of alechen, and make it into powder, mixing with egg albumen. If the patient's body heat is high, use this plaster, as it is of good composition, and it restores broken bones severely, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster for twists: take mugwort and visalva, X parts; myrrh and aloes, 7 parts; acacia, 6 parts; Armenian bole, X parts; grind well and mix with vinegar or egg albumen, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of splinting joints and realigning bones in their sockets, soothing the pain that comes from it, and using the saw to cut the bone, and the fracture: take a new cloth, moisten it with oil and heat, and place it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cyst splints do not restore, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of splinting that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves and land pavot (opium poppy) leaves, grind together, and make a paste.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of splinting to restore the broken bone and thereby lessen the pain of healing.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the roots of chamomile, violets, and valerian, all in equal parts; grind them fine, mix with wine, and apply to the affected member after heating it. Alternatively, mix with fresh coriander water or water alone, and use as needed.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of splinting when a hard abscess forms during the healing of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of alder, and flaxseed, and balm, and melilot, and fennel, and violets, and chamomile, from each a small part; grind them and prepare a paste with sharp salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that one should not apply heat or cold to a broken member, but instead use a plaster made only of wax and oil, neither too hot nor too cold.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen recommends applying warm, dry substances to a broken member to aid in healing, such as myrrh and aloe and incense, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of dressing that is effective against injury and pain: take moss and sheepskin or chicken feathers, and wool equal in amount, grind them, and make a paste and bind it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, afterwards, be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor do the bones move from their place; if it becomes painful or there is itching, feeling of restlessness or swelling, act quickly, remove the dressing and take out the plaster now; then take a light cloth, a moist sponge, dip it in water, and lift up the affected area until the itching stops and the pain subsides. Leave the member to rest for an hour, then put on a dry compress, moistened with water or rose oil, and bandage it tightly, making sure you are certain of the heat of the abscess. This will reduce the inflammation in the affected member and alleviate the pain; then repeat the process gently, using less plaster this time, and do not strain it too much as before; treat it gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red, swollen, painful, and hot, and it reoccurs, then you need to apply a poultice and bind it, just as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If the limb does not heal after what we have said, do not dislocate it before three or four or five or seven days; and never leave it for twenty days, as long as the fracture is open, and the adjustment of the bone to the flesh approaches; then you should restrain it more than initially, and fatten its flesh, as I have said above. And if you see that the limb dries out more than is necessary, know that healing will not come. Then apply hot water every time you dislocate it, every third day, and open the wound slightly; by this work, therefore, the healing of the limb is cut short, and a great deal of harm results from what the ignorant do, who distort the limb incorrectly: this is bad, and there are many dangers in it, and I see nothing else but to leave it alone and do it right.
des diverses manieres de brisure	From various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of fracture, with various shapes and distinct causes; for there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, where the bone breaks completely through to the other side, as in a hack or a thrust; this is why this type of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or, the sword may cut through the bone without piercing it, and this is called a "absolute" fracture; and these two types of fractures can be either large or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a pounding, or indentation, or cutting of stone, or injury from a fall upon stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a recent fracture, which approaches the skin just under the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is healed in the bone is as subtle as a hair, and the fracture is small, it is called a "capillary" fracture; and if the wound is made by striking with stone, or fall, or similar thing, and the piece of bone enters inside, and the bones are entangled as when a smith works on the furnaces; then between the bone and the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones in their heads, such as young children's heads; and it occurs in all these ways of dislocation, that small fragments are broken off, just as if they were. And I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the ways of dislocations by the traction on them, and the inquiry at close range, and by the corrupt flesh above them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is determined by the fact that when the bone is discovered and rubbed in place, it opens up the fracture, revealing its black nature.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be cautious regarding accidents with the patient, and if you notice any harmful accident, such as vomiting blood, loss of consciousness, excessive stretching, paleness, sudden fever, or other similar symptoms occurring in various combinations, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming accidents and hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the injury.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this happens, and you quickly remove the bone on the seventh day, so that the wound beneath the bone is corrupted, then the complications that we have described will occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone breaks down to the tissue that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split the broken part in this way: and it is important that you press the patient's head with pain, and expose the bone in every way possible, and clean the wound gently as much as you can, and if blood oozes upon exposing the bone, or an abscess forms later, then seek help from those who know, and fill the space around the bone with moist, rose-scented cloth; and rest the wound until the swelling subsides and you are sure of no further bleeding. Then begin removing the bone, and this is done in two ways: one way is to carefully cut a narrow opening in front, and this is its shape...
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then take another treatment even greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is that you have many different-sized treatments, some narrow and others wide, and they are sharp and made of indurate iron; and perform them gently so as not to damage the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, it is necessary that you pierce around it, so as to administer treatments with care, so that they do not go through the bone too deeply, and there should be a margin or a circle on top of the point, preventing it from going through the bone; and you need several of them, so that each one comes in its proper place according to the thickness of the bone, so as to have care for all bones; and this is the form of the three types of treatments:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.
