The quality to know when an bone is broken is that you apply pressure on the bone, and return your hand to its normal position until you know the bone is set; then place the pressure elsewhere a little later, doing this all around, then cut with incisions the space between the fractured parts of the bone, and do so as delicately as possible, lightly, as we have said, while still holding the bone in your hand or using any tools you have such as pliers or tweezers; be careful not to touch the brain or the soft tissue.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have set the bone and treated it, it is necessary to observe the tension that remains in the bone compared to any other tool similar to an incisive; however, it should be more gentle and subtle than the others. If there is no remaining tension in the small bones or scales, gently remove them with any suitable tools; then dress the wound with bandages and treatments as we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that which Galen says, which is safer; it is very powerful, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone, either where the break is open, and once you have exposed this part, place the sharp edge of this lens-shaped incision tool against it, which has this shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, but expose the acute part on the inner side, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then gently strike with a small hammer, so that you slightly raise the bone all around, and be careful to protect the tissue underneath; if it is distant from the bone, gently lift it, for otherwise it will cause great pain and suffering.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the skin, and the bone is only cut from above, leaving small pieces, then it is necessary to clean these asperities, and remove the scales with a delicate rasp, having various quantities of it at hand, to apply in each case the most suitable, according to the severity and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you encounter great resistances, and afterwards more subtle ones, do not cease from this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate incisions and fractures, it is necessary to apply treatment according to their location; and this is something that is not easily answered by one who has dedicated his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the patient is satisfied with the treatment and it needs to be uncovered, you should press a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, soaked in rose oil, onto the wound; then take another cloth, doubled over twice or thrice, soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; do this as lightly as possible so as not to harm the patient, then apply another bandage and don't tighten it too much until the wound is only slightly covered; leave it like that for a day or two, until the abscess has calmed down, then remove it and administer medications such as licorice roots, flour of alder trees, incense powder, arisology, and similar substances; make a powder from these things and apply it to the wound, and give the patient universal remedies without blistering; ensure the wound is always clean, and do not leave any dressing on it or let pus accumulate, because when pus accumulates under the cloth, it will corrode and destroy the flesh of the patient, causing great harm.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no adverse event comes to the patient as we have said, it is uncertain without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness comes only due to the medicine placed upon it, how much virtue it holds, then you should press a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and wrap it in a cloth; then apply it to the sick, and cure it with the remedies that are appropriate, as long as they are healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You should know that the two parts of the bone are never broken, either completely or only partially, because they are two bones; and the inner part is cartilage, which does not break, but only bends or twists, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should insert your little finger or a narrow tool into the gap, and place the same fragment back in its proper position, and close it gently, until the bone returns to its natural shape; and do this carefully, so that the patient does not feel pain from your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the bone near the joint, and the fingers cannot reach it, you should place a thin, straight tool under one edge of the break and gently straighten it until the finger can access the broken area.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in both parts, you should do the same and try to restore it on the first day, if possible; if not, wait until the swelling has subsided after the seventh or tenth day, then gently pull the broken pieces together using strips of linen, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or turn to another side if it is broken, and let the fragments be; so that the edges are thick enough to fill the gaps in the wound.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no restoration is required if the edges are moistened with butter, and each day they must be changed.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think this is good, but it is necessary that they be moistened with an egg yolk mixture and mill powder; then leave the edges, until the bone is healed and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never burn the skin with hot pens or needles on different parts, and if it hurts greatly around, and holds the bruise, and breathes among the patient; or do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses occur at the site while you are treating it, apply a plaster or moist cotton dipped in rose oil or in a poultice of duck fat.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not form, apply an external plaster made of flour, incense powder, confited with egg albumen, then place light stays on top and do not tie the skin; and if the bruise is small and broken into small pieces, remove it with suitable instruments, then clean the gap, and treat with charred things, and stitch it up, as appropriate plasters and bandages for it; and if there are no wounds inside the abscess, cure it externally, and place splints until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the dislocation of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only slightly out of place, and it is not broken into two pieces, but only crooked inward, then if you recognize this lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should insert your index finger of the left hand into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, insert your index finger of the right hand, gently pushing the fracture inward, and then pull it outward with the other hand, making it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is severe in two places, then it is necessary that you administer extension to both parts, as long as they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or loosening, using a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then apply cerate to the broken jaw and place a double cloth; on the cloth, place a large, well-made star or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, secure it to the muscles you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes after three days, then reset it as it was; apply plaster next, using fine powder with an abundance of egg or sesame flour, after removing the cerate; place a thin layer of plaster and let it dry; if it does not change the patient's condition and becomes healthy, leave it until it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses appear, it is necessary to do as we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both a fracture and a wound together, it does not matter which part of the bone is broken; it is necessary to use suitable instruments for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, it should be widened with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And after you have removed all these pieces and it does not delay, if the wound is wide, close it with suitable plaster, to promote healing, as long as it is healthy.
de la forcele	from the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break many times near the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: it may be broken and separated into two parts, with fragments, and is easier to restore; or there is a fracture with an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is as follows when the fracture is without an injury, that you have two assistants: one holds the aid that is broken; and the other extends the collar towards the affected part; then set the fracture equally in both hands, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is no bulge or depression.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place a round, thick cloth or woolen spear beneath the patient's shoulder, according to your need; stretch and gently apply force, holding the spear with your hand, so that you align the fracture correctly as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the fracture away from the stronger part, because it is firmly stuck, then it is necessary for the patient to lie on their side with their shoulder supported, and have the assistants push the shoulder downwards, until the bone of the fracture is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture with your hands, and if you feel any debris, it is necessary to cut through; gently pull the pieces apart, and if the bone cannot join together despite your best efforts, use the instrument beneath the fracture to achieve the desired effect.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it should look like a spoon, and is not broken off, and is as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it has two ends, as you see, one being wider than the other, just as the rupture of the wound that you made when treating the bones; and when you are certain of the hot abscess, if you cut the wound deeply, or if the incision is small, then doubt the hot abscess, and apply drapes and bands to the wound according to its amount.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses occur, then moisten the bandage with rose oil and silk and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is wounded and broken, is to place on the bone the plaster of very fine powder and egg albumen, and put light bandages on top, and insert a spike under the shoulder blade if needed; then take a very wide strip of cloth, put the bandage with plaster on it, wrap it around the injury, so that the ends of the cloth hang down from the broken bone; place the splint on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the collarbone and under the healthy shoulder blade and the injured one; rearrange each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the splint firmly, and clearly see that the splint does not move on the fractured bone, reward it every day, and when the ligament loosens, tighten it; put the patient on his back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder blade while he sleeps, to raise the injury; lighten the fracture by aligning the shoulder, or tie the arm to the collarbone, and do not loosen it for twenty days, unless a bad accident happens; then recommence the plastering if needed, tighten it, and leave it thus until it is healed; it is healed in no more than 28 days, and less so for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	If the shoulder is dislocated and does not move except by touch, then reset it according to the shape of the dislocation, in every way that you can. Then apply a fine, powdery poultice with plenty of egg, and cover it lightly with a double cloth. Place a wide and thin board, slightly larger than the shoulder, and lay the dislocated bone so that it is evenly covered by the poultice; then fasten it firmly with a strong bandage, ensuring that the bone does not move from its place, and check it each day. Whenever it loosens, tighten the bandage and realign the bone if it has moved. Place the patient on their side, and in this way the shoulder will be restored in 10 to 25 days. And when this number of days is complete, untie it carefully, for it is not a bone that can be easily put back.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out and is not pulled away from the heart, it pushes up the bone and does what we said about soothing the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the break of the worst abscess
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The fracture is never broken in the middle, but that happens rarely; it often breaks at the extreme ends.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines away from the heart, causing the patient great pain and weakness, sometimes bleeding, opening up the fissures in the broken bone, and feels all better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and places a cushion between their shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and aligns the ribs with both hands, subtly adjusting it to the proper shape of the bone; then apply plasters and compresses over the delicate salt or other light bandage, wrapping it in a cloth and securing it to the broken bone so that it does not move. And re-tie the linen around the back, tightening it appropriately, and check the wound every hour, if it becomes softer, tighten it; if it needs to be released due to corrosion, itchiness, pain, or an abscess at the site, act quickly, remove the plaster, scratch off the ointment, and address the cause of the condition with appropriate treatment. Then reapply the plaster and continue to tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	from the fracture of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You know that the fracture of ribs only occurs in the upper part of the back, and at the top, and they do not bend unless they are broken; and this causes great pain to anyone examining them.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you place the fracture correctly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a stick, if you have such materials at hand.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inward, it makes the patient feel very great pain and piercing, as if from crying, because the bone pierces the flesh; and then he loses his breath, vomits much blood, and this causes great suffering and illness, and the ancients have put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And for those who say that it is appropriate to administer foods that cause bloating in the stomach to expel the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not pretend that incisions without heat will not come if they have not previously been caused.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it appears, then it is healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that none of you should apply suction cups to the limbs for draining, as it seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the suction cup might draw away excess fluids from the limb due to weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that none of you should cover the wound with moistened wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to equalize the pressure around it, then treat it with care for pleurisy, flesh, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure through the bone where the fracture is, and there is doubt in the patient, it is necessary to cut into the broken ribcage, and place an instrument to hold it; then one must break the bone, pull gently, and then sew the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with poultices, until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses form, place moistened oil-soaked rags on them and lay the patient down; treat while the abscess is present, lying flat on their side where it formed, until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	from the fracture of the collarbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No fracture occurs to the collarbone bone at any time, and it rarely happens that it hurts; also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to a person, and you want to know if they will recover, pay attention if you see their hands becoming soft, swollen, and numb, and are unable to move or stretch them, and if you prick them with a needle, they don't feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Knowing that it is dangerous in many ways, if the patient remains silent and feels well when you press upon them, but not when they are moved, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the illness of the patient will be cured, if proper treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things occur in the back of the spine, you must know if there is a fracture or not, if you observe whether their legs are weak, and if there are accidents that are in the hands, and on the back, sudden movements and expulsions without will; and when it is remembered on the belly, such sudden expulsion without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is remembered on the back and he wants to move, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Knowing that it is deadly: therefore, do not labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that if there is an abscess, you apply hot oil or egg-yolk oil to it until it is soothed; then put a comforting and drying plaster on it and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is detached, it should be covered with bandages; then the bone is removed, and the two edges of the wound are sutured if it is large, then treated with poultices in a warm manner until it heals; and if the fragment of bone is broken off, which is called the "fragment of the wound," you press it gently with your left hand, and place it level with the other hand, then apply the plaster and the splint, if needed; then bind it tightly, and if there are any detached bones, reduce them and treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	From the fracture of the bone of the spine.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the bone of the spine is fractured, and if there is not even a little reduction in the head, it causes pain, swelling, and inflammation at the site of the fracture.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it (the fracture), as long as you are above the break; and you know what the fracture is and its form; and if the fracture is only at the top, then make an equal cut, as long as it retains its natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, it bends inward, then place the patient on his stomach until the healing of that fracture becomes apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And once you have made it even, place a splint over it, then put a board or hard cloth on top and tighten the fracture so that it does not move, and keep the patient's side elevated until the bone is aligned.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess appears and is not touched, until the abscess is calmed down, apply what we have previously said; then return to restoration, holding it as appropriate, if there is no adverse event, and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	dislocation of the shoulder joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is located between the collarbone and the top of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, it must be restored using one of two methods: one involves taking a thick, middle-sized stick, according to this shape...
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And hold the two feet, and stretch them upwards, and place the patient on a seat; then break one of his arms over the thigh, until it becomes relaxed, and wrap it with a bandage of cloth, then stretch it onto a heavy object or have someone pull it down; then bring the broken part back to its proper position, as is necessary.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is to lay the patient on his back, and tie one hand to his neck, then instruct the attendants to dip what is above the broken part of the hand in water, and below in alcohol, and extend each part accordingly.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that extraction is too forceful, then tighten the ligature around the break, and on the break, extend each of the assistants to their respective sides.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is near the top of the shoulder, it is necessary to place a ligature halfway under the acromion, and another towards the side of the neck, underneath the break; and if the break is on the side of the neck, it is necessary to apply a light ligature without strain, as long as the break remains level on the bone, then set it properly and tighten it, without causing complications.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if a muscle pulls (aposteme) and will not release for seven days, apply a moist cloth in ash and rose oil until the pull is soothed; then tighten it, and the manner of tightening is to place the plaster on the tear, then reassemble the arm over the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; and cover with a drape, tighten over the muscle and the arm, so that the arm is in a straight position, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moved, use pins, and place a wider and stronger pin on the tear, leaving two spaces between each pin, and make each pin so large that it passes through the tear three times; then tighten the pins, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter regarding the tear, from a distance first.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the stars and the straining, as we have said, when you return the broken member, and doubt the heat of the abscess, leave it bound for seven days, as we have said; then every three days check the binding, that no swelling or pain comes to the place, or the healing cannot come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it agrees, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident happens, do not take off the binding for three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; place beneath the dislocated limb a flat cushion of equal thickness made of wool, and every hour during the day or night watch that the shape of the limb does not change or the binding become loose; if it agrees through the virtue of medicine, and give them food as we have mentioned above, in such a way that the food is first made subtile; and when they begin to recover, it will be substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is custom that the shoulder and leg should be reset after forty days, and then the dislocation must be released and treatment with baths and medicinal herbs be administered to correct the position.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the contraction is severe and tight, it may take several days or even months to release it.
de la brisure du bras	of the dislocation of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, called the femur and radius, where one is smaller and extends towards the hand, and the other is larger and lies below, towards the elbow; so it may happen that only the large bone (femur) or small bone (radius) breaks, or both may be affected.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small fractures are broken, the restoration and healing is light, but when the large ones are broken, the healing is poor, and more painful than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small fractures that are broken, it is necessary to extend them slightly and evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large fractures, it is necessary to pull stronger; and stretch them on a cushion, and place the palm of the hand higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the others, and let the patient cross his legs over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher than the patient's pain allows; then have one minister extend his strong arm to the part below his hand, or to the wrist, and another minister above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then arrange them evenly, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture, each one is placed in its place, and if there is none that grips the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, by making it on top of the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the specific chapter; then take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if, in the beginning of restoration, abscesses occur, then I apply a bandage made of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and I wrap it gently over, until the abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the plaster, and apply the pouder from the soft mill with enough egg, then place the needles, making the needle of the fracture stronger and a little wider than the others; know that it should have 6 needles or more in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; tighten more over the fracture than elsewhere, but not too far away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and make the drapes on top of the fracture soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread, from which it is pulled, be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after no days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if no adverse event occurs in the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you soak the limb in hot water until the itching is soothed; and let the limb not be squeezed too tightly at rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then repeat the stretching, and if the ligaments loosen and the bones disalign, or any similar thing, address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, it is necessary to loosen it slightly and leave it for a few days until the swelling goes down, and then tighten it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to the patient, then he should be released after twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If in doubt, bind his hands to his chest, making sure the collars are even, and guard against movement and gestures, and have him sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is healed in thirty days or forty-five, or perhaps in twenty days, depending on the combinations and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and in the fingers there are often fractures, and they come but with great pain many times over.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the hand's bone is broken or bent, it is necessary for the patient to cut across it, and place it straight before him equally; then he places his hand on a stretched-out cloth, and extends the broken bones' ministers, and aligns them properly, until they are well joined; and applies the poultice and compresses if there is no abscess, and then wraps it with a piece of linen cloth according to its size.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is near the joint's belly, make a ball of cloth, and instruct the patient to press it against his broken hand; then pull it out with a long cloth, and take a piece of gauze as large as the hand, and wrap it tightly, as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the end, it is necessary to place a stick across and another under the sole, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and stop the bleeding between them.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in neither of the joints, and it is dislocated, place it evenly, as it should be; tighten it with the sole, and if you see that putting a small, straight stick will raise the dislocation without moving it, do so. And if the dislocation is in the other finger, like the index or any other, place it evenly and tie it with the healthy joint afterward; either hold them all tightly or put a stick on it, as needed, taking care during the restoration and alignment of the abscess above, and support what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	from the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The hipbone is often broken, and one can clearly see it when it returns to its original position in front and behind; its restoration is achieved by binding it tightly over the break and from the other side.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their face, then each limb extends equally to both sides; this is when the break is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the hipbone, one ligament should be bound towards the knee, and others ligaments should bind from below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, then loosen the ligaments of the knee, and allow the extension; then place the splint so that the bone is level in both hands, as per its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and fasten it, so that there are no gaps.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside, then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is advisable to wrap the fracture with a hard bandage, cutting off the excess, and then return the leg until the heel reaches the root of the toe, and insert a long thread between the calf and the leg below the knee joint, and bring the end above; then return to the leg and calf, wrapping the bandage again, and place a stirrup on it, and put a stirrup on the leg bone; then use eight pieces of soft cloth between the leg and calf to make equal compression. Then, as you move higher on the bandage, loosen the grip, and tie three or four knots above the bandage; and take two threads that you had inserted between the leg and calf, and tie three stirrups above them, then return to below the knee with the thread, until you reach the foot. Tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it as it is, so that there is no further abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens that he dislocates it again and it comes back as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that are caught, one must try to free them if possible; and if one cannot, it is necessary to break the joint and pull out the fragment, and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never should the ankle be broken in this way with staples, as is done in the aid of the shoulder or arm; however, even after such restoration, the patient does not recover.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the ankle is restored in 7 to 10 days, or a bit less or a bit more, depending on the variety of conditions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the gutter of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	You know that in the gutter of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, even if it is only a crack or an opening, it affects every wound, and feels wounded, and this feels good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when you put each part back in its place as much as possible, and then apply a poultice, and place a round plaster if necessary, and tighten it appropriately, and follow all the arrangements we have mentioned for other breaks, such as an abscess or any similar condition; apply what is appropriate to each case, as long as it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	from the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	You know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called the "tibia" and the other the "fibula"; and all fracture occurs in the same way as in the arm, and the treatment is similar. If both bones are broken together, the leg will turn in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bones are broken, they bend forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the thick bone is broken, it causes great pain, and one can see it well; and it turns inward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension, and set it equal, and tie the stars equally; but still, it is necessary that the rupture be ugly, and there are many parts, so that the extension is smaller and lighter; and align according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of strong cloth that cover the leg on both sides, and are as long as the leg from the knee to the foot; then wrap them in two layers and bind them tightly in the middle, so the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and so it is well. And no one should administer any treatment along the length of the leg, and if it is of strong cloth, they place the leg to prevent movement, and they properly perform this at the rupture where there is an abscess or other complication; and each day they move the leg to see if there is an abscess or other accident; if so, they treat it until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the fracture of bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones in the foot can be fractured and the toes, and there is no permanent cure except for various splints.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If the bones in the foot are fractured and you see them pushing against each other, so that the patient cannot bear weight on their foot, just as if they wanted to walk, then place your foot on theirs, holding the broken bones in place until they return to their natural position; then apply a splint and bandages above, and place a small, flat table inside the sole of the foot with two holes, then tighten it around the foot, wrapping cloth and other necessary items around it.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three days or four have passed, if you loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones even, either broken or discolored.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are no bones broken, if they are restored, as we said about the hand's joints, then take a stick according to the length of the bone and make it slightly wider, then place the table (splint) from below on the foot, and bind it firmly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, then put on each bone a stick according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the table from below the foot; and let it be firm on top of the stomach of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, when we have discussed them; and treat each injury as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	on the fracture of the bone in the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When a woman's bone in her hand is fractured and the swelling subsides, then she should incline her body to one side, holding it from behind. Next, fill the gap left by the fracture with cotton, and also add a significant amount; then raise the woman up slightly, pressing her back gently, and repeat this process until the cotton reaches the entrance of the bone, helping the bone to heal in place. If she needs to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished, replace it, repeating this seven times or so. This will restore the fracture, and if you see any signs of infection, take a bladder from a goat, attach a tube to the opening, and completely fill the bladder inside the fracture site; then blow on the tube until the bladder is inflated inside: this will help the bone heal. Then fill it with cotton again and leave it like that for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the arm or the leg is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from one who puts his study and skill into it, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture indicates various dispositions for the right way of restoration; understand this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the staff is broken, take a goose throat and insert it into the staff; then wrap cloth around it, leave it for three or four days, and it will heal naturally.
de brisure avec plaie	from fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is great, such as the bone of the leg or shoulder or similar, it is necessary for him to be healed now, so that the healings we have mentioned bear witness to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but there is residual poison, and you have nothing else, then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour or day, before abscesses form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscess begins to heal, let it be for new days until the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it for a third or fourth day, lest you bring about a harmful outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible through the skin when you uncover the heart, it is necessary that you place it gently with your hands, slightly extended.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear suitable to place equally in your hands, then take this instrument made of iron, with seven or eight fingers (inches) long, and its width should be according to the amount of the wound; and for this purpose, it is best that he imprudently takes three or four (times), according to what is needed for each break treatment; and it should be rounded and slightly thick, so that it does not bend under pressure on the member during your work, and it should be thin in front, thick in the middle towards the front, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," so the dislocated bone should be placed back on the visible head of the joint; then close it once, until it returns, and be even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot grasp the bone firmly, you must hold the head of the bone until the instrument has a firm grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, with a suitable instrument such as a chisel or saw, within your power; then remove what is left in the bone from jaggedness and small fragments.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reduced, and the patient feels great pain afterward, knowing that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do your best to ensure it is in its place, then moisten the cloth with a dry black styptic wine, and apply it properly; do not put any wax or other substance on the wound that could lead to putrefaction and corruption. Then administer remedies after you have restored the bone, leaving the wound uncovered, and clean the surrounding area according to the size of the wound; be very careful not to strain the wound with the fracture. Often, this has led to the patient's death or caused corrosion. The compresses should be softer and gentler than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or great, and you doubt that a worse accident may come, as we have said, and you feel pain in place, unless it is necessary to put bandages on, but wrap around, instead of bandages, hard cloth, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is beginning to close, remove everything you have put on it, and apply a healing dressing for wounds, such as a four-ingredient ointment or similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to dislocate the member two times a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is swollen and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be dislocated in such a way that the bow of the joint moves slightly downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the dislocation persists, and it cannot be reduced fully, understanding that there may be small fragments of bone, then you must open the wound with a knife, and remove all these unwanted pieces causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms in the place, or any other type of corruption, then it must be treated according to what is said in this chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when a bone is broken and open on the limb, like the bone of the calf or the shoulder, or other similar bones in the great limbs, do not pull it, for often death results, but let it rot until it falls off; perhaps after 20 days or 30, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	burns that come from the heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the burn, especially when it is near a joint, and it is a bad sight to see the shape of the limb; and by chance, the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then, if we must administer: if you give stiffening medicines like aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar ones, be sure to press any of these things, or all together, into a compact mass with pungent wine, or with abundant honey, or with ash; and place it on the affected area, hold it tightly, and do not release it for several days; and then dislocate it and begin again with another, until the swelling is gone; or press a piece of well-made lint; for the property of lint is to draw out all swelling from the limbs; and if the dislocation has already hardened like stone, it must be removed, cutting off the excess above, and treating the remaining part until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the weak member after treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed and the weak and delicate member remains, it occurs for many reasons: one is because it was bound too tightly and not properly secured; or because there are too many bindings and it cannot follow the natural movements of the limb; or due to excessive swelling; or from too great movements, not in their proper time; or because it has little blood in its body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	The treatment is as follows: you make the patient eat, and stretch their body, until blood flows abundantly within them; then administer a bath, give them joy and comfort; next, apply soot to the member, so that the soot attracts great blood flow, and often splash it with cold water, until the circulation reaches the limb; and it will return to its natural state.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The dislocated joint must be straightened after its healing.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When a member is twisted after healing and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those who claim one must break the limb from the moment of new growth, and many foolish practices have been observed in our lands. Such acts are blameworthy and cause great harm, perhaps even death.
