However, if the inflammation and pain are recent, it is necessary to raise them with hot water or cook soft herbs such as fennel leaves, roots, licorice, and similar things; prepare a mollifying poultice as well, using a carefully prepared aqua-distilled eagle's claw, and take the mucilaginous extract of fennel, mixing it with goose fat or oil of chamomile, and apply it as a poultice. Alternatively, use fig extracts and grind them with colon powder and other medications that help reduce stiffness.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the node crushed by continuous and prolonged friction with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow the limb to move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the swelling and hardness become like stone, also as in the case of a stone, it is necessary to crush with iron, if required all the way to the bone, using a delicate incision; and apply compression and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begin the books on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur from no joint being in its proper place, which prevents movement, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs from no cause, it is necessary to bring the limb back towards its proper position immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the limb swells, and by chance if it is reset at a later time, it may be painful; for this reason, it is not advisable to move it immediately when it is swollen. Often, it causes inflammation and other pains; however, once this occurs, make the patient better, then leave it until the abscess has healed; then apply hot water and oil, and gently reset the limb, treating each member as it comes.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder joint all the way down to the foot.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It is often the case that the jawbones become dislocated, and there are two types of dislocations: either they are slightly out of their sockets, soft and flexible; or they are completely dislocated, hanging down towards the chin, and draining saliva from the mouth, preventing it from closing, and causing the tongue to protrude when speaking.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself through various dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it forcefully, without delay; and in such a way that the healer places the patient's head with his sick mouth, pulling the lower jaw towards the root of the dislocation, so that it becomes aligned; and the other two hands should be extended equally; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And [he/she] should make it equal, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is brought back, it should be carefully, especially when both mandibles are involved, by raising them with hot water and oil, gently aligning them; do not delay in bringing it back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back equally, and the patient's mouth closes well without straining, apply moistened cloth cerates made of rose oil and wax, then gently tie it with soft strings; let the patient sleep on their back, keeping their feet between two pillows so that neither moves to the right or left, nor makes any effort to move more; instead, gently feed them light food until the pain is gone and the jaws are healed; and then they can eat normally without opening their mouth too widely.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be brought back to their proper position within an hour and do not return to their normal place, this causes fever and frequent sweating, perhaps intestinal issues, and sometimes pure vomiting of bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know it is a sign of impending death; and often those who experience it die within seven days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot be dislocated from either side within the continuity of it, and it is never dislodged outwardly, and one feels it very much.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then he presses the joint firmly into the palm of his hand, and it will return; then he applies the plaster and the bandage, and tightens it; and the part that is towards the shoulder cannot dislocate; if it does not dislocate at all, or only occasionally, then he must put it back in place as we have said; then he applies the plaster and the bandage, and tightens it, and instructs the patient to rest until he is healed; and in this way the dislocation of the shoulder is brought back, when it is out of its proper position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	**On Shoulder Dislocation**
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one is when it dislocates at the joint below the acromion; the second is at the part of the scapula itself; and sometimes it dislocates above, which is rare, and it does not dislocate behind the shoulder or inside the nerf; and often it dislocates towards the acromion, especially in those with little muscle, for them it happens easily; but in those with enough muscle, it barely moves, and returns barely.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to no one that there is a bruise or fracture, and a hot abscess forms in the shoulder, and they think it is dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary for you to test it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And the dislocation is known when it deviates towards the joint, and it distinguishes between the injured shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a clear difference; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and by touching the shoulder blade, the top of the shoulder feels like one entity; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his body, or move in any way; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, as long as it is not completely hidden, because you find it clearly visible when touched; and this kind of dislocation is not just for resetting, when it is new, or if the entrapped part is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister holds the patient's hand gently above, then places his palms beneath the joint, and pulls the joint forcefully upward towards the bone; and the minister holds the hand again, extends it upward, and puts it beneath; this will bring relief.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If it does not come as we have said above, in a few days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and administer a gentle, softening, and soothing application, such as a decoction of althae and fenugreek and melilote in water, and apply it. Then help the patient to lie down on their back, and place a piece of equal thickness of wool beneath the joint, not too soft nor too hard, then place the heel of the foot upon this pad, and with gentle strength pull the head of the shoulder upwards, while also pulling the hand of the patient; and another minister should hold the head of the shoulder to prevent it from moving. This will correct the position of the shoulder immediately, and if you see that it is returned to its place, follow this method: and ensure there is a man present who is taller than the patient; and he should stand straight against the side of the patient, pull the shoulder away from the joint of the patient's back, and pull the joint upwards, so that the patient's arm hangs down; and another minister pulls the hand of the patient downwards towards their stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, and any heavy thing is laid upon him, then the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also corrected in another way: take a long stick and insert it into the ground so that the end is as bright as a pistal, but neither too thick nor too thin; then place it under the patient, ensuring there are soft rags above, and the patient's arm is straight and firm. Then extend the patient's hand downwards from the other side, and the joint will return to its place; and if it does not want to come back for all the reasons we have mentioned, do this treatment: take a stick that is two arms long and four fingers wide, which has a pointed end to enter perfectly under the shoulder according to this shape.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then place a heavy cloth over the head, so that it does not hurt the patient, and then lay the patient flat; extend one arm above the head and fasten the aid to the head, and the arm at the elbow of the hand, then put the arm on the edge of a broad shovel, and let the hands hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will now be realigned.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is dislocated in any way, it is necessary to place under the joint a piece of equal woolen thread, then apply a plaster with a mixture of powder from the mill, with incense and egg yolk, over the entire shoulder and around it, then pull the joint gently, and tie the string to the plaster, and press the hand against the collarbone, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move the dislocated part little by little, as long as the limb is comfortable, because it will heal faster; and then move it again after a few days or seven, and it will be cured. If it remains stiff and is not softened, it will heal.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is firmly out of place due to moisture or any other reason, it is necessary that you apply cautery at three points, as described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after seven days the dislocation still does not hold, and he cannot raise his arm above his head, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is either cut, stretched, or damaged; and know that the joint will never be firmly in its place again.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the worst, and the limbs, or behind, if it is done by a blow, and stretching of the hands, and is held in another place; and treat as long as it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing comes cracking in the member, and late movements, if the patient uses it often, until the cracking is relieved, and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation cost
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	You know that the jointure cost is relieved by a few things, and it returns; if it is despoiled from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not completely healed, because we see it well and feel it well; and it heals according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased part with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is injured, and cannot bend the arm, or touch the shoulder to anything.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in such a way that the apothema does not come again, because if the apothema comes back, it will be difficult to bring it back; and by chance it cannot be brought back entirely from the rear part; it is worse than other dislocations, causes greater pain, and by chance may lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is possible when it can be brought back, you extend his hand with both of yours; and his arms are spread out, and the hands moved gently according to the cost around, inside and outside, and bring the joint to his thighs together, or at the base of his palm, until he returns to his place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and presses from the base of the palm the joint that is out of place.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, apply a strong extension; and let the minister extend his arm, and tie him with a double long and wide strip, so that he does not move at the extension. Then turn each part of the arm, after you have wrapped the bandage around the joint. When you see the joint in place, add a little oil to soften the joint, then bring it back into shape, until it returns to its place. And when it is in place, apply dry plaster with egg white, form it, and bend the arm towards the patient's chest, leaving it for several days, then loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not properly secured, repeat the splint and the bandage, and leave it for several days, until it is firmly placed; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if the patient feels pain after the joint is reset, and it becomes stiff, bathe and gently rub it, applying pressure until it is relieved; or place a grease-soaked woolen pad on the joint, leave it for a day and night, then remove it and give the patient a bath; and when they are washed, gently rub the joint, then apply the pad again, and repeat this process two or three times until it is healed; and if you notice, use fine moist warm wax with butter and strain it over the joint; it will return to its original state.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand joint is misaligned and its return to position is light, more so than other joints. Nonetheless, it needs to be carefully realigned, immediately upon its dislocation, so that the swelling or hot abscess does not set in.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the realigning is such that you place the afflicted hand on a table, extend the patient's fingers, and observe them until they are even, so that the palm rests upon the joint's surface, holding it in position until it returns to its correct place. However, you must check if it is back in its proper location; then, place the patient's hand with the back side down on a table for extension and realigning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, let the patient lay his back on his hand on a table, and look closely at the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is good; otherwise, if the strain of soothing compresses on abscesses does not cease, and it remains thus without repeating.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place for any number of days, then the joint remains twisted; and it does not harm the patient that the hand is bent, and nothing can be extracted: then know that the nerve or artery is cut; unless there is no other mechanism by which to extract it safely, and perhaps there is nothing else worth trying.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, if you put on the plaster as we have said, then pull it and leave it for a day, then loosen it and leave it such.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no fracture, then apply hot water moisture, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	on the dislocation of the two joints of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Under no circumstances should the joints of the hand be dislocated at both ends, either on the back of the palm or on the sole; then, pull the joint and release it until it returns, then hold the top of the joint and bend it towards the side where it is separated; leave it for a day, and then repeat this process; do not tie it, as we have said, but loosen it during the day and move it, and then relink it; continue to do this until it is tight, and also do so if it is dislocated on the sole of the hand, following the same method until it heals.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or the neck is dislocated, and there is no cure, the patient often dies quickly.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the patient's movements become involuntary, they cannot control them, and often, a limb becomes weakened, such as both legs or one arm, or sometimes even both arms; and occasionally, the spine becomes bent to one side—this is called "scoliosis". The treatment for this is to reward and correct the scoliosis if it originated in childhood; if there is no cure or remedy for it at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from a fall or from impacts or similar things, the old methods of treatment speak of in great words, but they offer little benefit to all; however, I have abbreviated them according to my understanding and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the stiffness that comes to the penis in front, no one has a remedy; and also that which comes straight to the second side, and it is only the one who properly comes to the back, as I say, that can be cured. And let the patient lie on his face equally in the first position, and stretch him tightly from below so he does not bleed. Then take a stick and make an impression in the ground with your head, and another at the other side, and tie a string around the parts of the patient's body that are afflicted, one to the head and the others to the feet, among the two sticks; and they should be well secured, the stick as we have said, and let the midwife place her palms on the forming spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a table three feet long, remove the wall from behind it, place the patient on their side, and turn the head of the table away from the wall; then place the middle of the table over the spine, and put both legs of the table on the other side of the table, pressing firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see it moving, do it in a circular motion that comes back to your hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And take two sharp sticks, one of great length, and insert them through the side of the patient's arm, leaving two others outside; between each stick, dig a space as long as your palm, and make in each stick a hole for the rotation or turn, so that they are firmly stuck in the ground, not moving; and between these two turning sticks, place one smaller stick to return the turns, also of the length of a palm, so that each minister returns his stick to its whole length, and the master makes the spine equal as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a drying plaster with plenty of heat, and then the compresses, and then the stick of a tablet three fingers long, which will own the joint of the stiffness and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the patient's mild relief, as long as it is healed; and if any thing comes about at the end of health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the stick that we have mentioned above; and never once should anything be administered, and never does the appearance appear in the back spine, and one must think it is dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, for which one must not have any presumption: perhaps death would come.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the spine
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You know that the joints of the spine and the joints of the shoulder only cause dislocations, unlike other joints; and the joint of the spine is misaligned according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside, less misaligned in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within itself is such that when you join the affected leg with the healthy one, it becomes longer, and opens up the sick knee more widely than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their kneecap; and it is the swelling around the abscess on top that causes this, because the bone in the thigh comes over here.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who is approaching death, it is that this event is contrary to what has been said before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of someone who is about to die, it is that their leg is weak according to what is expected; however, do not bend the knee without pain, and if they want to walk, they cannot do so before, and they hold in their urine, and the ankle swells, and when they look, they pass over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of someone who is dying from behind, it is that they cannot spread or bend their knee, and one leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the thigh is in a position opposite to the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	They reset this appearance of dislocation if it is such that you reward it since the dislocation is ancient and lingers according to its nature, if there is no cure; and one must not let him have any presumptions.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for the one whose dislocation is fresh, and it's of the four types of dislocation, you must act swiftly: return the joint to its original position inside and outside, and adjust it to the right and left; then it may heal on its own and no other treatment is required.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it doesn't return in this manner, you must then use a strong minister, extending the leg strongly to two hands or binding it at the knee; and other ministers extend their hands from above in such a way that they press the patient's hands down onto their knees, then tighten a soft band around the calf; and others hold the head with a rope; and all pull together simultaneously, lifting the patient off the ground once, and holding them suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all three cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If it is not, it is necessary to take care of its appearance. When the dislocation is in the wrong place, it is advisable for you to place the patient on their healthy side, then tie the limb at the root of the foot, and the joint that is above the angle; then stretch the tie upwards towards the angle and towards the stronger part. Then have other assistants grasp the patient's arms, embrace the large joint of the afflicted foot, and extend it to a different form; it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in the manner we have said, then you should tie both feet of the patient together with a strong, soft ligature on both heels and both knees; then extend the sick leg two hands more than the other; then hang it over a post, and let it hang two arms' length above the ground; then command the assistant to embrace the top of the thigh, and have another assistant hanging with the patient, who embraces the thigh, for the joint will now come back healthily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when dislocation occurs away from the body, if the patient lies as we have said in the case of gibbosity, then tighten the ligature properly on the sick leg and also on the other side; then place two hot coals, one at the head and one at the foot; then insert a hot coal between the thighs of the patient, in the middle; and surround him with moist towels so that he does not feel cold, then extend each assistant towards him, and have them equalize the dislocation with their hands.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not return, place it on a table and press it as we have said in the previous section, and lay the patient on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg forcibly, as I have said; and ease their pain by placing them on the healthy side, then press with the other hand, and stretch it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not necessary to stretch the affected leg down, nor to lift it up towards the sky, but rather, it should remain as the hip was dislocated backwards, as we have said earlier, gently on both hips; and place it on its face, and extend the joint as we have previously said, and all should press on the joint against the table; and at this point, when the patient extends their legs, they will be even. Then tighten the bandages and apply a poultice, and wrap a strap around it so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then untie it and apply a poultice again; and gently make them walk, as long as the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The limb is dislocated in three ways: internally, externally, and backward; but not forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and if it does not yield to the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend their leg if they can, and place their face on your hands, and rest their foot on yours. Then take hold of their kneecap in both hands, and pull between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the kneecap; and another assistant extends their foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it yields slightly at the knee. And apply a poultice, and straighten the leg at the knee, and bind it together firmly for three or four days, then release it; and do not let the patient move about, until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not at all extended, apply a strong stretch as we have said in the treatment of the spine, as long as it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	On the dislocation of the talus bone.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The talus bone is neither completely dislocated nor fully restored, either internally or externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and there is tension before the dislocated part; the reduction is light, and one should gently extend their hand to it when it is slightly dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is slightly dislocated, you should make the patient lie straight, and hold the leg away from the body with the hands above the ankle; then take the foot in your right hand, and twice in your left, then stretch it upwards, and bring the foot back nicely to its place; and do this twice as we have said, pulling and stretching the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, you must begin again with the treatment, for it will return; and if it cannot be brought back like that, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and insert a firm stick between his thighs, and bind him tightly so he does not injure himself; then have the assistants hold the healthy leg from below, and others stretch the dislocated leg to its place at the ankle; then each assistant should equally position the mirrors at the dislocation in the hands, and another assistant straighten the healthy leg at the knee, and the dislocation will return firmly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when the bone has set, apply a plaster and bind it tightly, pressing the leg to the foot and securing the straps behind the ankle so that the bonds are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the straps have relaxed, untie them on the third or fourth day, and the patient must walk after four days; and if he improves before this time, it is not fortunate that he will no longer heal.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms, it is necessary to soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, while it is fresh.
des dois	Of two things
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the eyes are dislocated, if they need to be nicely extended without effort, it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any other part of the body, besides the neck or foot, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back or on a table completely straight, and place your foot on what opens up from these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it returns; and when it is even, and there is nothing open, put a wooden block under the sole of the foot, then pull firmly, and leave it for three days, then loosen it; and let it rest, until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	From wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and we want to restore it, often the patient dies if they are not treated properly: so do not be presumptuous in their care, unless you are skilled in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and do not be hasty or tardy. Begin by applying hot apathy to the wound, and leave the patient in God's hands if there is no hope of recovery; but if there is hope, then immediately realign the limb as the dislocation heals; and while the limb is healing, apply warm apathy to the wound and care for it as appropriate from dehydration. If there is fracture and small broken bones with dislocation, cure them as we have said in simple illnesses; and be careful not to enter a path of fear, as I have said, for this will guide you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your arms and body.
